That's the full Phase 1–4 stack running in a real browser — IR → layout passes → render → pointer → transaction → commit → IR mutation → re-derivation. If any link in the chain broke, the bar wouldn't visibly persist its new position.
- **Port 8702 chosen to not collide with the parity reference's 8701.** Both servers can run concurrently for side-by-side comparison once a VRT pass lands.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.2)

- New workspace package `@chronixjs/example-gantt-vue3` at `examples/gantt-vue3/` (the first entry under the existing `examples/*` pnpm glob). `private: true`; never published.
- Standard scaffold: `package.json` (vite + plugin-vue + vue-tsc + vitest, workspace deps on `@chronixjs/gantt` + `@chronixjs/gantt-vue3`), `tsconfig.json` (extends base + `noEmit + jsx: preserve`), `vite.config.ts` (plugin-vue, port 8702, strictPort), `eslint.config.js` (chronix vue preset), `shims-vue.d.ts`.
- `src/sample-data.ts`: 8 bars across 4 workshop rows (`workshop-a..d`) on the day axis. All bars anchored at local midnight today, hours 1..22. No progress overlay (Phase 4.3+).
- `src/App.vue`: two-column grid (chart left, event panel right). `editable + selectable` toggles + a `reset` button. Wires `<ChronixGantt @bar-drop="…">` to a `pushEvent` ring buffer (last 20). `onBarDrop / onBarResize` also write the new range back into `bars.value` — the bar visibly persists its new position, proving the round-trip.
- `src/styles.css`: chronix-native `cx-demo-*` + `cx-gantt-bar` selectors only. Color-codes events by kind: green for `bar-drop`, amber for `bar-resize`, indigo for `select`. No `.gantt-*` literals; banned-names scan stays clean.
- `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/example-gantt-vue3 dev` → `http://localhost:8702/`.

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.2)

- `@chronixjs/example-gantt-vue3` (vs `@chronixjs/demo-gantt-vue3`): "example" matches the directory name (`examples/`) and the audience (someone reading the library docs wants to find an _example_, not a _demo_).
- `cx-demo-*` CSS prefix for the demo wrapper (vs reusing `cx-gantt-*`): the demo wrapper isn't part of the gantt component's surface; namespacing it `cx-demo-` keeps the component's own classes uncontaminated and makes it obvious which selectors are example-only.
- Port 8702 picked sequentially after the parity-reference's 8701. Future chronix examples land at 8703, 8704, etc.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.2)

- **No view-toggle.** The demo is day-view only. Multi-view + a header toolbar lands when an axis-tick render exists to give the user something to look at across views.
- **No axis ticks rendered.** `<ChronixGantt>` only paints bars right now. Without ticks the user has no time reference — they see bars but don't know what hour each bar covers. Phase 4.3 candidate.
- **No scroll wrapper.** The SVG is sized to `contentSize.width / height` directly; if the bar range exceeds viewport the SVG just grows. Real chronix apps need a scrollable container with the SVG inside; that requires the `<ChronixGantt>` pointer handlers to add the wrapper's `scrollLeft / scrollTop` to the content coords (parked in Phase 4.1's "Open / parked").
- **No example for `useGanttPointer` standalone.** The composable path (without `<ChronixGantt>`) is theoretically supported but has no demo. Adding one would prove the composable's call-site ergonomics independently of the SFC.
- **No VRT goldens for the chronix demo yet.** The `tooling/golden-runner` workspace already supports `CHRONIX_DEMO_URL` env override (read-only check: not yet wired; need to confirm). When ready, capture chronix-side goldens at 8702 and eventually diff against the parity-reference goldens.

## Phase 4.2 — DONE

- `examples/gantt-vue3/` workspace package + vite app + 94-file banned-name scan clean.
- 201/201 vitest cumulative (no new vitest in this commit — the example is verified by browser smoke test + build).
- Real-browser confidence: Phase 1 IR → Phase 2 layout → Phase 3 hit-test + capture → Phase 4 adapter → Phase 4.1 pointer → Phase 4.2 example. The whole stack runs in a real Vue3 + vite app.

## Phase 4.3 — axis-tick header band in `<ChronixGantt>`

### Reference reading (Phase 4.3)

- None new. Phase 2's `AxisRangePlanner` already emits `PlannedAxis.ticks: readonly AxisTick[]` with `{ x, time, label }`; the adapter just consumes it. The k-ui side's tick rendering lives in `packages/gantt/src/timeline/TimelineHeader.tsx` and is preact-specific — chronix doesn't port the render layer, only the planner output shape.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 4.3)

- **Bar group transform is the right shift mechanism — not per-rect y offsets.** The bars' layout y comes from `BarPlacementPass` and is computed against `SwimlaneStrip.y` starting at 0. Adding the axis band by mutating every rect's y would force every test that asserts `rect.y` to learn about `headerHeight`. Instead wrap the bar group in a `<g transform="translate(0, headerHeight)">`: rect attributes stay identical to the layout output, and the visual offset is one parent-`<g>` away. Existing rect-attribute tests survive without changes; only the new "bar group transform" test references the offset directly.
- **Pointer math must subtract `headerHeight` symmetrically.** The hit-tester operates in bar-group content space, where strip y=0 means the top of the first row. If `getBoundingClientRect` returns `{top: T}` and the cursor is at `clientY = C`, contentY must be `C - T - headerHeight` to keep `bar.y` semantics intact. Failing to subtract makes a click on row 0 (content-y near 0) look like a click on row 0 plus `headerHeight` pixels — usually still inside the strip, but bar-edge resize zones (8 px) flip from "start" to "end" silently.
- **Axis-row click filtering at the adapter, not the hit-tester.** Hit-tester input `contentY < 0` would never match a strip (strips have y ≥ 0), so technically the hit-tester already filters axis clicks. But making the contract explicit — early-return when `pos.y < 0` in `onPointerdown` — documents intent and avoids relying on a "happens to return null" behavior of the hit-test layer. Filtering happens at `begin` only; `advance` / `commit` accept negative y because an in-flight drag should survive a brief cursor visit to the axis band without aborting.
- **`Intl.DateTimeFormat('zh-CN', { hour: 'numeric', hour12: false })` emits exactly `'0时' … '23时'` in Node 22 + happy-dom + V8.** Verified empirically (`node -e "..."`). Not `'00时'`. Not `'00:00'`. This is the literal we test against; if a future Node / ICU bumps the format, the tick-label vitest is the canary.
- **SVG height = `contentSize.height + headerHeight`.** Width is unchanged because the axis tick spacing is identical to bar layout x — they share `slotWidth`. The natural extension when headerRows lands is to add per-row heights to `headerHeight` (sum over `axis.headerRows.length`), not to introduce a new prop per row.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.3)

- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts` extended: new `headerHeight: number` prop (default 24, 0 hides the band). Render function now emits two top-level `<g>` children — `cx-gantt-axis` (one `<line class="cx-gantt-tick-line">` + `<text class="cx-gantt-tick-label">` per tick, plus a `cx-gantt-axis-divider` baseline) and `cx-gantt-bars` (`transform="translate(0, headerHeight)"`, contains all bar rects). SVG height grows by `headerHeight`. Pointer math subtracts `headerHeight` from `clientY` and early-returns on axis-row clicks.
- 6 new SFC vitest in `chronix-gantt.test.ts` under a third describe block "ChronixGantt axis ticks":
  - 24 `.cx-gantt-tick-label` text content `'0时' … '23时'` (day-view zh-CN).
  - 24 `.cx-gantt-tick-line` x positions strictly monotonically increasing in `[0, axis.totalWidth)`, `x1 === x2`.
  - default `headerHeight=24`, SVG height = 77 (two 38-row + 1 rowSpacing) + 24 = 101.
  - custom `headerHeight=40` with one bar on r1: BarStackHeightPass pads r1 to 42 (= 8 + 30 + 4), so SVG height = 42 + 1 + 38 + 40 = 121; `.cx-gantt-bars` transform attr = `"translate(0, 40)"`; rect's own `y` stays 8 (unchanged from layout output).
  - `headerHeight=0`: no axis-divider line, SVG height = 77, but tick lines + labels still render (we don't gate them on the band height — only the bottom divider gates).
- 1 new SFC interaction vitest covering axis-row click filter: with `editable + selectable` both true, `pointerdown` at `clientY=10` (< headerHeight 24) emits no `bar-drop / bar-resize / select`.
- 4 existing interaction vitest updated: `clientY: 20` → `clientY: 20 + 24` (a `DEFAULT_HEADER_HEIGHT` constant at module scope keeps the offset documented in one place).

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.3)

- `headerHeight` (vs `axisHeight` / `tickHeight` / `headerBandHeight`): "header" matches the parity reference's vocabulary (`headerFormats`, `headerToolbar`) and frames the band as the row of meta above the bar area, not as a property of the ticks themselves. The future month / season / halfYear / year views will stack two header rows here, and `headerHeight` reads naturally as a top-level sum.
- `cx-gantt-axis` (group) / `cx-gantt-tick-line` / `cx-gantt-tick-label` / `cx-gantt-axis-divider` / `cx-gantt-bars` (group): all consistent with the existing `cx-gantt-bar` convention. The bottom divider gets its own selector so styling can shift (light vs dark theme would want different stroke contrast for it).
- `axis-divider` placed inside the `cx-gantt-axis` group (vs as a sibling baseline): the divider is conceptually part of the axis (it's the band's bottom edge), not the bar layer. Keeping it in the axis group lets a future "hide axis" knob just toggle one parent.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.3)

- **headerRows still unrendered.** Month / season / halfYear / year views carry multi-row `PlannedAxis.headerRows` (e.g. month band over day ticks). The current implementation only renders the tick row. When the demo's view-toggle (Phase 4.6 candidate) lands, this branch needs a second `<g>` above the tick row, with `headerHeight` becoming the sum of `headerRowHeights` + tick-row height, or split into `tickRowHeight` and `headerRowHeights`. Until then `<ChronixGantt>` renders correctly only for day + week (which have 1 header row that's collapsed into the tick row visually).
- **No CSS styling for axis elements yet.** Stroke/fill colors are inline attributes (`stroke="#d1d5db"`, `fill="#6b7280"`) so the example app works without dedicated CSS. The example's `cx-demo-*` selectors don't theme the tick line/label either; a future styling pass should move the inline colors to CSS so consumers can override them.
- **No clamp on `headerHeight` lower bound.** Negative values would draw the divider above the axis and translate bars upward into negative SVG space. Not currently validated; a `prop` validator could enforce `headerHeight >= 0` if a misuse surfaces. Default 24 + the type being `Number` is enough for the demo.
- **Live-browser verify deferred for this iteration.** Port 8702 was already held by a leftover `node_modules/.bin/vite` from the k-ui vue3 example (PID 38220, started earlier today, unrelated to this session's work). Killing an unrelated dev server without asking would violate the harness's "executing actions with care" guideline; the 36-test vitest suite confirms tick render + pointer-coord shift end-to-end, and the user can manually open `http://localhost:8702/` after freeing the port to confirm visually.

## Phase 4.3 — DONE

- `<ChronixGantt headerHeight>` renders 24 day-view ticks `'0时' … '23时'` above the bar area; pointer math + axis-row filter keeps existing drag / resize / select interactions untouched (after `clientY` offset in the 4 existing interaction tests).
- 36/36 vue3 adapter vitest (was 30; Phase 4.3 added 6 — 1 axis-row interaction filter + 5 axis-tick render).
- 207/207 vitest cumulative (Phase 2: 95, Phase 3: 76, Phase 4 entry: 14, Phase 4.1: 16, Phase 4.3: 6). ci-check fully green (format / lint / typecheck / 207 vitest / build / banned-names 104 files).

## Phase 4.6 — headerRows render + example view-toggle

### Reference reading (Phase 4.6)

- None new. Phase 2's `AxisRangePlanner` already emits `PlannedAxis.headerRows: readonly AxisHeaderRow[]` for all six views (one row each in v0). The adapter consumes that shape; no upstream-reference reading was needed for this iteration.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 4.6)

- **One `<rect>` + one `<text>` per header cell is enough.** Cell rendering is the simplest possible: a background-filled rect with a 1-px stroke as the outline, plus a centered `<text>` for `cell.label`. Adjacent cells share an edge; each rect's stroke draws over the shared boundary, giving a visually continuous separator without a separate `<line>` element. The doubled-stroke effect is invisible at 1px.
- **Default `headerRowHeight = 20`, opt-out via `0`.** Setting a non-zero default means the demo (and any naive consumer) gets the outer band for free in the day view — without it the band looks "incomplete." Tests that want the bare bar area pass `headerRowHeight: 0` explicitly; the headerRows render is then suppressed and the `<g class="cx-gantt-axis">` group sits flush at SVG `y=0`. The "0 hides" contract mirrors `headerHeight: 0`'s existing behavior.
- **`<g class="cx-gantt-axis">` gets its own transform now.** Previously it sat at SVG `y=0` because the tick row was the top band. With headerRows above it, the axis group is translated to `(0, headerRowsHeight)` so its child elements keep their `y ∈ [0, headerHeight]` coords. The bar group's transform sums both: `(0, headerRowsHeight + headerHeight)`. Pointer math subtracts the same sum, exposed as a `computed` so it stays in lockstep with `axis.headerRows.length × headerRowHeight + headerHeight`.
- **The reactive `axisInput` getter is what drives view-switching.** The `useGanttLayout` composable already accepted `MaybeRefOrGetter<AxisRangePlanInput>` on its input. Switching from a literal axisInput to a `computed(() => ({ ...viewId-driven... }))` re-derives the entire pipeline — `axis` → `strips` (BarStackHeightPass + swimlane) → `placedBars` — every time the user clicks a view button. No special "rebuild" or "invalidate" call is needed.
- **`overflow: auto` on the SVG wrapper is sufficient for horizontal scroll.** Week/month/season/halfYear/year views produce axes wider than the demo's chart pane (week: 52 × 168 = 8736 px; year: 65 × ~365 = ~23 700 px). Wrapping the SVG in a `overflow: auto` frame lets the browser handle the scroll bar; pointer math already uses `getBoundingClientRect().left`, which goes negative when the SVG scrolls left of the viewport, so `clientX - rect.left` still resolves to the correct content-x. No adapter change needed for horizontal scroll to "just work."
- **`Intl.DateTimeFormat('zh-CN', { weekday: 'short' })` emits `"周X"`, not `"X"`.** Chronix's planner uses `weekday: 'short'`, so month/season/halfYear/year tick labels look like `"1日周五"` — the reference DOM renders `"15日三"` (narrow weekday). Hidden divergence: the golden-runner parity tests don't compare tick labels for non-day views (only slot widths), so this was not caught. The Phase 4.6 SFC vitest covers what chronix actually produces and parks the divergence for a later parity-aligned planner change.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.6)

- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: added `headerRowHeight: { type: Number, default: 20 }` prop. The render function now emits three top-level `<g>` children in order:
  - `cx-gantt-header-rows` — one `<rect class="cx-gantt-header-cell">` + one `<text class="cx-gantt-header-cell-label">` per cell, stacked into rows at `y = rowIdx × headerRowHeight`.
  - `cx-gantt-axis` — translated to `(0, headerRowsHeight)`. Body unchanged from Phase 4.3.
  - `cx-gantt-bars` — translated to `(0, headerRowsHeight + headerHeight)`.
  - SVG total height grows by `axis.headerRows.length × headerRowHeight + headerHeight`. Pointer `toContentXY` subtracts the same amount, exposed as `computed(() => …)` so it stays reactive to view changes.
- `examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue`: added a 6-button view-toggle in the header (`日 / 周 / 月 / 季 / 半年 / 年`). `axisInput` flipped from a literal to a `computed<AxisRangePlanInput>(() => ({ viewId: viewId.value, anchorDate: todayLocalMidnight(), … }))`. Clicking a button sets `viewId.value` and the chart re-renders end-to-end.
- `examples/gantt-vue3/src/sample-data.ts`: `todayLocalMidnight` is now exported (was module-local). Removed `defaultAxisInput` since the App owns the axis-input shape now.
- `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css`: `.cx-demo-svg-frame` changed `overflow: hidden` → `overflow: auto` (plus `max-height: 70vh` for vertical scroll headroom on multi-row demos). Added `.cx-demo-view-toggle*` selectors for the toolbar group + active-button state.
- 7 new SFC vitest in `chronix-gantt.test.ts`:
  - day-view: 1 header cell spanning `[0, totalWidth]` with non-empty label.
  - week-view: 7 uniform header cells × 168 tick lines.
  - month-view: 1 header cell, 28–31 tick labels matching `/^1日周?[一二三四五六日]$/u`.
  - year-view: 12 header cells.
  - `headerRowHeight: 0` hides cells but keeps tick row.
  - `<g class="cx-gantt-axis">` transform = `translate(0, headerRowsHeight)`.
  - "between header-rows and tick row" pointer click is still blocked (axis-row filter).
- Existing tests updated:
  - `DEFAULT_HEADER_HEIGHT` (24) renamed to `DEFAULT_HEADER_BAND_HEIGHT` (44 = 1×20 + 24). All 4 interaction tests pick up the new offset.
  - "SVG height" assertion bumped from `77 + 24` to `77 + 44`.
  - "custom headerHeight" test now passes both `headerHeight: 40` and `headerRowHeight: 30` and asserts the new sum (`70`) in the bar group's transform.
  - "headerHeight=0" test extended with `headerRowHeight: 0` to keep the "no band" semantics.

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.6)

- `headerRowHeight` (vs `outerHeaderHeight` / `bandRowHeight` / `cellHeight`): names the per-row dimension, consistent with `axis.headerRows`. Future multi-row views (e.g. year-band over month-band over day ticks) extend trivially — same prop applies to every row in the stack.
- `cx-gantt-header-rows` for the parent group + `cx-gantt-header-cell` / `cx-gantt-header-cell-label` for the leaves: mirrors the `cx-gantt-axis` / `cx-gantt-tick-line` / `cx-gantt-tick-label` cluster from Phase 4.3. The plural group name (`-rows`) hints that multiple rows can land in it.
- `VIEW_TOGGLE` (module-scope constant array in the example, vs a Vue `ref`): the available views don't change at runtime — they're a config, not state. Module-scope keeps the template's `v-for` cheap and signals intent.
- `cx-demo-view-toggle-button.active` (compound class) for the active-view state: chronix BEM prefers `cx-block--mod`, but the active-button rule is part of the example layer (`cx-demo-*`), not the gantt component surface, so the demo-internal compound is fine. Stylelint passes because the strict pattern only enforces top-level block names.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.6)

- **`weekday: 'short'` vs `'narrow'`.** chronix month/season/halfYear/year tick labels look like `"1日周五"`; reference DOM is `"15日三"`. Aligning chronix to `'narrow'` is a one-line change in `axis-range-planner.ts` and should land alongside a `tooling/golden-runner` parity assertion for month-view tick-label set equality (currently only day-view checks labels).
- **Multi-row header bands.** All chronix planner outputs are 1-row today; the `headerRows: readonly AxisHeaderRow[]` shape is multi-row-ready. Future parity work for month-banded-over-day-ticks (or year-banded-over-month-banded-over-day-ticks) will return `headerRows.length === 2 || 3`. Render code already iterates the array; no changes there. The planner is the gap.
- **Scroll plumbing inside `<ChronixGantt>`.** The example wraps the SVG in `overflow: auto`; pointer math survives that because `getBoundingClientRect` reports `left` relative to the viewport, including the scroll offset. But sticky-on-scroll header rows (so the day/month name stays visible while the bar area scrolls vertically) require `position: sticky` on a separate DOM band — not achievable inside a single SVG. A future split-pane layout (SVG header / SVG body) is the path.
- **No vertical scroll synchronization yet.** With `overflow: auto + max-height: 70vh`, the header row scrolls vertically with the SVG. That's only correct because the SVG is one element — once a split header/body lands, vertical scroll has to be plumbed.
- **Live-browser verify still deferred.** Port 8702 is still held by the leftover k-ui vite (PID 38220). The 43-test vitest suite covers headerRows render across views + the existing pointer / interaction behavior; visual verification will happen when the user frees the port.

## Phase 4.6 — DONE

- `<ChronixGantt headerRowHeight>` renders one cell per `axis.headerRows[].cells[]` entry; example app has a working 6-view toggle and an `overflow: auto` scroll wrapper for the wider views.
- 43/43 vue3 adapter vitest (was 36; Phase 4.6 added 7 — 1 axis-row mid-band filter + 6 headerRows render).
- 214/214 vitest cumulative (Phase 2: 95, Phase 3: 76, Phase 4 entry: 14, Phase 4.1: 16, Phase 4.3: 6, Phase 4.6: 7). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 4.7 — `weekday: short → narrow` parity alignment

### Reference reading (Phase 4.7)

- No new file reads. The divergence + the target format (`"DD日<wd>"` with narrow weekday) were already captured in Phase 4.6's open / parked. The change closes the gap; the reference DOM is the oracle.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 4.7)

- **`Intl.DateTimeFormat('zh-CN', { day: 'numeric', weekday: 'narrow' })` emits `"<DD>日<wd>"`** where `<wd>` ∈ `{一, 二, 三, 四, 五, 六, 日}`. Verified empirically on Node 22 + V8: 7 weekdays produce 7 distinct narrow Han chars (`Sun → 日`, `Mon → 一`, …, `Sat → 六`). Matches the reference DOM exactly.
- **The chronix workspace's parity tests are decoupled from `pnpm test`.** `tooling/golden-runner/package.json` exposes `capture` and `verify` only — no `test` script — so `pnpm test` (and therefore `pnpm ci-check`) skips them. Running parity assertions is a manual step: terminal 1 `pnpm dev` against the k-ui demo on port 8701; terminal 2 `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/golden-runner verify -g "<test name>"`. This is deliberate: parity tests need an external dev server, so CI can't run them unattended.
- **Three call sites of `weekday: 'short'`, two changed.** `planMonthView` (line 153) and `planMonthBandedAxis` (line 206) emit the day-resolution ticks used by month / season / halfYear / year — those are the tick labels the reference renders as `"15日三"`. The third call site (`planWeekView`, line 262) emits day-cell **header-row** labels for the week view (e.g. `"5月13日 周三"`) — a separate concern; the reference's format for week-view outer cells hasn't been parity-checked yet, and conservatively leaving it on `'short'` avoids changing a string we haven't verified.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.7)

- `packages/gantt/src/layout/axis-range-planner.ts`: `weekday: 'short'` → `weekday: 'narrow'` in `planMonthView` (line 153) and `planMonthBandedAxis` (line 206). Comment added at the first site explaining why narrow matches the reference DOM, with a back-pointer to this journal section. Left `planWeekView` untouched.
- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.test.ts`: Phase 4.6's tolerant regex `/^1日周?[一二三四五六日]$/u` tightened to `/^1日[一二三四五六日]$/u`. Now asserts the exact reference format.
- `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts`: new `'month-view tick labels (set equality)'` parity assertion. Same shape as the day-view one — Set-equality between chronix's `axis.ticks.map((t) => t.label)` and the reference's leaf-text labels matching `/^\d+日[一二三四五六日]$/u`. **Empirically green against k-ui demo on port 8701**: both produce the same 31 labels `'1日五' … '31日日'` for May 2026.

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.7)

- No new identifiers — the change is a single-token format flip plus one new test.
- Parity test name uses `'month-view tick labels (set equality)'`, mirroring the day-view name verbatim. Future month-banded views (`season-view`, `halfYear-view`, `year-view`) will add similar tests by name pattern.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.7)

- **Week-view day-cell header format hasn't been parity-checked yet.** chronix emits `weekday: 'short'` → `"周X"` here; the reference's format is unknown. Closing it requires a `week-view header-cell labels (set equality)` parity assertion, then adjusting if the reference uses narrow. Park until a consumer cares.
- **The third Intl-format trio — `monthFmt`'s `month: 'long'`** — emits `"2026年5月"` for month / season / halfYear / year header cells. Reference rendering hasn't been compared either; could be `"5月"` (short) or `"2026年5月"`. Park alongside the week-view header check.
- **No season / halfYear / year tick-label parity yet.** Same shape as month-view, just longer label sets (3 / 6 / 12 months of `"DD日<wd>"`). Adding three more parity tests is mechanical; left for the next time chronix's planner changes.
- **Parity infrastructure stays opt-in.** Running `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/golden-runner verify` requires an external dev server on 8701, so it's not in `pnpm ci-check`. The Phase 4.7 month-view assertion was verified manually against a running k-ui dev server (process 17184) but doesn't gate CI.

## Phase 4.7 — DONE

- chronix month / season / halfYear / year tick labels now emit `"DD日<wd>"` (e.g. `"1日五"`), matching the reference DOM character-for-character.
- 14 parity assertions (was 13): added month-view tick-label set equality. Empirically green vs k-ui demo at 8701.
- 214/214 vitest cumulative (no count change — one test's regex tightened; no test added or removed). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 4.8 — tick-label parity for season / halfYear / year

### Reference reading (Phase 4.8)

- No new reads. The format target (`"DD日<wd>"`) and the parity-probe pattern already landed in Phase 4.7; the new code reuses them verbatim for the three remaining day-resolution views.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 4.8)

- **Set-equality is sharper than count-equality for cross-month boundaries.** Slot-width parity (Phase 2) already asserts that chronix's `axis.slotCount` matches the rendered tick count within 1px-of-spacing tolerance — but two planners producing the same count can still disagree on which days they include (e.g. Feb 28 + Mar 1 + Mar 2 vs Feb 28 + Mar 1 + Mar 1). Set-equality catches that class of off-by-one: a single missing or duplicated `"DD日<wd>"` makes the symmetric difference non-empty. Year view (~365 ticks, only ~216 unique strings) is the most sensitive because the same `"1日X"` recurs multiple times with the same weekday — if chronix mis-iterates calendar months the dedup-by-string set still flags it.
- **`countDaysAcrossMonths` is the planner's correctness pivot.** Season / halfYear / year all funnel through `planMonthBandedAxis` which advances via `cursor.setDate(cursor.getDate() + 1)` until `cursor.getMonth() === monthIndex` flips. JavaScript's Date arithmetic handles month rollover + leap years (Feb 28/29) correctly, so the parity tests passing for `viewportWidth=1440` at `anchorDate=2026-05-13` doesn't just verify chronix today — it verifies chronix's iteration agrees with k-ui's iteration over 12 calendar months of mixed-length data.
- **`year` view's 365-to-216 unique-set ratio is the right shape.** 31 day-of-month values × 7 weekdays = 217 possible distinct `"DD日<wd>"` strings. The chronix `axis.ticks.map((t) => t.label)` set on 2026 produces 216 — one combination doesn't occur in a single 365-day window. Both sides agreeing on exactly that 216 is non-trivial.
- **Parameterizing the test loop saved 90 lines of copy/paste.** Following the existing slot-width-loop pattern (`NON_DAY_VIEWS.map(...)`) keeps the parity spec's structure consistent: standalone tests for the day view, loop-driven tests for the rest.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.8)

- `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts`: Phase 4.7's standalone `'month-view tick labels (set equality)'` test refactored into a `DAY_RESOLUTION_VIEWS` loop covering all four day-resolution views (`month`, `season`, `halfYear`, `year`). Net: +3 parity assertions, same total probe pattern.
- Empirically verified against running k-ui demo (port 8701):
  - month: chronix 31 / reference 31 unique labels — set equal.
  - season: chronix 92 / reference 92 unique labels — set equal.
  - halfYear: chronix 184 / reference 184 unique labels — set equal.
  - year: chronix 365 → 216 unique / reference 216 — set equal.

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.8)

- `DAY_RESOLUTION_VIEWS` (vs `MONTH_BANDED_VIEWS`): names the property of the ticks (day-resolution), not the planner internal (`planMonthBandedAxis`). The set is "every view whose ticks are at day granularity" — that includes `month` (which uses `planMonthView`, not `planMonthBandedAxis`), so `MONTH_BANDED_VIEWS` would be misleading.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.8)

- **Week-view header-cell parity still open.** chronix planWeekView emits `weekday: 'short'` → `"周X"` for the outer day-cell labels; reference format unverified. Same probe pattern (set-equality over leaf-text matching a week-day-cell regex) would close it. Park until week-view consumers care.
- **`monthFmt` (header-cell labels) still unverified.** All four `planMonth*` functions emit `"YYYY年M月"` via `{ year: 'numeric', month: 'long' }`. The reference's outer-band format hasn't been parity-checked — could be `"5月"` (short) or `"2026年5月"`. Sibling to the week-view header-cell open item.
- **No `weekendsVisible: false` parity yet.** All current parity tests pass `weekendsVisible: true`. When chronix gains weekend-filtering support in `planWeekView` (currently always-on, the prop is unused), parity tests should fork: `weekendsVisible: true` + the reference's `weekends-off` toggle state should both filter the same way.

## Phase 4.8 — DONE

- All four day-resolution views (month / season / halfYear / year) now have tick-label set-equality parity against the reference DOM. The week-view tick-label test is hour-based and was already covered (Phase 2).
- 17 parity assertions (was 14): +3 from the parameterized DAY_RESOLUTION_VIEWS loop. Empirically green vs k-ui demo on 8701.
- 214/214 vitest cumulative (no count change — parity tests live in golden-runner, gated behind a running reference dev server). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 3.x — progress-handle path (hit-test + composable + render)

### Reference reading (Phase 3.x)

- No new file reads. The reference mechanics were captured during Phase 0 + Phase 3 (recording-replay) and parked since: the progress triangle lives in a separate SVG overlay group (`gantt-progress-triangles` with `pointer-events: auto` above an otherwise `pointer-events: none` parent), which is why the upstream code carries a `requireInitial=false` escape valve. chronix already promoted that valve to `PointerCaptureConfig.requireInitialHit` in Phase 3.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 3.x)

- **Handle position = `bar.x + progress/100 × bar.width`.** The triangle anchors at the right edge of the filled portion. Layout-wise it can sit slightly below the bar's body (the protruding-triangle visual); chronix's hit zone is a rect centered on that point, allowed to extend past the bar's bounding box. The hit-tester treats the rect as the visible hit shape — no intersection with the bar's own bounds.
- **Handle takes precedence over body / edge zones within the same bar.** When the pointer lands inside both the handle rect AND the bar's body, the handle wins. The current implementation checks the handle rect FIRST during the top-down bar walk, before the bar-bounds containment check. This mirrors the reference's behavior where the triangle's `pointerEvents:auto` overlay catches the event before the bar body.
- **The composable owns the percent→pixel math; the hit-tester stays geometry-only.** Phase 2's pure-functional design held: `useGanttPointer` reads `BarSpec.progress.value` + `PlacedBar.x/width`, computes the handle rect, and hands a `Map<barId, rect>` to the hit-tester. The hit-tester just compares pointer coords to rects. This keeps the core layer ignorant of progress semantics — if a future consumer wants handles in a different position (e.g. centered on the bar's vertical mid-line of a non-standard layout), the adapter changes, not the core.
- **`pointer-events: none` on the rendered handle is the chronix simplification.** The reference renders the triangle in an `pointer-events: auto` overlay layer that catches events; chronix instead drives all pointer events through the root SVG and resolves them through the synthetic `progressHandleByBarId` map. This avoids the separate-overlay-layer rendering complexity. The handle rect is purely visual; its hit testing is done by the composable. The `requireInitialHit: false` config flag is still set on the transaction (preserving the IR-level escape valve documentation), but in chronix it's no longer mechanically required — the synthetic-map approach works either way.
- **Live-update during drag is NOT implemented yet.** The reference shows progress percentage updating in real-time as the user drags the triangle. chronix v1 is commit-on-pointer-up only: the handle stays visually pinned until release, then the new progress lands and the next render moves the handle. Adding live update would require the renderer to read the active transaction's `projectedProgress`. Parked.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 3.x)

- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/pointer-hit-test.ts`: added `'progress-handle'` to `PointerHitResult['kind']` discriminator; added optional `progressHandleByBarId: ReadonlyMap<barId, { x, y, width, height }>` input; hit-test logic now checks the handle rect for each bar first during the top-down walk, before the bar-bounds containment. +7 vitest in `pointer-hit-test.test.ts` covering: handle hit, precedence over bar-body, fall-through to body when outside handle, overlayId pass-through, protruding-rect support, ghost-bar handle ignored, omitted map disables the path entirely.
- `adapters/vue3/src/use-gantt-pointer.ts`: added `barProgressById`, `progressHandleSize`, `onBarProgress` to the input shape; added `BarProgressPayload` export. The composable computes `progressHandleRectsByBarId` from `placedBars` × `overlayIdByBarId` × `barProgressById`, hands it to the hit-tester, and routes `'progress-handle'` hits to `beginProgressHandle` with `config: ALLOW_MISS` (requireInitialHit=false) and the bar's `initialProgress` + `barWidth`. `advance` / `commit` got matching branches. +8 vitest in `use-gantt-pointer.test.ts`: begin / advance / commit / clamp-high / clamp-low / no-overlay / not-editable / handle-position-tracks-progress.
- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: new `progressHandleSize` prop (default 12), new `bar-progress` emit. The render function now emits two extra `<rect>` per bar that has BOTH `progress` AND `pointerOverlayId`: `cx-gantt-progress-fill` (translucent green overlay from `bar.x` to `bar.x + fillWidth`) and `cx-gantt-progress-handle` (green square centered at the handle position). Both rects carry `pointer-events: none` and `data-progress-bar-id` (NOT `data-bar-id`, to keep the existing test query unambiguous about placed-bar count) plus the handle carries `data-overlay-id`. +6 vitest in `chronix-gantt.test.ts`: render shape, skip when no progress / no overlay, end-to-end `bar-progress` emit via pointer events, handle precedence over bar-body, falls through to bar-body outside handle, 25%-progress fill width.
- `adapters/vue3/src/index.ts`: re-exported `BarProgressPayload`.
- `examples/gantt-vue3/src/sample-data.ts`: `barAt` gains an optional `progressValue` parameter; when set, the resulting BarSpec carries `progress: { value }` and `pointerOverlayId: 'progress-handle'`. Sample bars now include 3 progress-enabled entries (50% / 25% / 80%).
- `examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue`: `onBarProgress` handler updates `bars.value[idx].progress.value` (rounded to int) and pushes a `bar-progress` event into the side panel. `@bar-progress="onBarProgress"` wired on `<ChronixGantt>`.
- `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css`: new `.cx-demo-event.kind-bar-progress` CSS rule (green left border) so progress events are visually distinct in the side panel.

### Naming justifications (Phase 3.x)

- `BarProgressPayload` (vs `ProgressDragPayload` / `ProgressHandlePayload`): mirrors `BarDropPayload` / `BarResizePayload`. The event surface is keyed by the IR concept (bar progress changed), not the interaction kind (handle drag). Future consumers reading just the emit list see `bar-progress` next to `bar-drop` / `bar-resize` and the semantic is obvious.
- `progressHandleSize` (vs `progressHandleWidth` / `progressTriangleSize`): the hit zone is a square, not a triangle (chronix's simplification); a single `size` is enough. "Triangle" would be misleading for the chronix-native rendered shape (we render a square; the reference renders a triangle).
- `data-progress-bar-id` for the fill / handle rects (vs `data-bar-id`): existing tests use `[data-bar-id]` to count placed bars. Reusing the same attr on overlay rects would triple the count for every progress-bar and silently break those tests. A distinct attribute keeps the test selectors composable.
- `cx-gantt-progress-fill` / `cx-gantt-progress-handle`: follow the established `cx-gantt-*` selector cluster (`cx-gantt-bar`, `cx-gantt-tick-line`, `cx-gantt-header-cell`, etc.). The `-fill` / `-handle` suffix names the visual role.

### Open / parked (Phase 3.x)

- **Live-update during drag is still parked.** The handle and fill rects don't update mid-drag; only on commit. To live-update, the SFC would need to subscribe to `pointer.activeTransaction.value` and, when it's a `progress-handle` kind, draw the handle / fill at `projectedProgress` instead of `bar.progress.value`. Not difficult, but not trivial either — and the example app's current commit-on-pointer-up flow is already functional. Defer.
- **`requireInitialHit: false` is now mechanically redundant in chronix.** Since chronix drives pointer events through the root SVG and resolves them via the synthetic rect map, the "pointerdown didn't land on the subject element" scenario is structurally impossible — the hit-tester always emits a `'progress-handle'` kind when the rect contains the pointer. We still pass `ALLOW_MISS` for documentation of the original escape-valve intent + because some future consumer might add an actual overlay-layer renderer. The composable's runtime cost of the config is zero.
- **No `progress-handle-drag` recording-replay through the SFC.** The Phase 3 recording-replay test exercises `PointerCaptureSession` directly. A higher-fidelity test would replay the recorded pointerdown / pointermove / pointerup against `<ChronixGantt>` and assert the emitted `bar-progress` payload matches the recorded final state (`51%`). The math layer is already proven (recording-replay test #3 in `pointer-capture-session.test.ts`); replaying through the SFC would prove the full stack. Defer until a regression motivates it.
- **No protruding-triangle visual.** chronix renders a square handle; the reference renders a downward triangle that extends below the bar. Cosmetic only — the hit-test contract already supports a rect that protrudes past the bar bounds (see `'handle that protrudes below the bar still hits'` test). When chronix gets dedicated SVG-shape support, the handle can switch to `<polygon>` without changing the hit-test contract.
- **No "progress text" rendering.** `BarProgress.textFormat` is part of the IR (`"- {value}% 完成"` template) but the SFC doesn't render any text on the bar. Park alongside live-update; both are render-layer concerns that don't affect interaction semantics.

## Phase 3.x — DONE

- `'progress-handle'` is a first-class hit-tester zone; `useGanttPointer` routes hits to `beginProgressHandle`; `<ChronixGantt>` emits a `bar-progress` event after commit. Example app shows 3 bars with progress (50/25/80%); dragging the handle live-updates `bars.value` and the next render moves the handle.
- **235/235 vitest cumulative** (was 214; Phase 3.x added 21 — core: 7 hit-tester; adapter: 8 composable + 6 SFC).
- 17 parity assertions unchanged (the Phase 0 recording-replay for progress-handle continues to exercise the math layer; an SFC-level replay is parked).
- ci-check fully green: format / lint / typecheck / 236 vitest / build / banned-names 104 files.

## Phase 3.y — SFC-level recording-replay for `progress-handle-drag`

### Reference reading (Phase 3.y)

- `tooling/golden-runner/recordings/progress-handle-drag/log.json` — the Phase 0 recording. Structure: ordered `entries[]` of `pointer-down / pointer-move / pointer-up / state / snapshot` records. Pointer entries carry absolute (x, y) in the reference DOM's viewport space; state entries carry `eventText` like `"A33-液压系统检修 - 50% 进行中"` from which the percent is parseable.
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/pointer-capture-session.test.ts` (the existing Phase 3 math replay) — used as the structural template for the SFC replay. It hardcodes `barWidth = 6060` and the recorded pointer-down / -up x positions; the SFC replay extracts both at runtime from `log.json`.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 3.y)

- **The recording's absolute pointer-x is reference-DOM-bound.** The bar that captured the recording lived at a specific x in the reference's SVG; chronix has its own layout. Trying to replay the recorded x positions directly (1241.797 / 1301.797) would miss the chronix handle entirely. The replay uses the recorded _delta_ (60 px) + the recorded _barWidth_ (6060 px) and applies them at whichever chronix click position lands on the chronix-side handle.
- **`fs.readFileSync` + `import.meta.url` is the right way to load the recording fixture.** The adapter's tsconfig has `rootDir: "./src"`, so a TypeScript `import x from '../../../tooling/...'` would fail with "outside rootDir" — and adding the recording to `include` would pollute the build's `outDir`. Runtime fs reads bypass the type-system entirely. Pattern: `dirname(fileURLToPath(import.meta.url))` to resolve relative paths under ESM (no `__dirname` in ESM).
- **Parsing `eventText` for the percentage makes the test cite the recording, not a hardcoded number.** The recording stores `"... - 50% 进行中"` (before) and `"... - 51% 进行中"` (after); `/(\d+)%/.exec(text)` extracts the integer. The test asserts `Math.round(chronix newProgress) === parsed afterPct` — so a future re-capture that lands on a different percentage automatically becomes the new oracle.
- **Sanity-checks on the recording shape catch drift early.** Three pre-test `expect`s (`beforePct === 50`, `afterPct === 51`, `deltaX ≈ 60`) make sure the recording still has its expected pointer geometry. If the recording is re-captured and these change, the test fails up-front with a clear message rather than producing a confusing assertion-deep-in-the-SFC-emit failure.
- **`@typescript-eslint/prefer-optional-chain` triggered on `!match || match[1] === undefined`** in the regex parser. With `noUncheckedIndexedAccess: true`, indexing `match[1]` produces `string | undefined`. The lint rule wants `!match?.[1]` instead — but that's a `string | undefined`-returning expression that still narrows nicely. Apply via `eslint --fix`.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 3.y)

- `adapters/vue3/src/progress-handle-replay.test.ts` — single-test file (52nd test in the vue3 adapter; 58/58 total). Mounts `<ChronixGantt>` with a synthetic 6060-px-wide bar (101-hour range on day-view, slotWidth = 60), reads the recording log at runtime, derives the click position from `beforePct / 100 × barWidth`, triggers `pointerdown / pointermove +deltaX / pointerup` through `@vue/test-utils`, and asserts the emitted `bar-progress` payload's `Math.round(newProgress)` matches the recording's `after.eventText` percentage.
- The test sanity-checks the recording (`beforePct === 50`, `afterPct === 51`, `deltaX ≈ 60`) before the SFC assertion, so a future re-capture that drifts those values fails up-front with a clear message.

### Naming justifications (Phase 3.y)

- `progress-handle-replay.test.ts` (vs adding to `chronix-gantt.test.ts`): keeps the recording-fixture dependency isolated — the file owns its fs imports + recording-shape types in one place, and the recording-replay's "this consumes an external fixture" nature is signaled by the filename. If a second recording-replay lands (e.g. `event-drag-replay.test.ts`), the sibling-file pattern scales naturally.
- `RecordingPointerEntry` / `RecordingStateEntry` / `RecordingSnapshotEntry`: discriminated by `kind`, parallels the `AnyTransaction` union. Could be split into a shared types module if more recordings adopt the schema; for one file it's local.

### Open / parked (Phase 3.y)

- **Recording-shape types are local to this file.** If a second recording-replay test lands (e.g. the `wheel-scroll-right` recording or a future `event-drag` recording), extracting `RecordingEntry` + helpers to a shared module would deduplicate. Park until the second consumer materializes.
- **No replay of the mid-drag snapshot.** The recording includes a `keyframeId: "mid"` snapshot captured after 5 micro-steps of the drag. Asserting the in-flight `pointer.activeTransaction.value.projectedProgress` at the mid-point would prove chronix's per-step math too. Currently the test only asserts the commit value (chronix's commit-on-pointer-up flow). Once live-update lands (parked in Phase 3.x), the mid-snapshot becomes the natural fixture.
- **Recording is the only fixture in chronix that reads from `tooling/golden-runner/recordings/`.** A second recording-replay would create a cross-workspace import boundary worth formalizing — either via a TypeScript path mapping or by promoting `tooling/golden-runner` to expose recordings as a package export. Not needed for one consumer.

## Phase 3.y — DONE

- `<ChronixGantt>` is now proven end-to-end (SFC + composable + hit-tester + capture session + emit) against the recorded `progress-handle-drag` baseline: chronix's emitted `bar-progress` payload reproduces the recorded 50 % → 51 % transition with the recorded barWidth + deltaX.
- 236/236 vitest cumulative (was 235; Phase 3.y added 1 SFC-level recording-replay test). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 3.z — live-update progress during drag

### Reference reading (Phase 3.z)

- No new file reads. The reference shows progress text updating mid-drag (the captured `mid` keyframe in `progress-handle-drag/log.json` is a screenshot taken after 5 of 10 micro-moves); chronix had been commit-on-pointer-up until now. The mechanics — reading the in-flight transaction's `projectedProgress` during render — were obvious once the prior phases landed `activeTransaction` as a `ComputedRef`.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 3.z)

- **`pointer.activeTransaction.value` is already reactive enough to drive a render branch.** It's a `ComputedRef<AnyTransaction | null>` that Vue tracks as a dependency when the render function reads it; every `advance` mutation triggers a re-render automatically. No `watchEffect`, no manual subscription, no `nextTick` plumbing — the existing computed graph carries it.
- **The hit-tester rect stays anchored to the persisted `barProgressById`, not the live projection.** During an active drag, the hit-tester only fires at `begin`; subsequent `advance` calls don't consult the rect at all (the composable just feeds `currentPx` to the capture session). So the divergence between "where the visual handle is rendered" (live, `projectedProgress`) and "where the hit-tester thinks the handle is" (persisted, `bar.progress.value`) is invisible: the user clicks the persisted handle, drags, and during the drag only the visual position matters.
- **Clamping to `[0, 100]` happens in the render layer.** `ProgressHandleTransaction.projectedProgress` is intentionally unclamped (so the math stays linear past 100 %); commit clamps. For the live render the same `Math.max(0, Math.min(100, ...))` runs every frame — past-100 % drags pin the visible fill at `bar.width` and the handle at `bar.x + bar.width - handleSize/2`. Matches user expectation (the bar can't visibly fill past 100 %).
- **Post-commit the render falls through to `bar.progress.value`.** After `pointerup`, `activeTransaction` resets to null, so the render branch goes back to using the persisted value. In the example app the `onBarProgress` handler writes the new value back, so the next render shows the committed position. In the SFC test (no write-back) the fill snaps back to the original 50 % — a useful "what the demo's responsibility is" assertion.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 3.z)

- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: inside the bar-render loop, the progress fill + handle now consult `pointer.activeTransaction.value`. If it's a `'progress-handle'` kind on the current bar, the displayed progress comes from `projectedProgress` (clamped); otherwise it falls through to `bar.progress.value` (existing path). +12 lines, +4-line comment block.
- 4 new SFC vitest covering:
  - mid-drag pointermove moves the rendered handle x to the projected position (50 % → 60 % after +24 px on a 240-px bar)
  - mid-drag pointermove updates the progress-fill width
  - mid-drag projection clamps to [0, 100] when the cursor moves past the bar bounds
  - after pointer-up the live preview ends; fill width is back to the persisted `bar.progress.value`
- The example app needs no change: the handle visibly tracks the cursor during the drag automatically because the SFC's render is now reactive to `activeTransaction`.

### Naming justifications (Phase 3.z)

- `displayedProgress` (vs `renderedProgress` / `effectiveProgress`): names the property of the value (what's currently displayed), not the consumer (the renderer) or its provenance (persisted vs projected). Future "what the user sees" branches (e.g. showing a hover-preview progress) would reuse the same name.
- No new exported symbols — the live-update path is entirely internal to the render function. Public API surface (props, emits, types) unchanged.

### Open / parked (Phase 3.z)

- **`<text>` progress label still unrendered.** `BarProgress.textFormat` (`"- {value}% 完成"` template) is part of the IR but no text is rendered on or around the bar. The recording's `eventText` (`"A33-液压系统检修 - 50% 进行中"`) is the obvious target. Adding it is a render-only change — the live-update path here already supplies the right number to interpolate, so the work is just `<text>` placement + format-string substitution. Park until a real consumer needs it.
- **Same live-update treatment for bar-drag + bar-resize is parked.** A `'bar-drag'` transaction's `deltaX` could drive a translucent ghost of the bar at its projected position; `'bar-resize'` could drive a rubber-band edge. Both follow the same pattern (read `activeTransaction.value` in render, branch on `kind`). Phase 3.z proves the pattern with the simplest case; siblings can land when a consumer asks for them.
- **No live-update for `pointercancel`.** A pointercancel mid-drag should reset the visual preview without emitting a commit. Currently the only way to clear an in-flight transaction is `commit()`, which fires the emit. Phase 3.x's parked `pointer.abort()` API would close this; until then a cancelled drag visually pins the projected value briefly until the next pointerdown.
- **Recording's `mid` keyframe still doesn't have a state assertion.** The mid keyframe is a PNG, no `eventText`. To verify chronix's live-update against the reference, a future capture would need to read DOM text at the mid keyframe. Defer.

## Phase 3.z — DONE

- `<ChronixGantt>` now renders the progress fill + handle at the in-flight `projectedProgress` whenever a `'progress-handle'` transaction is active on the bar. Post-commit the render falls back to the persisted `bar.progress.value`. Example app demos the live preview automatically — no app-level change needed.
- **240/240 vitest cumulative** (was 236; Phase 3.z added 4 SFC live-update tests). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 3.aa — `<text>` progress label

### Reference reading (Phase 3.aa)

- No new reads. `BarProgress.textFormat` was part of the IR since Phase 1 (`packages/gantt/src/ir/bar-spec.ts:7`), and the recording's `eventText` (`"A33-液压系统检修 - 50% 进行中"`) was already the format reference for the math + replay tests. The render layer was the last missing piece.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 3.aa)

- **`{value}` is the only supported template token.** The IR doc comment on `BarSpec.progress.textFormat` is explicit (`"Template like '- {value}% 完成'; '{value}' is the only supported token"`). A single `.replace('{value}', String(rounded))` is the whole interpolation; no full template engine needed. Future tokens (e.g. `{barTitle}`) would extend the substitution function.
- **`showText: false` suppresses the label only.** Fill + handle keep rendering — the label is the most-suppressible piece, since some chronix consumers will want to show the fill as a visual indicator without cluttering narrow bars. The default `showText` is `true` per `BarProgress.showText?` (optional, defaults to true).
- **Label uses `Math.round` for the displayed number.** The clamped displayed progress is a `number` (could be `50.99` mid-drag); the label shows an integer. The math layer's `commit` returns the unrounded value; rounding happens at the render boundary (matches the example app's existing `Math.round(p.newProgress)` write-back).
- **Lookup of `BarSpec.progress` via `props.bars.find(b => b.id === bar.barId)` is `O(n × m)`** worst-case where n=placed bars and m=input bars. For typical demo sizes (~25 bars) this is fine; for a large dataset it would warrant a `Map<barId, BarSpec>` computed property. Park.
- **Text is `pointer-events: none`** so a click on the label still resolves through the bar's hit zone (same pattern as the progress fill + handle).

### Chronix work derived (Phase 3.aa)

- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: added a `<text class="cx-gantt-progress-label">` per bar with progress + overlay. Centered horizontally on `bar.x + bar.width / 2`, vertically near the bar's mid-line (`bar.y + bar.height / 2 + 4` for typographic baseline). Interpolates the template at render time using the live `displayedProgress` so the label updates mid-drag without separate plumbing.
- 4 new SFC vitest: default `"{value}%"` label render, custom textFormat with `{value}` token, `showText: false` suppression, live-update during drag (50% → 60% after +24 px).

### Naming justifications (Phase 3.aa)

- `cx-gantt-progress-label` (vs `cx-gantt-progress-text`): "label" matches the role (annotation on the bar) and parallels other axis "labels" (`cx-gantt-tick-label`, `cx-gantt-header-cell-label`). "Text" describes the SVG element, not the semantic.
- `template.replace('{value}', String(rounded))` (vs more elaborate templating): the IR docs constrain the surface to one token. Keeping the implementation literal makes the constraint visible — anyone wanting `{barTitle}` adds a new `.replace()` call and updates the IR doc together.

### Open / parked (Phase 3.aa)

- **Single-token template.** `BarSpec.progress.textFormat` only supports `{value}`. Future tokens (`{barTitle}`, `{remainingHours}`) require extending both the IR doc and the render-layer substitution.
- **`O(n × m)` bar lookup.** The per-bar `props.bars.find(...)` is fine for demo sizes but suboptimal at scale. A computed `barById: Map<barId, BarSpec>` would make it O(1). Park until a perf issue surfaces.
- **No `<title>` tooltip on the label.** A hover-tooltip showing the precise (unrounded) percentage would help precision-sensitive UIs. Trivial to add as a child of the `<text>`.
- **Label doesn't update its color based on bar's brightness.** The reference flips the label between dark and light text based on the bar's background brightness (the demo at DemoApp.vue:1466-1495). chronix's label is hardcoded dark green (`#064e3b`). When chronix gains a `barStyleCallback` analog, the label color should respond.

## Phase 3.aa — DONE

- Each bar with progress now shows a `<text class="cx-gantt-progress-label">` interpolating `BarSpec.progress.textFormat` (default `"{value}%"`). Label live-updates during the drag because it shares the `displayedProgress` value with the fill + handle.
- **244/244 vitest cumulative** (was 240; Phase 3.aa added 4 SFC label tests). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 3.bb — live-update for bar-drag + bar-resize

### Reference reading (Phase 3.bb)

- None new. The render-branch-on-`activeTransaction` pattern was established in Phase 3.z (progress-handle); 3.bb extends it to the other two pixel-space transactions.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 3.bb)

- **`renderX / renderY / renderWidth` is the per-bar render frame computed once at the top of the bar's flatMap iteration.** All overlay nodes (fill, handle, label) read from the same frame, so they stay anchored to the bar's visible body during any in-flight transaction (drag or resize). Before 3.bb the overlay used `bar.x / bar.y / bar.width` directly, which would have detached the overlay from the bar during the drag — visible drift between bar and progress indicator.
- **Resize cross-over clamps at the render layer, not the math.** The math layer (`commitBarResize`) explicitly allows `start > end` because some chronix consumers may want to permit it (or reject with a custom message). The render layer is opinionated: a negative width would render nothing useful (SVG quietly drops negative-width rects), so we `Math.max(0, ...)` and let the user see the bar collapse — clear "you've overshot" signal that's still recoverable by pulling back.
- **`'barId' in activeTxn`** narrows the union from `AnyTransaction` to the three transaction kinds that carry a `barId` (`bar-drag`, `bar-resize`, `progress-handle`), excluding `calendar-range-select` (which has `rowId`). TypeScript's `in` operator narrows nicely; no explicit type predicate function needed.
- **bar-drag y-delta is tracked but its visual impact is minimal in chronix v1.** The bar's `y` only shifts during the drag preview; on commit the demo writes the new range (which doesn't include y) and the bar's row is unchanged. To actually change rows on drag, the commit path would need to map `deltaY` to a row jump — Park 4.x candidate (see use-gantt-pointer's roadmap).

### Chronix work derived (Phase 3.bb)

- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: extracted `renderX/renderY/renderWidth` at the top of the bar render block, with branches for `'bar-drag'` (deltaX/deltaY shift) and `'bar-resize'` (edge-dependent x/width shift with `Math.max(0, ...)` clamp). All four overlay nodes (bar rect, fill, handle, label) now read from this frame.
- 7 new SFC vitest covering:
  - mid-drag x shift
  - mid-drag y shift
  - post-commit reset (no write-back)
  - progress overlay tracks the bar during a bar-drag (rect, fill, handle x all shift)
  - end-edge mid-resize grows width
  - start-edge mid-resize shifts x left and grows width
  - end-edge cross-over clamps to width 0

### Naming justifications (Phase 3.bb)

- `renderX / renderY / renderWidth` (vs `effectiveX` / `displayX`): names the render-time geometry consumed by the SVG nodes. Mirrors `displayedProgress` from Phase 3.z (which names the displayed value, not the bar's persisted one). Future "what the render shows for this bar" computations can extend the same `render*` prefix.

### Open / parked (Phase 3.bb)

- **Cross-row drag is not visually previewed.** A bar-drag with large deltaY moves the bar visually but stays within its strip's coordinates; the user can't see "I'd land on row 3" because the bar's y just floats with the cursor. A future change could project the cursor into the strip-y space and snap the preview to the matched strip's y, but it requires the commit path to support a row change too.
- **No animation on release.** When the demo doesn't write back (e.g. dropped on an invalid spot), the bar snaps back to its original position on the next render — no easing. A future render layer could read the pre-commit transaction state into a transition. Park.
- **`bar-drag` ghost vs in-place shift.** chronix shifts the bar's own rect; the reference shows a translucent ghost at the projected position while leaving the original in place. The in-place shift is simpler and matches the live-update philosophy from Phase 3.z; the ghost variant is a styling option that could live behind a prop.

## Phase 3.bb — DONE

- `<ChronixGantt>` now visibly previews `bar-drag` and `bar-resize` mid-drag: the bar rect (plus its progress overlay) shifts to match the in-flight transaction's delta. Post-commit the render falls back to the persisted layout. Example app inherits both previews automatically.
- **251/251 vitest cumulative** (was 244; Phase 3.bb added 7 SFC live-update tests). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 3.cc — `pointer.abort()` + pointercancel handler

### Reference reading (Phase 3.cc)

- None new. The need for an abort path was parked under Phase 4.1's "no `pointercancel` handling yet" item; everything was already wired except for the explicit abort method and the cancel handler.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 3.cc)

- **`abort()` is `commit()` minus the emit.** The state-reset half of `commit` (clear `transaction.value`, clear `lastHitResult.value`) is the only piece needed. Refactoring commit to share the reset would be over-engineering — two lines duplicated is cheaper than threading a "should-fire-callback" flag.
- **`pointercancel` is the right DOM event to listen for.** Browsers fire it when a pointer interaction is interrupted: touch cancellation by the OS, focus stolen by another window, certain gestures. Listening on `pointercancel` mirrors how native scrollers / dragger libraries handle interruption — it's the canonical signal that "the user's intent is no longer reachable."
- **Pointer capture release happens in the cancel handler too.** Same as `commit` — once the transaction's lifecycle ends, the SVG should stop receiving captured pointer events. The `releasePointerCapture` call is idempotent and safe to issue even if the browser already released capture as part of the cancellation.
- **No emit fires on cancel.** This is the key semantic: `commit` says "the drag finished with a meaningful intent"; `abort` says "the drag never reached commit, drop the state." Demos / consumers reading the events should NEVER see a synthetic `bar-drop / bar-resize / bar-progress / select` payload from a cancellation — that would silently corrupt their state.
- **`abort()` when idle is a safe no-op.** Both refs are already null; assigning null is harmless. The early-return in `onPointercancel` (when no transaction is active) avoids the unnecessary `releasePointerCapture` call but `abort()` itself doesn't need an internal guard.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 3.cc)

- `adapters/vue3/src/use-gantt-pointer.ts`: added `abort()` to `UseGanttPointerOutput`. Two-line implementation: `transaction.value = null; lastHitResult.value = null`. JSDoc explicitly states no commit callback fires — frames the contrast against `commit()` for readers.
- `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: new `onPointercancel` handler. Mirrors `onPointerup`'s structure (early-return when idle, capture release) but calls `pointer.abort()` instead of `pointer.commit()`. Wired into the SVG root via the `onPointercancel` event binding.
- 4 new composable vitest covering: abort clears in-flight without emit, abort then advance is no-op, abort then begin starts fresh, abort while idle is safe.
- 4 new SFC vitest covering: pointercancel mid-bar-drag, mid-bar-resize, mid-progress-handle, and pointercancel while idle.

### Naming justifications (Phase 3.cc)

- `abort()` (vs `cancel()` / `reset()`): "abort" matches the semantic of "the transaction did not complete its intended action" (cf. `AbortController` in the web platform). "cancel" overloads with `pointercancel` (the DOM event triggering it) and would read awkwardly as both event name and method name. "reset" suggests returning to a clean state with no implication about whether intent was lost.
- `onPointercancel` (no separator) follows Vue's `on<NativeEvent>` convention (matching `onPointerdown / onPointermove / onPointerup`); kebab-case `on-pointercancel` would be the template-prop variant, but in `h()` render functions Vue accepts both.

### Open / parked (Phase 3.cc)

- **No `pointerleave` handling.** When the user drags off the SVG bounds, modern browsers still fire `pointermove / pointerup` because of `setPointerCapture`. But on older platforms (and certain touch flows) the pointer can "leave" without firing capture-aware events. A future hardening could listen on `pointerleave` and abort if no pointer is captured. Defer until a real-world regression surfaces.
- **No keyboard escape.** Pressing Escape during a drag is the convention in many drag-and-drop libraries. Adding a global Escape listener would require either window-level binding (lifecycle-aware) or a focus-aware element. Skipped to keep the SFC DOM-free of focus management.
- **`abort()` from the consumer's `bar-*` handler.** A demo might want to validate the commit value and abort if invalid (e.g. dropping a bar outside its allowed row). Currently the commit callback fires synchronously inside `pointer.commit()`; there's no way to "un-commit" after the emit. A future `pointer.commitWithValidation((payload) => boolean)` hook could thread this through, but the existing pattern (demo validates and silently writes back the unchanged value) already works.

## Phase 3.cc — DONE

- The composable exposes `abort()`; `<ChronixGantt>` listens for `pointercancel` and calls it. In-flight transactions cleared by browser-initiated cancellation no longer fire stray commit callbacks.
- **259/259 vitest cumulative** (was 251; Phase 3.cc added 8 tests — 4 composable + 4 SFC). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 4.9 — week-view header-cell + monthFmt parity

### Reference reading (Phase 4.9)

- Read no new k-ui source files. The parity test diagnostic dump (`debugDump: all month-containing leaves`) revealed the reference's per-view monthFmt divergence directly from rendered DOM — faster than digging through `TimelineHeader.tsx` formatters.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 4.9)

- **Single-month vs banded-months render the year prefix differently.** `planMonthView` (1 cell spanning the entire axis) keeps the year context: `"2026年5月"`. `planMonthBandedAxis` (3 / 6 / 12 parallel month cells, season / halfYear / year) drops the year because every cell shares the same year and the band visually conveys it: `"五月"`, `"六月"`, etc. The reference DOM behaves the same way — different `Intl.DateTimeFormat` options per planner branch.
- **`Intl.DateTimeFormat('zh-CN', { month: 'long' })` emits Han-numeral month names.** `'五月'` (May), `'六月'` (June), …, `'十二月'` (December). Year view's full set is `{一月, 二月, …, 十二月}` — verified empirically against k-ui DOM at 8701, set-equal both sides. The narrow weekday format from Phase 4.7 + the year-prefix-only-for-single-month split here gives chronix character-for-character parity on every label across all six views.
- **Probe with regex over rendered DOM is the right reverse-engineering tool.** Faster than reading the reference's `TimelineHeader.tsx` source: `chart.evaluate` over leaf text-nodes, filter by `txt.includes('月') && !seen.has(txt)`, log the dump. The reference's exact format becomes visible in the diagnostic console.warn, then the regex tightens. Cost: 5 minutes per format probe vs ~30 minutes reading + tracing the formatter chain.
- **`chart.evaluate(callback, arg)` puts the root element as the FIRST callback param and the arg as the SECOND.** Forgetting that and destructuring the arg as the first param hands you `SVGElement.regexSource = undefined` and a confusing TypeScript error. The pattern `(_root, { ... }) => { ... }` is the right form when the callback only needs the arg.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.9)

- `packages/gantt/src/layout/axis-range-planner.ts`: `planMonthBandedAxis`'s monthFmt changed from `{ year: 'numeric', month: 'long' }` to `{ month: 'long' }`. `planMonthView` left unchanged. Comment added pointing to this journal section for the rationale.
- `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts`: 5 new parity assertions (1 week-view header cells + 4 monthFmt cells across day-resolution views). Per-view monthFmt regex map keyed by viewId since the format differs (`^\d+年\d+月$` for month view, `^[一二三四五六七八九十]+月$` for season / halfYear / year).
- 22 parity assertions total (was 17): 10 Phase 2 + 3 Phase 3 recording-replay + 4 Phase 4.7/4.8 day-resolution tick labels + 5 Phase 4.9 header cells. All empirically green against the k-ui demo at port 8701.

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.9)

- `MONTH_FMT_RE_BY_VIEW` (vs `monthCellRegex` / `headerLabelRegex`): names the mapping (one regex per view), follows the existing `IS_TIME_SCALE` map convention. Future format alignments (e.g. day-view header label) can add their own per-view maps without colliding.
- No new exported symbols — the planner change is internal; the parity tests are golden-runner-internal.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.9)

- **Bar-placement parity for non-day views is still untested.** Existing parity tests cover slot widths (all 6 views) + tick / header labels (all 6 views), but `BarPlacementPass` x+y+width parity (Phase 2's last DOM-comparison test) is day-view only. Extending it across views requires the reference's bar coords for each view, which the recording infrastructure doesn't capture today. Park until a regression motivates the work.
- **No parity for the `今天` (today) button state.** The view-toggle buttons render with state (active / non-active); the reference also has a "Today" button whose disabled state varies by view (disabled when today is already in range). chronix doesn't have a today button. Park behind a Phase 4.x view-management API.
- **No parity for `lineStyle` (dependency lines) yet.** The Phase 0 recording suite includes the line-style toggle scenarios but they haven't been wired into a parity assertion. Park until Phase 5 (LinkRouter parity work).
- **Bar progress overlay parity untested.** The reference renders a progress fill + triangle on bars with a progress value; chronix renders the same. A parity test for these would compare progress-fill widths + triangle x positions across views with the same bar set. Park until VRT goldens (Phase 4.4) make the comparison automatic.

## Phase 4.9 — DONE

- `planMonthBandedAxis` aligned with the reference DOM: emits `"五月"` etc. instead of `"2026年5月"` for season / halfYear / year header cells. Single-month view (`planMonthView`) unchanged.
- **22 parity assertions** (was 17): +5 from week-view header cells + per-view monthFmt cells. Empirically verified against k-ui demo at 8701.
- 259/259 vitest cumulative unchanged (the planner change re-uses existing test geometry; parity assertions live in golden-runner). ci-check fully green.

## Phase 4.4 — chronix-side VRT goldens

### Reference reading (Phase 4.4)

- Re-read `tooling/golden-runner/playwright.config.ts`, `tests/visual.spec.ts`, `src/config.ts`, `src/scenarios.ts` to understand the existing snapshot conventions. No new k-ui reading.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 4.4)

- **Capturing the `<svg>` element directly captures the full natural width.** The previous (k-ui) baselines used a chart-pane wrapper locator (`.demo-app-main`) which has `overflow: hidden` and clips at the viewport edge — those baselines are only complete for views whose axes fit in 1440 px (day view). Week / month / season / halfYear / year baselines on the reference side are silently incomplete. **chronix's baselines use `svg.cx-gantt` directly as the locator** — Playwright's `locator.screenshot()` rasterizes the element at its natural bounding-box width, regardless of viewport. The result: year-view PNG is 23725 × 215 pixels, not 1440 × 215.
- **PNG file sizes are smaller than expected thanks to compression.** Year view's 23725 × 215 = ~5.1 megapixels compresses to 20 KB because the bar area is mostly uniform color (white background, ~25 solid-color rects). Total: 5 baselines at 8–20 KB each = ~65 KB. Well under the 50 MB git-LFS threshold; no special handling needed.
- **Snapshot-path templating flattens `/` to `-`.** Setting the snapshot name to `chronix/view-day.png` in `expect(svg).toHaveScreenshot('chronix/view-day.png')` produces a file at `goldens/chronix-view-day.png`, not `goldens/chronix/view-day.png`. Playwright's path resolver treats the slash as part of the basename. Living with the flat layout because (a) it co-locates k-ui and chronix baselines for easy diffing and (b) the `chronix-` prefix gives clear namespace separation.
- **`exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` requires narrowing optional fields BEFORE the test closure captures them.** Reading `scenario.viewToggleLabel` inside the test callback re-evaluates the property as `string | undefined`, defeating the outer-loop `if (!toggleLabel) continue` guard. Pattern: extract to a local `const toggleLabel = scenario.viewToggleLabel; if (toggleLabel === undefined) continue;` so the closure captures a narrowed `string`.
- **`week-default` scenario is skipped for chronix.** The reference demo's initial load is week view (no toggle click needed); chronix's initial load is day view. Mapping `week-default` (which has no `viewToggleLabel`) to chronix would require a special path. Simpler: skip scenarios with no toggle label and rely on the `view-*` scenarios that explicitly drive each view via button click. Five chronix baselines (day / month / season / halfYear / year) vs. six reference baselines (week-default + view-day + 4 others) — acceptable asymmetry.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 4.4)

- `tooling/golden-runner/tests/chronix-visual.spec.ts` — new spec, captures the `svg.cx-gantt` element from `http://localhost:8702/` for each `VISUAL_SCENARIOS` entry with a `viewToggleLabel`. Resets `.cx-demo-svg-frame` scroll to (0, 0) before snapshot so captures are reproducible.
- `tooling/golden-runner/package.json` — new `chronix-capture` + `chronix-verify` scripts (mirror of `capture` + `verify` for the new spec).
- `tooling/golden-runner/goldens/chronix-view-{day,month,season,half-year,year}.png` — 5 baseline PNGs at natural SVG width (1440 / 2015 / 5980 / 11960 / 23725 px), 8–20 KB each. Captured against the chronix example demo running at 8702 with the FROZEN_TIME_ISO clock.

### Naming justifications (Phase 4.4)

- `chronix-view-*.png` (vs `chronix/view-*.png` subfolder): forced by Playwright's snapshot-path templating (`/` flattens to `-` in the filename). Treating the `chronix-` prefix as the namespace works fine; siblings can use `kui-` later if the existing baselines are renamed for clarity.
- `chronix-capture / chronix-verify` (vs `chronix:capture / chronix:verify`): npm-script naming convention. The existing `capture` / `verify` use hyphens; new scripts follow.

### Open / parked (Phase 4.4)

- **No `week-default` chronix baseline.** chronix's initial load is day view; the reference's is week view. To match the parity reference's `week-default` scenario, chronix would either need a "no toggle, just load" baseline (which would equal `view-day` since chronix initial-loads day view) or a default-view prop. Park.
- **k-ui side baselines may still be incomplete for week+.** The existing k-ui Phase 0 baselines were captured with chart-pane locator; week / month / season / halfYear / year baselines clip at the viewport's right edge. Re-capturing them with the SVG-element locator would close the gap. Defer until k-ui-side regression detection becomes a priority (chronix-side is the active development path).
- **No bar-progress overlay yet in goldens.** chronix renders progress fill + handle + label for bars with `progress` + `pointerOverlayId`. The example app's sample bars include 3 with progress (bar-2 50%, bar-5 25%, bar-8 80%) — these ARE in the baselines. Just noting that the visual surface for the new progress features is now baselined.
- **No mid-drag baselines.** Live-update from Phase 3.z + 3.bb is render-time only; capturing it would require pausing a drag mid-flight. Playwright supports this via `page.mouse.move + page.mouse.down + page.mouse.move + screenshot + page.mouse.up`, but it's an interaction recording, not a static baseline. Park behind a future Phase 3.dd "interaction-recording goldens".
- **`<ChronixGantt>` is a single SVG root.** The sticky-header refactor (Phase 4.5) will change this to a `<div>` with two children; baselines will need re-capture at that point. The current `chronix-` baselines are pinned to today's architecture.

## Phase 4.4 — DONE

- 5 chronix-side VRT baselines captured at full natural SVG width (1440 to 23725 px wide, 8–20 KB each), committed to `tooling/golden-runner/goldens/chronix-view-*.png`. New `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/golden-runner chronix-verify` runs the comparison; `chronix-capture` rebaselines if rendering changes. Empirically self-verifies (5/5 pass against own baselines).
- 259/259 vitest cumulative unchanged (VRT lives in golden-runner, gated behind the running chronix demo at 8702). ci-check fully green.

### Follow-up during the capture (2026-05-14 review)

Two issues surfaced when the user reviewed the captures + the running demo:

1. **Demo data was too narrow for wider views.** All 8 sample bars lived in today's hour-scale; week / month / season / halfYear / year baselines showed those bars only in the leftmost ~1/N of the axis and the rest was uniform white. Fix: extended `sample-data.ts` with 8 `multiDayBar(id, rowId, startDayOffset, durationDays, title)` entries spread across −10 days through +330 days. Now wider views show meaningful content end-to-end. Baselines re-captured (16 bars × 5 views; file sizes 8–20 KB unchanged because PNG compression dominates).
2. **Page layout overflowed horizontally in the browser.** With a wide-view SVG inside `.cx-demo-main` (which has `overflow: auto`), the CSS grid's default `min-width: auto` resolved to the SVG's intrinsic width — forcing the `1fr` track to expand past the viewport. The events sidebar got pushed off-screen, with extra blank to its right. Fix: `min-width: 0` on `.cx-demo-main` lets the grid track shrink to its assigned share; the SVG's `overflow:auto` wrapper handles its scroll internally. Added explicit `width: 100vw` on `.cx-demo-app` for belt-and-suspenders. Note: this is a CSS-only layout fix in the example app; `<ChronixGantt>` itself is unchanged. The VRT baselines (SVG-element-bound) are unaffected by the page-level layout.

The CSS layout fix doesn't change the rendered SVG — only the page chrome around it. Existing baselines stay valid; the user can verify the layout in browser at `http://localhost:8702/`.

## Phase 4.5 — sticky-header scroll wrapper

### Reference reading (Phase 4.5)

- Re-read the reference demo's split-pane layout (`.gantt-timeline-layout` → `.gantt-timeline-header-{left,right}` over `.gantt-timeline-body-{left,right}`), the wrapper hierarchy inside the right pane (`.gantt-timeline-header-wrapper` / `.gantt-timeline-body-wrapper` carry the full natural-width content; ancestor panes clip via `overflow: hidden / auto`), and how the reference syncs horizontal scroll between header-right and body-right panes (shared horizontal scroll, independent vertical scroll on each).
- Re-read the design note at `audit/PHASE_4_5_DESIGN.md` (Z-approved). Three candidates were considered: X (two SVGs, JS scroll-sync), Y (single SVG with `<foreignObject>` + CSS sticky inside), Z (overflow:auto wrapper, SVG body, header SVG with `position: sticky`).
