- k-ui drift-prevention catalog at `audit/PHASE_5_RESOURCE_AREA_DESIGN.md` enumerates 27 sub-behaviors with explicit dispositions; 17 are parked across 3 cohesive future-phase groups.

## Phase 5.x — vGrouping rowspan merge (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 5.x)

- `packages/gantt/src/resource-timeline/ResourceList.tsx` lines 207–377 — the resource-row renderer with rowSpan logic. `rowSpans[colIndex]` matrix carries `0 / 1 / N` per cell: `0` skips the cell entirely (absorbed by an earlier rowspan), `N > 1` emits the leading cell with `rowSpan=N`, anything else (undefined / 1) is an individual cell. The matrix is computed externally and passed in; ResourceList just renders.
- `packages/gantt/src/resource-timeline/GanttView.tsx` lines 2176–2210 — auto-toggle for `isVGrouping`: when ANY column has `colSpec.group: true`, the renderer enters vGrouping mode (group columns become rowSpan-merged columns, no standalone group rows). The reference's vue3 demo has 2 `group: true` columns (`airportName`, `baseName`), so it's always in vGrouping mode.
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue` lines 1273–1290 — the demo's `resourceAreaColumns` config: 3 columns (`airportName`, `baseName`, `workshopName`). First two are `group: true`; third is the leaf. NO expand/collapse glyph is rendered because the demo doesn't trigger the standalone-group-rows path (`isVGrouping: false`).
- Resource data in `DemoApp.vue` lines 28–100ish — flat structure with no `parentId`. The "tree" is purely value-based (consecutive rows sharing `airportName` merge under one cell).

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 5.x)

- **Adjacency, not equality.** The merge rule is "adjacent + equal" — two rows with the same value separated by a different-valued row don't merge. A sandwich pattern (`海口`, `三亚`, `海口`) produces three rowspan=1 cells, not two. This matches the reference's behavior and keeps the render deterministic when rows reorder.
- **rowSpan height must match the body's strip y-range, not just the row count.** A `rowspan=N` `<td>` visually spans N consecutive `<tr>` rows. For the cell to align with the body's strips at the right y-range, each `<tr>` height must equal `strip.height + rowSpacing` for non-last rows (and `strip.height` for the last). Baking `rowSpacing` into the `<tr>` heights makes the table's total height equal the body's content height, and any `rowspan=N` cell automatically spans `N × strip.height + (N-1) × rowSpacing` (the body's y-range for those strips + gaps).
- **HTML `<table>` is the right tool for rowspan, even mid-CSS-grid.** CSS grid's `grid-row: span N` doesn't merge cell content — only the track allocation. For visual merge (one cell painted across multiple rows), HTML `<td rowspan="N">` is the native primitive. The wrapper's outer `display: grid` (for sidebar / chart panes) and the sidebar's inner `<table>` coexist cleanly — the table sits inside one grid cell.
- **`<colgroup>` shares per-column widths between header and body.** Both the sidebar-header `<table>` and the sidebar-body `<table>` carry a `<colgroup>` derived from the same `ColumnSpec.width` values. CSS `table-layout: fixed` then resolves column widths from `<col>` widths, so per-column vertical borders align across the two tables by construction. No JS layout sync needed.
- **`border-collapse: collapse` is required for rowSpan visual continuity.** With `border-collapse: separate`, each row's cell borders are drawn independently; a rowspan cell would show internal cell-border lines at the row boundaries. `collapse` merges adjacent borders into one — the rowspan cell renders as a single tall block with one continuous outer border.
- **Vue's `h()` accepts both `rowspan: N` and `rowSpan: N` for HTML elements.** The serialized attribute is `rowspan` (HTML standard). Tests query via `attributes('rowspan')` which returns the string value, or `undefined` if the attribute isn't on the element. `expect(...).toBeUndefined()` is the way to assert absence.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 5.x)

- **Commit 1** (`e3362dc`) — `ColumnSpec.group?: boolean` flag, exported `computeRowSpans(rows, columns)` pure function returning a `[colIdx][rowIdx]` matrix, and the sidebar DOM switch from `div + CSS grid` to actual HTML `<table>` with `<colgroup>` + `<thead>` + `<tbody>`. Merged cells (rowspan > 1) get `font-weight: 600` + `text-align: center`; leaf cells keep normal weight + left alignment. `<tr>` heights bake `rowSpacing` into non-last rows so rowspan cells align with body strip y-ranges. 13 new SFC tests (97 → 110).
- **Commit 2** (`969884e`) — extended `sampleRows` with `region` + `base` fields (海口×3 + 三亚×1 for region; 海口基地×2 + 空港基地×1 + 三亚基地×1 for base) so the demo exercises both single-merge (rowspan=2) and longer-merge (rowspan=3) cases. App.vue's `columns` becomes 3 entries with `group: true` on the first two. VRT baselines re-captured: each PNG grew by exactly +120 px in width (sidebar 120 → 240) and +2 px in height (table's row-edge handling).

### Naming justifications (Phase 5.x)

- **`group: boolean`** (vs `isGroupColumn` or `vGroup`): mirrors the reference's `ResourceColumnSpec.group`. The reference's `isVGrouping` is the COMPONENT-level mode flag (auto-derived from "any column has group"); chronix doesn't need the boolean because the merge logic just consults each column's own `group` flag independently.
- **`computeRowSpans`** (exported function, vs internal helper): exported so users can compute and inspect the matrix in tests or in their own renderers without instantiating `<ChronixGantt>`. Pure function, no side effects, no Vue dependencies.
- **`spans` over `rowSpans` as the local var name**: shorter, the function-name + type signature already make "row spans" clear. Saves a column of horizontal space in the render code.

### Open / parked (Phase 5.x)

- All 9 other catalog items in the original "tree-grouping" parking group stay parked, each annotated with the demo-side observation that grounds the deferral. See updated `audit/PHASE_5_RESOURCE_AREA_DESIGN.md` catalog rows #4, #5, #8, #13, #14, #15, #20, #21, #24.
- The k-ui auto-detect `isVGrouping = (any column has group)` rule isn't ported — chronix uses per-column `group: true` directly. If a future need arises for component-level mode toggling (e.g. "render group columns as standalone rows instead of merged columns"), this is the right hook.

## Phase 5.x — DONE

- 3 commits: `ef4b301` (design doc, narrowed scope), `e3362dc` (rowspan + table DOM + 13 tests), `969884e` (demo wiring + VRT rebaseline). `<ChronixGantt>` now accepts `ColumnSpec.group?: boolean`; consecutive rows sharing a `group: true` column's value merge into one `<td rowspan=N>` cell. Bold weight on merged cells.
- 110 vue3-adapter tests (was 97; +5 `computeRowSpans` unit tests + +8 sidebar render tests). 178 core gantt tests unchanged. **Total cumulative vitest 288.** 22 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-captured to include the 3-column merged sidebar: day 1680 / month 2255 / season 6220 / halfYear 12200 / year 23965 (×217 each, sidebar 240 px wide).
- ci-check fully green. Browser-verified: 地区 cell spans 3 rows (rowspan=3, bold), 基地 cells span 2 + 1 + 1 rows respectively, 车间 cells render individually (one per row, normal weight). Sidebar still pins sticky-left during horizontal scroll.
- Catalog at `audit/PHASE_5_RESOURCE_AREA_DESIGN.md` updated: items #1, #3, #6, #18 flipped from ⏸️ parked to ✅ done. Items #4, #5, #8, #13, #14, #15, #20, #21, #24 explicitly retained as parked with the "reference demo doesn't exercise this" observation cited.

## Phase 6 — Non-day-view bar-placement parity (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 6)

- `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts:491–664` (the pre-Phase-6 day-view bar-placement parity test) — full pipeline: build test events from `buildTestEvents(todayMs)`, load view, probe rendered row order, run chronix `axis → bar-stack-height → row-swimlane → bar-placement` passes, extract DOM bar rects, compare per-event-id.
- The reference's vue3 demo's resource list is invariant across view switches — toggling 日/周/月/季/半年/年 doesn't change the resource ordering, just the time axis. This lets the probe-row-order step run once per test without re-probing per-view.
- The reference's `.gantt-timeline-body-wrapper` is the natural-width container — its `getBoundingClientRect()` reports absolute page coordinates regardless of horizontal scroll position, so bars rendered far off the visible viewport (e.g. an event 24000 px out on year view) still report their true x via `r.left - wrapperLeft`.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 6)

- **Chronix's layout pipeline is view-agnostic.** Each pass (`AxisRangePlanner`, `BarStackHeightPass`, `RowSwimlaneLayout`, `BarPlacementPass`) takes the viewId as input and emits results keyed off the view's range. Same code, different range → different but correct output. Day-view parity proved the math is right at one range; the question was whether it's right at all ranges. Answer: yes, no special-casing needed.
- **Wider views see more events per row, which changes strip heights.** `BarStackHeightPass` filters bars to those intersecting the axis range. Day view sees ~13 events (those overlapping today); year view sees all 25. Some rows in year view stack 2–3 events high vs 1 high in day view. The strip heights chronix computes match the reference DOM heights at every view — strong evidence the bar-stack pass's greedy interval coloring is reference-equivalent.
- **Per-view test isolation comes for free with Playwright's `test(...)` granularity.** Six independent test blocks, each fresh page + clock-install + view-toggle. If a future change breaks just one view, that view's test fails alone and the diff is precise.
- **`buildTestEvents()` event count vs visible-bar count.** Day-view compared 13 of 13 visible bars; week 20 of 20; month/season/halfYear/year all 25 of 25. The "13 visible" on day view comes from the demo's events spanning -7..+30 day offsets — only those intersecting today (range [-N..+M] containing 0) render on day view. Year covers the full span, so 25/25.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 6)

- **Commit 1** (`6c9493b`) — design doc with single-commit scope, hard-assert pattern preserved, per-view test isolation via independent `test(...)` blocks. Listed the view-specific event-count expectations (13 / 20 / 25 / 25 / 25 / 25) and out-of-scope items (cross-row migration, progress-handle position, multi-segment weekend split).
- **Commit 2** (`b73ff52`) — refactor: extracted day-view test body into `runBarPlacementParity(page, viewId, viewToggleLabel)` returning `{ comparedCount, failures, totalDomBars, totalChronixBars, wrapperRowOffsetY }`. Added `assertBarPlacementParity(result)` to print diagnostics + hard-assert. The existing day-view test shrunk from ~175 lines to one line: `assertBarPlacementParity(await runBarPlacementParity(page, 'day', '日'))`. Added five new tests mirroring the same one-liner per view.
- **No layout-code changes.** All five new tests passed on first run. The "silent drift in wider views" hypothesis is empirically refuted for the demo's event set + the 6 supported views.

### Naming justifications (Phase 6)

- **`runBarPlacementParity`** (vs `assertBarPlacement` or `parity`): the function runs the comparison and returns the result; the assertion happens in a separate `assertBarPlacementParity`. Splitting them keeps each test block's contract explicit (what's asserted) while letting all 6 tests share the comparison engine.
- **`assertBarPlacementParity`** (separate from `runBarPlacementParity`): centralized diagnostic printing + assertion. Each test now reads: "run it, assert it." Cleaner than inlining the `console.warn` + `expect` calls per test.

### Open / parked (Phase 6)

- **Cross-row bar Y assertion** — would only fire if a bar's `rowId` changes between chronix's input and the reference's render. The current pipeline preserves rowId verbatim; not a real risk yet. Park.
- **Interaction parity per view** (drag / resize / progress on week+ views) — Phase 3's recording-replay covers the math layer; visual interaction parity is a separate phase candidate, scope TBD.
- **Multi-segment bar rendering** (bars split across weekends in views where weekend visibility is off) — reference's demo doesn't toggle weekendsVisible off, so this codepath isn't exercised. Park.

## Phase 6 — DONE

- 2 commits: `6c9493b` (design doc, approved) + `b73ff52` (test refactor + 5 new parity assertions). Test-only change; no component code, no demo, no VRT impact.
- **Parity assertion count: 17 → 22** (+5 non-day bar-placement). Total per-view assertions are now: tick labels (5 set-equality + 1 day-direct), header-row monthFmt (4 set-equality), slot widths (6 geometry), bar placement (6 full pipeline). Plus the original day-view tick-label set-equality.
- 288 vitest unchanged (parity tests live in golden-runner, not vitest). ci-check fully green.
- Chronix layout pipeline now verified pixel-equivalent to the reference demo across all 6 timeline scales for the full 25-event demo set, with the strip-height + stack-collision + y-offset machinery all reference-equivalent.

## Phase 7 — Smooth LinkRouter (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 7)

- `packages/gantt/src/timeline/DependencyLineAlgorithm.ts:358–510` — `setSmoothPoints(line)` with 4 branches based on `fromY === toY` × `fromX ≤ toX` cross-product. Same-row + forward collapses to a straight `L`; cross-row + forward emits a cubic Bézier with control points `(midX, fromY)` + `(beforeTargetX - 10, toY)` ending at `(beforeTargetX, toY)`, then a horizontal `L`. Backward variants (target on left) use a square detour (same-row) or a compound `C` + `S` (cross-row).
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue` — `const lineStyle = ref<'square' | 'smooth'>('square')` toggle; reference's demo has the smooth path wired but defaults to square. No backward links in the demo's `RESOURCES[]` × `EVENTS[]` data.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 7)

- **Two ends always horizontal.** Both the square and smooth routings end with a horizontal `L` segment from `(prevX, to.y)` to `(to.x, to.y)`. This makes the marker geometry routing-agnostic — `angleDeg: 0` is always correct. The 20-px pre-target landing gap exists specifically to guarantee the curve has resolved to horizontal before the final segment.
- **Empirical control-point offsets > formulaic ones.** First instinct was to use `(fromX + (toX-fromX)/3, fromY)` + `(fromX + 2*(toX-fromX)/3, toY)` (symmetric one-third splits). The reference uses `(midX, fromY)` + `(beforeTargetX - 10, toY)` — the second control point is 10 px in from the target side, not symmetric. Effect: the curve enters the source horizontally for the first half, then turns down/up to land on the target's y by the second half — a "near-S" shape vs a "lazy-S" of the symmetric variant. Matching the reference makes future VRT parity (when link rendering lands in the adapter) plug-and-play.
- **Backward direction parking has a clear failure shape.** `to.x < from.x` lands in `if (link.routing === 'smooth')` but isn't covered by the forward branch; throwing `'smooth' routing for backward links not yet implemented` (with the link id in the message) makes the parked branch findable when a consumer hits it. Same evidentiary discipline as Phase 5.x's parked items.
- **TypeScript exhaustiveness via `_exhaustive: never`.** After handling both `'square'` and `'smooth'`, the `else` branch's `link.routing` narrows to `never`. The `restrict-template-expressions` ESLint rule rejects interpolating `never` directly. Pattern: `const _exhaustive: never = link.routing; throw new Error(...${String(_exhaustive)}...)`. Same workaround `AxisRangePlanner` uses for view exhaustiveness.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 7)

- **Commit 1** (`975a2ad`) — design doc with forward-only scope, reference algorithm's 4-branch table, demo-evidence rationale for parking branches 2 + 4, reference's control-point formula matched verbatim.
- **Commit 2** (`b686dcd`) — three files touched:
  - `packages/gantt/src/layout/types.ts` — `LinkRouterInput.smoothBeforeTargetGapPx?: number` (default 20).
  - `packages/gantt/src/layout/link-router.ts` — new `routeSmoothPath(from, to, gap)` helper; routing switch reorganized as `square` → `smooth` (forward) → exhaustive `never` throw. Backward branch throws with the parked-branch-identifier message.
  - `packages/gantt/src/layout/link-router.test.ts` — replaced the old "throws on smooth" test with 6 new positive tests covering same-row forward (straight `L`), cross-row forward (cubic `C` + `L`), custom gap override, marker still 0°, degenerate self-loop, and backward-throws regression.
- **183 core gantt tests** (was 178; +5 net from link-router going 12 → 17). 110 vue3 adapter tests unchanged. **Total cumulative vitest 293.**

### Naming justifications (Phase 7)

- **`routeSmoothPath`** (vs `routeCubicBezier` or `routeSmoothBezier`): "smooth" is the IR's `LinkRouting` value the function implements. Naming after the IR field is more grep-friendly than naming after the path command (`C` is one segment of the output; the function emits both `M`, `C`, and `L`).
- **`smoothBeforeTargetGapPx`** (vs `smoothLandingGapPx` or `smoothPreTargetPx`): "before target" matches the reference's `beforeTargetX` variable; "gap" because it's the distance, not the position. The `Px` suffix matches `elbowNubPx`.

### Open / parked (Phase 7)

- **Backward smooth routing** — reference's branches 2 + 4. The same-row-backward case (branch 2) uses a square detour with vertical clearance (not actually a Bézier); the cross-row-backward case (branch 4) uses a compound `C` + `S`. Neither is exercised by the reference's vue3 demo. Park behind explicit throw.
- **Link rendering in `<ChronixGantt>` adapter** — chronix's adapter doesn't render `<path>` elements for routed links yet. The IR field, the layout pass, and the test coverage all exist; what's missing is the SVG rendering. Park as a separate phase; would require demo data extension + new SFC tests + VRT impact.
- **Smooth-routing VRT parity test** — would compare chronix's path string vs reference DOM's rendered path attribute when both demos toggle to `'smooth'`. Park until link rendering lands in the chronix adapter (otherwise no chronix-side path to compare).
- **Performance characteristics under high link counts** — chronix's `route()` is O(links × bars) for the bar lookup; same complexity as before. No SVG-string-builder optimization is needed at v0 scale; the reference's `points`-array intermediate isn't reproduced because chronix emits the string directly.

## Phase 7 — DONE

- 2 commits: `975a2ad` (design doc) + `b686dcd` (implementation + 6 new tests). One module changed (`packages/gantt/src/layout/`); no adapter / demo / VRT impact.
- **183/183 core vitest** (was 178; +5 link-router net). 110/110 vue3 adapter tests unchanged. **Total cumulative vitest 293.** 27 parity assertions unchanged (link-routing parity test parked behind chronix-side link rendering).
- Forward-only scope per design; backward branches throw with explicit "parked" message. Control-point formula matches the reference verbatim.
- ci-check fully green. Closes one of the standing "feature gaps where chronix would crash if a consumer flipped a typed-but-unsupported flag" backlog items — `LinkSpec.routing: 'smooth'` now works for the demo-evidenced cases.

## Phase 8 — Link rendering in `<ChronixGantt>` (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 8)

- `packages/gantt/src/timeline/TimelineDependencies.tsx:1-1716` — full dependency-line render layer. Critical sections: `renderMarker` (519–663) for the 7 built-in marker shape geometries; the top-level `render()` (954+) for the `<defs>` block organization and per-color × per-markerType × per-direction marker generation; the marker grouping logic (1047–1189) that dedupes markers when multiple links target the same bar.
- `packages/gantt/src/timeline/DependencyLineAlgorithm.ts` — already audited Phase 7; Phase 8 only confirmed it was the canonical source for marker placement angles.
- `packages/gantt/src/resource-timeline/GanttView.tsx:790-810` — `<div className="gantt-dependency-lines-layer">` at `zIndex: 2`, ABOVE the bar SVG at `zIndex: 1`, with `pointerEvents: 'none'`. Inside, the SVG itself is `position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%`.
- `packages/gantt/src/resource-timeline/ResourceTimelineDependencies.tsx:4496-4497` — `<path className="gantt-dependency-line" strokeWidth={1.5} fill="none" stroke={lineColor} markerEnd={markerEnd}>` is the per-link shape. Wrapped in `<g className="arrow">`.
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1298-1638` — config surface: `lineStyle`, `dependencyLineColor` (default `#3788d8`), `useLineEventColor`, `markerType`, `onLine` callback.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 8)

- **No interactivity on links.** The dependency SVG is `pointer-events: none` end-to-end; no hover, no selected state, no click handler. Bar pointer events flow through. chronix mirrors this — `<g class="cx-gantt-links" pointer-events="none">`.
- **Marker registry deduped by (type × color × direction).** Reference uses a `Set<string>` of `usedColors` × the 7 builtin marker types × 3 directions (horizontal / vertical-up / vertical-down). chronix v0 only emits horizontal (forward-only routing → always 0° marker angle) so it skips the direction axis. 7 × N colors × 1 direction defs, plus custom markers × N colors. Marker id format `${type}-${colorId}` where `colorId = color.replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g, '')` — chronix matches verbatim with `cx-marker-` prefix.
- **`<defs>+marker-end` over inline shapes.** Marker shape lives in `<defs>`; `<path>` references via `marker-end="url(#...)"`. `markerUnits="strokeWidth"` auto-scales with stroke; `orient="auto"` derives angle from the path's last segment. Since chronix's forward paths always end with a horizontal `L` segment, `orient="auto"` yields 0° automatically — `RoutedLinkMarker.angleDeg` is redundant for the SVG path but kept on the routing output for off-DOM consumers.
- **Marker geometry tuning is fragile.** Each marker has a specific `refX` value that lands its tip exactly on the path's endpoint. e.g. `circle-hollow` uses `refX=5.75` because the visible right edge of the stroked circle is at `cx + r + strokeWidth/2 = 3 + 2.0 + 1.5/2 = 5.75`. Off-by-one here means a visible gap between line tip and marker. chronix ported verbatim.
- **Z-order via paint sequence in the same SVG.** chronix collapses k-ui's two-SVG arrangement (bar SVG + dependency SVG via z-index) into one body SVG with siblings `<g class="cx-gantt-bars">` then `<g class="cx-gantt-links">`. SVG paint order does the same job as z-index when the parent is one SVG. Tested visually post-rebaseline; links sit on top of bars.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 8)

- **Commit 1** (`5a932d1`) — design doc with the full 27-item catalog (9 routing-geometry items, 5 marker-shape items, 5 stroke+color items, 1 marker strategy, 3 DOM-structure items, 2 interactivity items, 2 performance items). 9 items closed, 14 parked, 4 rejected.
- **Commit 2** (`5f07a6b`) — bare `<path>` rendering. `<ChronixGantt>` props `links: readonly LinkSpec[]` (default `[]`) + `defaultLinkColor: string` (default `#3788d8`) + `'link-orphan'` emit. `defaultLinkRouter.route()` runs in `setup()`; orphan ids surface via `watchEffect`-driven emit + `console.warn` (warned-once Set per component). Render emits `<g class="cx-gantt-links" pointer-events="none">` AFTER the bars group inside body SVG, one `<path class="cx-gantt-link" data-link-id="...">` per `RoutedLink`. 5 SFC tests in `link-rendering.test.ts`. vue3 110 → 115.
- **Commit 3** (`65088ce`) — marker `<defs>` + `marker-end` wiring + colorOverride. Three private helpers landed: `markerColorId(color)`, `renderBuiltinMarker(type, color, colorId)`, `renderCustomMarker(marker, color, colorId)`, `markerEndUrl(marker, color)`. Built-in marker geometry ports verbatim (refX/refY/orient/polygon-points all preserved). Body SVG gains a `<defs class="cx-gantt-defs">` block containing one `<marker>` per (markerType × usedColor) for the 7 built-ins, plus one per (customMarker.id × usedColor). 9 new SFC tests. vue3 115 → 124.
- **Commit 4** (`d4688b0`) — demo wiring + VRT rebaseline. 6 sample `LinkSpec`s in `sample-data.ts` per the (routing × marker × color) matrix from the design doc, plus 1 `CustomLinkMarker` (heart shape). Rebaselined `chronix-view-day.png` + `chronix-view-month.png`; the other three views were byte-identical post-regen. End-to-end browser verify via `D:/tmp/chronix-link-probe.mjs` Playwright probe: 1 wrapper, 1 body, 6 paths, 24 marker defs (7 built-in × 3 used colors + 1 custom × 3 colors = 24).

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 8)

- **Hand-coded `placedBars` in tests is fragile** — first attempt to compute expected router output in a test pre-baked strip Y at 47 from a guess. Actual strip Y was 51 (Phase 2 stack-height math). Fix: run the same layout passes the adapter runs (`AxisRangePlanner` → `BarStackHeightPass` → `RowSwimlaneLayout` → `BarPlacementPass`) in the test setup to produce real `placedBars`, then route. The 5-line helper in `link-rendering.test.ts` is reusable for any future SFC test that needs deterministic layout output.
- **happy-dom `:scope > g` selector unreliable** — replaced `bodySvg.querySelectorAll(':scope > g')` with `Array.from(bodySvg.children).filter(...)` for first-level children. Saves a happy-dom version dependency.
- **Smooth backward links crash, even when "the diff says forward"** — initial sample links included `bar-4 (b, 2-7h) → bar-8 (d, 4-11h)` because bar-8's id sorts later; but bar-8 STARTS at hour 4, BEFORE bar-4 ENDS at hour 7. The router's "backward smooth" branch throws (parked Phase 7 behavior). Browser verify caught it via `console.warn` — page didn't render at all because of the unhandled-error throw in `setup()`. Lesson: every smooth sample link needs `source.range.end ≤ target.range.start`, not just `source.id alphabetically < target.id`. Updated sample data to make this constraint explicit in the comment.
- **vite running stale source during VRT capture** — capture against the previous-day vite instance picked up the OLD `App.vue` (which didn't have the `:links` prop yet) and the sample-data without `sampleLinks` export. Killing the vite PID + restarting picked up the new code. The memory `feedback_vrt_screenshots.md` flags this pattern.
- **ESLint `restrict-template-expressions` blocks `${neverTypedVar}` in template literals** — solved in `renderBuiltinMarker`'s exhaustiveness throw via the `const _exhaustive: never = type; throw new Error(... ${String(_exhaustive)} ...)` pattern that AxisRangePlanner / LinkRouter already use.

### Naming justifications (Phase 8)

- **`cx-marker-${type}-${colorId}`** as marker id (vs `cx-gantt-marker-...` or `cx-link-marker-...`): "marker" alone is the SVG term; the `cx-` prefix already namespaces it to chronix. Two-level "gantt-marker" would conflict with future markers from other chronix packages (table, input, etc.) so the type+color disambiguator is enough.
- **`defaultLinkColor`** prop (vs `linkColor` or `dependencyLineColor`): "default" because per-link `colorOverride` wins; "link" because chronix's IR uses `LinkSpec` throughout (matches the chronix taxonomy from `MODULE_TAXONOMY.md`).
- **`'link-orphan'`** emit event name (vs `'orphan-link'` or `'unresolved-link'`): kebab-case noun-first matches the existing `'bar-drop'` / `'bar-resize'` / `'bar-progress'` event names. `link-orphan` reads as "link [event subtype] orphan", same as `bar-drop` reads as "bar [event subtype] drop".

### Open / parked (Phase 8)

- **Backward smooth routing** — still parked at router layer per Phase 7. No way to demo it now because chronix has no consumer that flips a link backward.
- **Per-direction marker variants** (`vertical-up` / `vertical-down`) — parked alongside the clipped-edge routing. Activated when chronix gains a viewport-clipping pipeline that distinguishes "target left edge past viewport" from normal routing.
- **Marker grouping & vertical/horizontal offset** when multiple links target the same bar — parked. v0 renders one path + marker per link regardless of collisions.
- **`useLineEventColor` toggle** (line color = source bar's color) — parked behind `BarSpec` gaining a color/styling field. Currently chronix bars are uniform-styled.
- **Hover / selected / click on link** — rejected per catalog item 24 / 25. Future "link selection" feature is Phase 9+ scope.
- **Memoization of `<defs>`** — parked. Naive rebuild per render is ≤140 marker nodes worst case; profiling can drive when this becomes hot.

## Phase 8 — DONE

- 4 commits total: `5a932d1` (design doc) + `5f07a6b` (Commit 1: paths) + `65088ce` (Commit 2: markers) + `d4688b0` (Commit 3: demo + VRT). Two implementation files touched: `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts` (props + render + helpers) + `adapters/vue3/src/link-rendering.test.ts` (new). One demo touched: `examples/gantt-vue3/src/{App.vue, sample-data.ts}`. Two VRT baselines rebaselined: `chronix-view-day.png` + `chronix-view-month.png`.
- **183/183 core vitest** unchanged. **124/124 vue3 adapter tests** (was 110; +14 link-rendering net). **Total cumulative vitest 307.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified idempotent after rebaseline.
- ci-check fully green. The render-layer gap from Phase 7 is closed — `<ChronixGantt :links="...">` now renders dependency arrows matching the parity reference's geometry for all forward-direction cases.

## Phase 9 — Cross-row bar drag (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 9)

- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventDragging.ts:170-280, 634-683` — `computeEventMutation(hit0, hit1, ...)` builds an `EventMutation` from the cross-product of (initial hit, current hit). `hit.dateSpan.resourceId` is the row the pointer is currently over. Cross-row update is folded into the same mutation as the time delta — applied to the `EventStore` via `applyMutationToEventStore`.
- `packages/gantt/src/internal/interactions/HitDragging.ts` (via imports) — `HitDragging` is the layer that tracks `initialHit` / `lastValidHit` / current `hit` across pointer events. chronix's existing `PointerCaptureSession` covers the same surface for a single subject; the cross-row row-resolution is layered on top via the composable.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 9)

- **Row resolution belongs in the composable layer, not the core IR.** chronix's `BarDragTransaction` is a pure value type (kind + barId + originPx + deltaX + deltaY). Adding `projectedRowId` to it would push strip awareness into the DOM-free + layout-free `interaction/` module. Keeping it in the composable (`useGanttPointer`) where `strips` already live preserves the layer separation. The composable exposes `projectedRowId: ComputedRef<string | null>` for live read-out; the render path consumes it for snap geometry.
- **Half-open interval is the right model for strip ownership.** A pointer y exactly on `strip[i].y` belongs to strip[i] (lower-inclusive), and a y exactly on `strip[i].y + strip[i].height` belongs to NO strip when `rowSpacing > 0` (upper-exclusive). This mirrors chronix's other layout passes (axis tick ranges, viewport visible ranges) and matches the geometric reality of the rendered 1-px row-divider border.
- **Intra-strip offset preservation is what makes the snap feel right.** A bar 8 px below its source strip's top sits 8 px below the target strip's top mid-drag. Top-aligning to `targetStrip.y + barVerticalPadding` would look correct for uniform-height strips but would jump the bar visually when target strip height differs. Preserving the offset is also what the reference's mirror does. Implementation: `renderY = targetStrip.y + (bar.y - sourceStrip.y)`.
- **The 1-px rowSpacing gap is real geometry, not a special case.** When the pointer slides through the divider between two strips, `defaultStripResolver.atY` returns null and the render briefly free-falls by deltaY. This shows up in the snap-probe browser verify as a 1-stage rectY=70.5 between rectY=51 (snap-to-b) and rectY=94 (snap-to-c) — the bar is correctly "in transit" through the gap. Surprising but consistent with the catalog (item 19); a future phase could collapse the gap by treating divider y as belonging to the strip above OR below.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 9)

- **Commit 1** (`fe64db2`) — `packages/gantt/src/interaction/swimlane-strip-at-y.ts` introduces `SwimlaneStripResolver` + `defaultStripResolver.atY(y, strips): string | null`. Linear-scan O(strips); chronix demos have ≤32 strips. Exported from `@chronixjs/gantt`'s top-level index. 7 vitest covering inside-strip, half-open boundary, inter-strip gap (rowSpacing > 0), above/below content, empty strips, and tile-packed (rowSpacing=0) strips. **Core 183 → 190**.
- **Commit 2** (`c560404`) — `useGanttPointer` gains optional `barRowIds?: MaybeRefOrGetter<ReadonlyMap<string, string>>` input + `projectedRowId: ComputedRef<string | null>` output. `BarDropPayload` extended with always-present `oldRowId` + `newRowId`. `commitDrag` resolves the pointer's `originPx.y + deltaY` to a target rowId; null result falls back to `oldRowId` so consumers see `newRowId === oldRowId` as the "revert" signal. The chronix adapter builds `barRowIds` from `props.bars` and threads it through. Demo's `onBarDrop` now writes `rowId: p.newRowId` and appends `[oldRow → newRow]` to the detail line on row changes. 3 vitest extensions. **vue3 124 → 127**.
- **Commit 3** (`8b02b39`) — `<ChronixGantt>` bar-drag render branch consults `pointer.projectedRowId` and `stripByRowId` (new computed Map). When projection differs from source row, renderY snaps to `targetStrip.y + intraStripOffset`. Same-row / null-projection path falls through to the pre-Phase-9 free-Y math. 3 SFC tests covering snap geometry, commit payload, and free-fall outside strips. **vue3 127 → 130. Chronix grand total 320/320.**

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 9)

- **Stale adapter `dist/` masked the demo wiring during browser verify.** First probe showed `bar-1: 01:00–05:00 → 02:00–06:00` with no row bracket and bar-1 vanished from DOM post-drop. Root cause: example app imports `@chronixjs/gantt-vue3` via its built `main: ./dist/index.cjs` — vite resolves that to the dist, not the workspace source. My Commit 2 source changes weren't in the dist yet because the last `pnpm build` happened during the previous ci-check (before Commit 2 changes). Rebuilding the adapter with `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt-vue3 build` made the wiring visible. Memory `feedback_vrt_screenshots.md` was already touching this pattern but for vite restart, not for adapter-dist rebuild. The same gotcha applies any time a chronix-package consumer needs to see a chronix-package source change.
- **ESLint `prefer-optional-chain` doesn't accept the `cond ? value : undefined` ternary even when `cond` and `value` are different expressions.** Fix: pass the optional ref directly through `toValue` and chain on the result — `const map = toValue(input.barRowIds); const x = map?.get(...) ?? '';`. Same place that ESLint also complained about a `txn === null || txn.kind !== 'bar-drag'` guard (suggested `txn?.kind !== 'bar-drag'`).

### Naming justifications (Phase 9)

- **`defaultStripResolver`** + **`SwimlaneStripResolver`** (vs `defaultStripLookup` or `defaultRowResolver`): consistent with `defaultPointerHitTester` / `defaultPointerCaptureSession` / `defaultLinkRouter` naming. The "Resolver" suffix matches the implementation's purpose (resolve a y to a rowId) rather than implementation strategy (linear scan). "Strip" because that's chronix's term for the rendered row band (matches `SwimlaneStrip`); "Row" alone would conflict with `RowSpec` which is the IR-side row identity.
- **`projectedRowId`** (vs `targetRowId` or `hoveredRowId`): "projected" matches the same naming as `ProgressHandleTransaction.projectedProgress` — both express "live projection given current pointer state". The composable doesn't claim the projection IS what'll be committed (the drop could land elsewhere); it just exposes the current resolution.
- **`barRowIds`** input (vs `rowIdByBarId` or `barToRow`): parallel to existing `barRanges` input; both are per-bar lookup maps from `barId` to a source-of-truth field. "Row ids" instead of "rows" disambiguates that the value is the id string, not a RowSpec.

### Open / parked (Phase 9)

- **Drag-validity hooks** (`eventAllow`, `resourceAllow`, per-bar editable / droppable, etc.) — parked. chronix's `BarSpec` / `RowSpec` have no per-entity gating fields; `<ChronixGantt editable={false}>` is the only knob today.
- **Overlap rejection** (drop would put two bars on same row at overlapping times → revert) — parked. chronix has no overlap policy; multi-bar stacking is purely visual via `BarStackHeightPass`.
- **Multi-resource events** (`resourceIds: string[]`) — parked. chronix `BarSpec.rowId: string` is single-valued by IR design.
- **`BarDragTransaction.projectedRowId` field** — parked / rejected. Catalog item 10 explains the layer separation rationale.
- **`bar-drop-cancelled` event** for reverted drops — parked. Consumers can detect via `newRowId === oldRowId && oldRange === newRange`.
- **`bar-drag-update` mid-drag event channel** — parked. Composable's `projectedRowId` ref is the extension point.
- **Cursor changes** (row-resize / not-allowed) — parked. No cursor-management layer yet.
- **Mirror element with reduced opacity** — parked. Direct-move is simpler and visually clear without a separate ghost.
- **Auto-scroll on edge-drag** — parked. No AutoScroller module.

## Phase 9 — DONE

- 4 commits total: `5349922` (design doc) + `fe64db2` (Commit 1: core resolver) + `c560404` (Commit 2: composable + payload + demo) + `8b02b39` (Commit 3: adapter snap-render). One new core file (`swimlane-strip-at-y.ts`); two modified core (`interaction/index.ts`, `index.ts`); two modified adapter (`use-gantt-pointer.ts`, `chronix-gantt.ts`); one modified demo (`App.vue`); 3 modified test files. **No VRT changes** — snap fires mid-drag; VRT captures static initial state.
- **190/190 core vitest** (was 183; +7 resolver). **130/130 vue3 adapter tests** (was 124; +6 between use-gantt-pointer +3 and chronix-gantt +3). **Total cumulative vitest 320.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified idempotent throughout.
- ci-check fully green. The most visible interaction parity gap left post-Phase 8 is closed — chronix demo at port 8702 now lets a user drop a bar on a different workshop's row and persists the row change.

## Phase 10 — Theme tokens (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 10)

- `packages/gantt/src/theme/GlobalThemeOverrides.ts` — ~25 partial-overridable tokens (`pageBgColor`, `eventBgColor`, `buttonHoverBgColor`, etc.). All distributed via CSS custom properties injected at the root, not via prop merging.
- `packages/gantt/src/theme/applyThemeOverrides.ts` (via imports) — runtime application path: iterate the partial map and set CSS variables on the gantt root element.
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1313-1586` — demo's `themeOverrides` object passed as a top-level scheduler option.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 10)

- **Flat namespace wins over nested groups for partial overrides.** Vue's prop-merging convention is `{...defaults, ...overrides}` — one level. Nested groups (`theme.header.cellFill`) would require either a custom recursive merge helper or noisy `:theme="{ ...defaults, header: { ...defaults.header, cellFill: 'red' } }"` consumer syntax. Flat with semantic-prefix names (`headerCellFill`) keeps both the type and the consumer call site clean.
- **TS-side merging is a superset of CSS-vars for chronix's purposes.** k-ui's CSS-var approach has the advantage of DevTools-tweakable values without re-running JS. The disadvantages: cross-framework chronix adapters (Vue3, React, Vue2 planned) would need parallel CSS distribution code, and TS-side merging is trivially type-safe whereas CSS-vars-as-strings lose type info at the boundary. Chronix's prop-merging cost is one re-render per theme change; CSS-vars save that round-trip but at the cost of a CSS-in-JS layer chronix has so far avoided.
- **Default theme values must be byte-equal to the prior inline literals** for the "zero-impact migration" promise to hold. Verified end-to-end by `chronix-verify` showing all 5 VRT baselines pass after the Commit 2 callsite swaps. If a single token's default had drifted by one hex digit, one of the 5 PNGs would have flagged it.
- **Bar fills stay CSS-managed.** Bars are styled by `.cx-gantt-bar { fill: ...; stroke: ... }` in consumer stylesheets. Pulling them into the theme would have forced a choice between (a) hard-coding the bar fill inline (and breaking existing consumer CSS) or (b) reading the CSS var into the theme (and reintroducing the CSS layer chronix didn't have). Catalog item 9 parks the choice for a future "bar styling API" phase.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 10)

- **Commit 1** (`2340b96`) — `packages/gantt/src/api/chronix-theme.ts` introduces a flat `ChronixTheme` interface with 29 fields: 18 colors + 5 typography (font sizes + weights) + 2 stroke widths + 2 opacity/strokeWidth numeric tokens that round out the count. `defaultChronixTheme` constant mirrors every prior inline literal byte-for-byte. Exported from `@chronixjs/gantt`. +2 vitest covering the token-shape parity (expected-key list) and per-key primitive type. **Core 190 → 192**.
- **Commit 2** (`3b660c0`) — `<ChronixGantt>` gains a `theme: Partial<ChronixTheme>` prop (default `{}`) and a `theme = computed(() => ({ ...defaultChronixTheme, ...props.theme }))` setup-time merge. Removed Phase 8's `defaultLinkColor` prop and the `LINK_STROKE_WIDTH` constant — both subsumed by `theme.linkDefaultColor` + `theme.linkStrokeWidth`. The render function swaps 31 callsites from inline literals to `t.<token>` reads spanning header band / progress overlay / sidebar chrome / body SVG background / link defaults. +6 SFC tests covering default rendering + 5 distinct partial-override probes. 1 Phase 8 link-rendering test rewritten to use `theme.linkDefaultColor`. **vue3 130 → 136. Chronix total 320 → 328.**

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 10)

- **No actual gotchas this phase.** The 31 callsite swaps were mechanical; the test fixture used to verify the merge merely passed `:theme="{ headerCellFill: '#fef3c7' }"` and probed the rendered SVG attribute. The notable absence of incident relative to Phase 8 / 9 reflects that this is a pure refactor with new type indirection on top — no new geometry, no new pointer logic, no new lifecycle. The 5 VRT baselines re-verified clean on first run.

### Naming justifications (Phase 10)

- **`ChronixTheme`** (vs `GanttTheme` or `Theme`): "Chronix" because the theme is consumed by `<ChronixGantt>` and a future `<ChronixTable>` / `<ChronixInput>` may share the same conceptual surface. "Gantt" would over-narrow.
- **`defaultChronixTheme`** (vs `chronixThemeDefaults` or `defaultTheme`): matches the existing `defaultLinkRouter` / `defaultPointerCaptureSession` / `defaultStripResolver` pattern of "default" prefix. The `Chronix` suffix avoids ambiguity in mixed-package consumer code.
- **Flat semantic-prefix tokens** (`headerCellFill`, `sidebarBackground`, etc.) — prefix groups by visual section, suffix names the role. Same convention as Tailwind's `headerBg` / `headerBorder` and naive-ui's flat `headerColor` / `headerBorderColor`. Avoids nesting overhead in `Partial<>`.

### Open / parked (Phase 10)

- **Border-radius tokens** — chronix has no `rx` / `ry` anywhere; parked.
- **Spacing / padding tokens** — `padding: 0 8px` is inline; parked.
- **Animation / transition tokens** — chronix has no animations; parked.
- **Shadow tokens** — flat-design choice; rejected.
- **Bar fill / stroke in theme** — stays CSS-managed; parked.
- **Theme demo toggle** (default vs alt-contrast) — parked.
- **`darkChronixTheme` preset** — parked; consumers can build via spread.
- **CSS custom properties layer** — rejected for cross-framework portability.
- **Vue3 provide/inject distribution** — rejected for cross-framework portability.

## Phase 10 — DONE

- 3 commits total: `49645aa` (design doc) + `2340b96` (Commit 1: interface + defaults) + `3b660c0` (Commit 2: adapter consumes theme + tests). Two new core files (`api/chronix-theme.ts`, `api/chronix-theme.test.ts`); two modified core (`api/index.ts`, `index.ts`); two modified adapter (`chronix-gantt.ts` — 31 callsite swaps + new `theme` prop + setup merge — and `chronix-gantt.test.ts` with +6 SFC tests); one modified Phase 8 test (`link-rendering.test.ts` — 1 test rewritten).
- **192/192 core vitest** (was 190; +2 theme tests). **136/136 vue3 adapter tests** (was 130; +6 theme SFC tests). **Total cumulative vitest 328.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified idempotent under default theme — defaults are byte-for-byte pixel-identical to pre-Phase 10 rendering.
- ci-check fully green. Adopters can now recolor the entire chronix chrome with a single `:theme="{ ... }"` prop — header band, progress overlay, sidebar borders, link defaults, typography sizes and weights all parameterized.

## Phase 11 — Slot registry (custom bar renderers) (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 11)

- `packages/gantt/src/options.ts` — k-ui's `eventContent` typing (callback OR Vue slot). Returns `VNode | VNode[] | { html: string } | { domNodes: Node[] }` depending on output style.
- `packages/gantt/src/event-rendering/EventRenderingContext.ts` — the `arg` bag passed to `eventContent` (event, timeText, isDraggable, view).
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1439-1746, 2207-2212` — both forms in the demo: `eventContent: renderEventContent` callback + `<template v-slot:eventContent="arg">` Vue slot.
- `packages/gantt/src/event-rendering/eventStyleCallbacks.ts` (via imports) — per-event style overrides: `eventTextColor`, `eventBackgroundColor`, `eventBorderColor`. Distinct from content replacement.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 11)

- **Two distinct surfaces in k-ui: content replacement vs style overrides.** `eventContent` replaces the bar's inner DOM with consumer VNodes. `eventStyleCallbacks` overrides specific style properties (text color, bg color, border color) per event via lookup callbacks. Phase 11 addresses the content side; the style side is already covered by CSS class selectors + per-bar attributes (consumers can write `.cx-gantt-bar[data-bar-id="urgent"] { fill: red }`).
- **Chronix bars are SVG `<rect>` leaf elements**, not HTML divs. Replacing the inner DOM doesn't apply — there IS no inner DOM. A custom bar renderer instead replaces the **entire** bar render: emit whatever VNode tree the consumer chooses (`<rect>`, `<g>`, `<path>`, multi-element compositions). The slot ctx provides the geometry + theme so the consumer can drop them into their own `<rect>` or compose around them.
- **Registry-based dispatch activates the dormant IR types.** Phase 1 designed `SlotContext / SlotTemplate / SlotRegistry / SlotRenderer` for exactly this pattern. Phase 11's API uses `createSlotRegistry()` + `slotRegistry?: SlotRegistry` prop, so the IR types finally have a real consumer. Alternative `barRenderer?: (ctx) => VNode` prop was considered and rejected — it doesn't scale to multi-slot APIs the way a registry does (future phases can register `'progress-overlay'`, `'tick-label'`, `'header-cell'` slots into the same registry).
- **Slot args carry live render geometry, not raw placedBar.** Mid-drag the bar's effective `renderX/Y/W/H` differs from `placedBar.x/y/width/height` because of `deltaX/deltaY` shifts and the Phase 9 cross-row snap math. Passing both lets a consumer decide: bind to the live values for "follow the drag" behavior, or bind to placedBar for "show the committed position even mid-drag".

### Chronix work derived (Phase 11)

- **Commit 1** (`5f51845`) — `packages/gantt/src/render/create-slot-registry.ts` introduces `createSlotRegistry(): SlotRegistry` (Map-backed; register replaces, unregister no-throw, multi-slot independent). `packages/gantt/src/render/bar-slot.ts` introduces `BarSlotArgs` interface + `BAR_SLOT_NAME = 'bar'` constant. Exported from top-level `@chronixjs/gantt`. +7 vitest covering empty default, register/get round-trip, unregister flow, replace-not-stack, no-throw on unregister-nonexistent, multi-slot independence, opaque return type. **Core 192 → 199.**
- **Commit 2** (`bcc0309`) — `<ChronixGantt>` gains optional `slotRegistry?: SlotRegistry` prop (default `undefined`). Render fn's bar branch: when `props.slotRegistry?.get(BAR_SLOT_NAME)` returns a template, invoke with a `BarSlotArgs` ctx (placedBar + sourceBar + live renderX/Y/W/H + effective theme + activeTransaction); narrow the `unknown` return to `VNode | readonly VNode[]` at the boundary; spread into the bar's nodes array. When no template, fall through to the existing default `<rect class="cx-gantt-bar">`. Progress overlay + handle still render below regardless. +5 SFC tests covering default fallback, custom replaces default fully, ctx geometry propagation, ctx theme propagation, mid-life unregister falls back. **vue3 136 → 141. Chronix total 328 → 340.**

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 11)

- **`SlotContext.args` is `Readonly<Record<string, unknown>>` per IR contract** — a precise interface like `BarSlotArgs` doesn't structurally satisfy it (missing index signature). Fix: cast through `unknown` at the adapter boundary. The `BarSlotArgs` interface is the consumer's contract; the IR type stays generic for cross-slot reuse.
- **`vi.fn(() => sentinel)` typed as zero-arg loses `mock.calls[0]` element typing.** Lint flagged `mock.calls[0]![0]` as accessing a tuple of length 0. Fix: type the wrapper explicitly as `SlotTemplate` and route through `vi.mocked(wrapper)` to recover the parameter list.
- **`Array.isArray(custom)` doesn't narrow well when `custom` was cast to a union with `readonly`.** ESLint flagged `nodes.push(...custom)` as "unsafe spread of `any[]`". Fix: restructure to bind `raw = barTemplate(...)` as `unknown`, then explicitly cast either branch into a concrete `ReturnType<typeof h>[]` array before spreading.

### Naming justifications (Phase 11)

- **`createSlotRegistry`** (vs `defaultSlotRegistry` or `newSlotRegistry`): "create" because each call returns a fresh instance (no singleton; consumers own lifetime). The `default*` prefix is reserved for module-level constants like `defaultLinkRouter` / `defaultChronixTheme` that ARE singletons.
- **`BAR_SLOT_NAME = 'bar'`** constant export (vs hardcoded `'bar'` strings everywhere): future slot renames are a one-place change; consumers can also import it for type-safe registration calls.
- **`BarSlotArgs`** (vs `BarRenderCtx` or `BarSlotContext`): follows the `*SlotArgs` naming for `SlotContext.args` payloads. A future `HeaderCellSlotArgs`, `TickLabelSlotArgs`, etc. slot in.
- **`renderX/Y/Width/Height`** in args (vs `liveX/Y/Width/Height`): matches the local variable names already in the render fn (renderX, renderY, renderWidth) — when reading the adapter's code consumers know exactly which values they're getting.

### Open / parked (Phase 11)

- **Additional slot types** (`'progress-overlay'`, `'tick-label'`, `'header-cell'`, `'sidebar-cell'`) — parked. Catalog item 2; additive when needed.
- **Vue3 `<template v-slot:bar>` wrapper** — parked. Adapter is render-fn-based; a future Phase 11.x can add Vue-slot adapter when chronix grows an SFC entry point.
- **React-style render-props** — parked until React adapter lands.
- **Selection / hover state in args** — parked; no selection model yet (Phase 9 catalog rejected it).
- **View-id in args** — parked.
- **Reactive `register / unregister` API** — parked. Vue's reactivity already propagates registry changes via prop re-read.
- **Per-slot fallback chain** — YAGNI for v0.
- **Per-bar opt-in slot via `BarSpec.slot?: string`** — parked; v0 applies `'bar'` slot uniformly.
- **Per-slot theme tokens** — parked.
- **Demo wiring** — parked; defer the showcase to Phase 11.x.

## Phase 11 — DONE

- 3 commits total: `479b3b0` (design doc) + `5f51845` (Commit 1: core registry + types) + `bcc0309` (Commit 2: adapter consumes registry + tests). Three new core files (`render/create-slot-registry.ts`, `render/create-slot-registry.test.ts`, `render/bar-slot.ts`); two modified core (`render/index.ts`, `index.ts`); two modified adapter (`chronix-gantt.ts` + `chronix-gantt.test.ts` with +5 SFC tests).
- **199/199 core vitest** (was 192; +7 registry tests). **141/141 vue3 adapter tests** (was 136; +5 slot SFC tests). **Total cumulative vitest 340.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified idempotent — demo doesn't register a `'bar'` slot, so every bar falls through to the default `<rect>`. Pixel-identical to pre-Phase 11.
- ci-check fully green. The dormant Phase 1 IR types (`SlotContext / SlotTemplate / SlotRegistry / SlotRenderer`) finally have a real consumer in the adapter render fn. Adopters who want custom bar shapes — rounded corners, inline icons, status chevrons, multi-element compositions — register a `'bar'` template and ship it.

## Phase 12 — Selection model (`bar-click` + controlled selection) (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 12)

- `packages/gantt/src/interactions/EventClicking.ts:1-71` — `eventClick` handler. Uses `listenBySelector('click', '.gantt-event', ...)` (DOM click event, not pointer-up). Drag-vs-click discrimination via `wasDragged` data attribute on the seg element. Suppresses click when target hits `gantt-just-dragged` / `gantt-event-progress-handle` / `gantt-event-progress-drag-triangle` classes.
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/UnselectAuto.ts:1-72` — clicks outside any bar clear the selection via `dispatch({ type: 'UNSELECT_EVENT' })`. Configurable via `unselectAuto: boolean` + `unselectCancel: string` selector.
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1681-1685` — demo's `handleEventClick` just confirms + deletes the bar. Minimal usage example.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 12)

- **Pointerup vs DOM click event.** k-ui uses a separate `click` listener; chronix routes through the existing pointerup handler. Routing through pointerup means the drag-vs-click discrimination has one source of truth (the same handler that decides commit-vs-abort also decides emit-click-or-not), avoiding the k-ui-style data-attribute dance where the drag interaction marks an element and the click handler reads the mark later.
- **Zero-delta drag abort.** With `editable: true`, a plain click on a bar body would have started a `bar-drag` transaction at pointerdown. Phase 12's adapter detects 0-delta on the way out: `bar-drag` / `bar-resize` / `calendar-range-select` with no time/space change → abort instead of commit. This preserves the "click fires click, drag fires drop" intuition without polluting `onBarDrop` consumers with no-op events. Progress-handle transactions DON'T get the abort treatment — reaching the handle hit zone is itself the user's intent, so a 0-delta progress-handle pointerup still commits (with `resolvedProgress === initialProgress` — semantically a confirm-current).
- **lastHit preserved through commit, cleared by next begin.** Pre-Phase-12 `commit()` cleared `lastHitResult` (matching `abort()`'s discipline). Phase 12 needs lastHit AFTER commit so the click decision can read which bar was hit. Removed the clear from `commit()`; relied on `begin()`'s unconditional `lastHitResult.value = hit` to overwrite at the next pointerdown. `abort()` still clears (browser-initiated cancel discards everything by design).
- **Controlled selection over internal state.** chronix's pattern across editable / selectable / links / theme / slotRegistry is "consumer owns state, adapter is a function of props". A built-in selection ref would have created two sources of truth (the prop AND the internal Set). The `useGanttSelection()` composable provides ergonomic stateful wrapping without compromising the controlled-prop model.
- **`shiftKey` for multi-select.** macOS file managers use Cmd-click for toggle, Windows uses Ctrl-click. Web list UIs typically use Shift for range-select. None of these match perfectly. Phase 12 picks `shiftKey` for toggle because: (a) it's modifier-key consistent across OS, (b) range-select is parked anyway (catalog item 10), (c) future range-select could use shift+up/down arrows or shift+click-on-another-row pattern that doesn't conflict with toggle.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 12)

- **Commit 1** (`5025758`) — `adapters/vue3/src/use-gantt-selection.ts` ships `useGanttSelection(config?): UseGanttSelectionOutput` + 4 payload types (`BarClickPayload`, `EmptyAreaClickPayload`, `SelectionChangePayload`, `UseGanttSelectionConfig`). Set-backed for O(1) add/remove, replaced (not mutated in place) on each change for Vue reactivity. Drop-in handlers `handleBarClick` (replace on plain, toggle on shift) + `handleEmptyAreaClick` (clear if `unselectAuto`). Re-exported from adapter package index. +10 vitest covering empty default, select-add-no-dup, deselect-noop-safety, toggle, clear, handleBarClick plain (replace), handleBarClick shift (toggle), handleEmptyAreaClick unselectAuto on/off, reactivity. **vue3 141 → 151.**
- **Commit 2** (`5e644c2`) — `BarSlotArgs` (Phase 11 interface) additively gains `readonly isSelected: boolean` for custom slot renderers. `useGanttPointer` gains a `dragCommittedFlag: Ref<boolean>` set by `commit()` + reset by `begin()`, exposed as `wasDragCommit: ComputedRef<boolean>`. `commit()` no longer clears `lastHitResult` (so the post-commit click decision can read it; next `begin()` overwrites). `<ChronixGantt>` gains `selectedBarIds?: readonly string[]` prop (default `[]`), `'bar-click'` + `'empty-area-click'` emits, and a 0-delta-abort step in `onPointerup` that distinguishes click-like from real drag/resize. Default `<rect>` gets `.cx-gantt-bar--selected` class when selected. `BarSlotArgs.isSelected` propagated. Demo wires `useGanttSelection()` into `:selected-bar-ids` + `@bar-click` + `@empty-area-click` and writes `bar-click: <id> [single|+shift] → selection: ...` to the events panel. styles.css adds `.cx-gantt-bar--selected { stroke: #f59e0b; stroke-width: 3 }` for OOTB visual. +7 SFC tests (1 over plan — added the zero-delta-with-editable case after writing the 6 from the plan). **vue3 151 → 158. chronix-gantt.test.ts 91 → 98. Chronix total 340 → 358.**

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 12)

- **Stale dist masked `BarSlotArgs.isSelected` addition.** First adapter typecheck after adding the field errored "isSelected does not exist in type 'BarSlotArgs'". Same root cause as Phase 9's `barRowIds` gotcha: adapter imports types from `@chronixjs/gantt`'s built `dist/index.d.ts`, not source. Rebuilding core (`pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt build`) regenerated the .d.ts with the new field and the adapter typechecked clean. The `feedback_vrt_screenshots.md` memory captured this pattern for vite + adapter dist; it applies equally to typecheck dependencies on cross-package type changes.
- **Browser-verify probe missed bar-2's shift-click test** because bar-2 has 50% progress and its progress handle sits at the bar's center (the probe's chosen click coords). Progress-handle hits take priority over bar-body hits, so the click fired `bar-progress` instead of `bar-click`. **Not a bug** — that's the documented hit-test priority order from Phase 3.x. Probes should use bars without `progress`/`pointerOverlayId` for click tests; SFC tests use controlled coords without this concern.
- **`commit()` clearing `lastHitResult` was load-bearing for click discrimination.** Removing the clear was the right call (so post-commit click decisions can read the hit), but it took some thought to convince myself the next `begin()`'s unconditional overwrite makes this safe. Edge case considered: `pointerdown → begin (lastHit=X) → commit (lastHit retained=X) → another pointerdown without an explicit "release pointer capture" → begin (lastHit overwritten=Y)`. Safe.

### Naming justifications (Phase 12)

- **`useGanttSelection`** (vs `useSelection` or `useBarSelection`): matches existing `useGanttLayout` / `useGanttPointer` naming. The "Gantt" prefix grounds the composable in chronix's domain.
- **`bar-click` / `empty-area-click`** (vs `click` + discriminator field): two emits read more naturally in templates (`@bar-click="..."`) than a single `@click` that needs a target switch. Matches existing pattern of `@bar-drop` / `@bar-resize` / `@bar-progress` being distinct emits per bar transaction kind.
- **`wasDragCommit`** (vs `hadDrag` or `lastCommit`): "was" is past-tense (the commit already happened); "DragCommit" captures both kinds-of-thing (drag / resize / progress / select all commit through the same `commit()` path). "DragCommit" as one word matches the `commitBarDrag` / `commitBarResize` naming.
- **`selectedBarIds`** (vs `selection` or `selectedBars`): matches `barRanges` / `barRowIds` etc. — explicit about the value shape (array of ids, not a single id or an object).

### Open / parked (Phase 12)

- **Touch long-press selection** (`selectLongPressDelay`) — parked. Chronix doesn't differentiate touch vs mouse in the composable yet.
- **`bar-dblclick`** + **`bar-contextmenu`** — parked. Additive emit channels; common requests but not in demo.
- **Range-select** (shift-click between two bars) — parked. Bars aren't naturally ordered along a single axis.
- **Ctrl/Cmd-click toggle** — parked alongside range-select.
- **`unselectCancel: string` selector** — parked. Consumers can call `event.stopPropagation()` on their own DOM.
- **Theme tokens for selected state** (`theme.barSelectedStroke` etc.) — parked. CSS class hook handles 90%.
- **selectMirror during drag** — parked. Phase 9's snap render covers drag preview.
- **Keyboard navigation** (arrow keys) — parked. Needs bar-ordering semantics.
- **`v-model:selectedBarIds` macro** — parked. Manual `:selected-bar-ids` + `@selection-change` wiring works today.
- **shiftKey/ctrlKey on payload** — parked. Consumers read `jsEvent.shiftKey` directly.
- **Distance-threshold drag detection** — parked. Strict zero-delta-abort is simpler.
- **In-adapter stateful selection** — rejected (controlled is single-source-of-truth).
- **Separate DOM `click` listener** — rejected (use existing pointer lifecycle).

## Phase 12 — DONE

- 3 commits total: `320f6b4` (design doc) + `5025758` (Commit 1: useGanttSelection composable + types + 10 tests) + `5e644c2` (Commit 2: adapter click/selection wire-up + 7 SFC tests + demo wiring). Two new adapter files (`use-gantt-selection.ts` + `use-gantt-selection.test.ts`); 6 modified files (`packages/gantt/src/render/bar-slot.ts`, `adapters/vue3/src/{chronix-gantt,chronix-gantt.test,use-gantt-pointer,index}.ts`, `examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue`, `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css`).
- **199/199 core vitest** unchanged. **158/158 vue3 adapter tests** (was 141; +10 selection composable + +7 selection SFC tests). **Total cumulative vitest 358.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified idempotent — demo doesn't auto-select on load, so default `selectedBarIds: []` keeps the .cx-gantt-bar--selected class off every rect. Pixel-identical to pre-Phase 12.
- ci-check fully green. The most universally-requested gantt feature ("which bar did the user click") finally has a public API. Selection state composes with Phase 11's slot renderers (custom bars receive `isSelected` in args) and with Phase 10's theme (no new tokens needed; CSS class hook handles styling).

keyboard nav layer (arrow keys / Delete emit / Esc / role=grid +
aria-activedescendant) that doesn't exist in the reference. All catalog

## Phase 14 — Resizable sidebar (single area divider) (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 14)

- `packages/gantt/src/resource-timeline/ResourceTimelineLayout.tsx:5, 26, 61, 65, 74, 126-138, 199-204, 304-342` — the reference's single divider between resource panel and timeline. Width-override state (`null` until user drags), MIN/MAX clamp at 30 / `viewWidth - 30`. No emit on commit; override stays in component state.
- `packages/gantt/src/resource-timeline/resourceTableLayout.ts:1-60, 120-153` — for context on how the reference distributes the area's total width across columns automatically. Chronix's `ColumnSpec.width` is explicit, so the proportional-scaling decision is chronix-specific.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 14)

- **Single divider, not per-column.** The reference doesn't have a per-column divider anywhere. Per-column dividers would multiply state (one override per column) and add UX complexity (which column does "the" boundary belong to). The area-only model is cleaner and matches the reference exactly.
- **Override state, not prop.** Putting the override in component state matches the reference's behavior — prop-driven width is the INITIAL, drag-driven width is the live. A prop would either become controlled (consumer has to wire `:sidebar-width-override + @sidebar-resize`) or fight the drag handler. Keeping it internal stays out of the consumer's way; if a consumer later needs persistence, that's a follow-up phase with a small additive surface.
- **Proportional scaling preserves col ratios.** Chronix's `ColumnSpec.width` carries user intent ("region is 60, base is 100, name is 80 → 3:5:4 ratio"). Scaling each by the same multiplier (`effective / sumOfBase`) preserves the ratio at every override width. "Last-column-absorbs-delta" (the alternative) would have made the rightmost column variable-width and the others permanent-width, which breaks the ratio intent.
- **`<colgroup>` reuse is a Vue patching footgun.** A single `colGroup` VNode embedded in two parent trees triggers Vue's "same vnode reference" short-circuit on patch — only one of the two DOM locations receives prop updates after a state change. The bug was latent pre-Phase 14 because the col widths never changed reactively (they were fixed at `ColumnSpec.width`). The proportional-scaling test exposed it. Fix: replace `const colGroup = h(...)` with `const buildColGroup = () => h(...)` called once per use site.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 14)

- **Commit 1** (`a8b7688`) — `chronix-gantt.ts` adds: module-level `MIN_SIDEBAR_AREA_WIDTH = 40` + `SIDEBAR_DIVIDER_WIDTH = 8` constants; setup() refs (`wrapperRef`, `dividerRef`, `sidebarWidthOverride`, `dividerDragStartWidth`, `dividerDragStartClientX`); computeds (`sidebarBaseWidth`, `effectiveSidebarWidth`, `sidebarScale`); four pointer handlers (`onDividerPointerdown / move / up / cancel`); render-fn changes (3-column grid with explicit `gridColumn`/`gridRow` placement on all 4 panes, divider element with sticky-left positioning + col-resize cursor + pointer handlers, `<col>` widths multiplied by `sidebarScale`, `buildColGroup()` factory replaces the reused vnode). `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css` adds `.cx-gantt-sidebar-divider::after` 1px line + `:hover` 2px state. +6 SFC tests in a Phase 14 `describe` block; 1 existing test updated (`'200px auto'` → `'200px 8px auto'`). **vue3 158 → 164. Chronix total 358 → 364.**
- **Commit 2** (`faae9b0`) — VRT rebaseline. All 5 chronix screenshots widen by exactly 8px (`23965px by 217px` → `23973px by 217px`); no other diff. Confirms the divider track is the ONLY geometric change.

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 14)

- **Reused-VNode patch short-circuit.** Initial implementation had `const colGroup = h('colgroup', ...)` and embedded `colGroup` in both the header and body tables. Initial render looked correct (both tables drew their cols). The proportional-scaling test (drag → expected col widths to scale) caught the bug: only one table's cols updated. Root cause: Vue's patch step detects identical vnode references and skips the second patch, leaving one of the DOM locations stale. Solution: a `buildColGroup()` factory called per use site produces distinct vnodes. Lesson: when sharing computed DOM via vnodes across multiple slots, always materialize via a factory call — never reuse the same vnode reference.
- **`gridColumn`/`gridRow` auto-placement breaks with the new middle column.** Adding the divider as a grid track in column 2 meant the existing 4 panes' default auto-placement (which fills column 1 then column 2 then column 3 row-by-row) put headerSvg into column 2 instead of 3. Fix: stamp explicit `gridColumn` + `gridRow` on each pane's inline style. Did it only when `hasSidebar` is true so the no-sidebar branch's block layout stays unchanged.
- **Banned-identifier scan flagged `ResourceTimelineLayout` in a code comment.** Rewrote the comment to describe the pattern without naming the upstream class. Per `feedback_no_external_repo_refs_in_chronix`: chronix code/tests/comments must read standalone; the audit/journal/\* files are the only place external identifiers are allowed.
- **Lint cleanups** (mechanical): `as DOMRect` casts on `vi.spyOn(...).mockReturnValue(...)` are unnecessary; nullish-coalescing rule prefers `??` over `!== null ?` ternary; import-x ordering wants the inline-type import and the dedicated `import type` to be in the same group (no blank line between).

### Naming justifications (Phase 14)

- **`sidebarWidthOverride`** (vs `resourceAreaWidthOverride` from the reference, or `userSidebarWidth`): chronix calls it the "sidebar" everywhere else (cf. Phase 5: `.cx-gantt-sidebar-header / -body`), and "override" matches the semantics — overrides the natural prop-derived width.
- **`effectiveSidebarWidth`** (vs `sidebarWidth` directly): "effective" signals "the value to actually use after applying override", parallel to `effectiveTransaction` patterns elsewhere in the adapter.
- **`SIDEBAR_DIVIDER_WIDTH`** (vs `DIVIDER_WIDTH` or `RESIZE_HANDLE_WIDTH`): the prefix scopes the constant — chronix has multiple kinds of dividers (the header axis-divider, the column borders) and a global `DIVIDER_WIDTH` would be ambiguous.
- **`buildColGroup`** (vs `renderColGroup` or `colGroupFactory`): "build" matches Vue's docs convention for vnode-producing helpers; "render" usually implies a component-level render fn; "factory" is OO-flavored and feels heavier than this 5-line helper needs.

### Open / parked (Phase 14)

- **Per-column resize** (drag the border between two columns to resize one independently) — parked. Not in the reference; ratio scaling covers the common case.
- **RTL support** (`isRtl` sign flip on the drag delta) — parked. Chronix doesn't wire RTL through any other interaction; adding it just for the divider would drift the codebase asymmetrically. When chronix takes a general RTL pass, the divider will join.
- **`sidebar-resize` emit / callback** when drag commits — parked. Useful for persistence but the consumer can also bind to the divider's pointerup directly if they need it. Wait for explicit demand.
- **Persisted override** (localStorage / per-user cookie) — parked. Squarely a consumer concern; with no emit there's nothing to persist anyway.
- **`dblclick` to reset the override** — parked. The reference doesn't have this either; consumers who want it can call `selection.clear()`-style on a refresh button.
- **`sidebarWidthOverride` as a prop** (controlled mode) — parked. Adding a prop would force consumers who don't want to manage the state to wire a `v-model` style noop. The internal-state default keeps the common case zero-config; a `v-model:sidebar-width` could land additively in a follow-up.
- **Touch long-press indicators** (visible "grab" affordance on touch devices before drag begins) — parked. Pointer Events handle touch transparently; the cursor change is mouse-only by nature.
