- **199/199 core vitest** unchanged. **164/164 vue3 adapter tests** (was 158; +6 sidebar resize divider SFC tests in the Phase 14 describe block, 1 existing test updated for the new 3-column grid template). **Total cumulative vitest 364.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines rebaselined: `Expected 23965px by 217px, received 23973px by 217px` on every view (day / month / season / half-year / year). +8px is exactly the divider track width; no other pixel change.
- ci-check fully green. Sidebar UX is now interactive without any new prop / emit surface (k-ui-style parity). The latent reused-vnode `<colgroup>` bug is fixed as a side effect — any future state-change reactivity on the colgroup widths (e.g. animated column collapse) will work correctly by default.

## Phase 16 — Drag / resize lifecycle emits (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 16)

- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventDragging.ts:140-159` — `eventDragStart` fires inside `handleDragStart` ONLY when `this.isDragging` is `true`. The `isDragging` flag is set by a separate pointer-distance threshold — pure clicks (pointerdown + pointerup with no movement) never set it, so neither start nor stop fires for them. Payload shape `{ el, event, jsEvent, view }` with the originating PointerEvent as `jsEvent`.
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventDragging.ts:440-456` — `eventDragStop` fires inside `handleDragEnd` at line 450, BEFORE the mutation-application / drop-emission logic that starts at line 457. Stop fires regardless of whether the mutation is valid; the reference's comment notes "Last valid hit is same as initial - don't apply any move" but still calls trigger('eventDragStop') unconditionally.
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventDragging.ts:161-164` — `handleDragMove` has a one-line body with the comment "Note: We don't reset mirror during drag move to allow smooth visual feedback". No emitter trigger. **Confirms: reference has no continuous "drag move" emit.**
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventResizing.ts:115-132` — `eventResizeStart` mirrors the drag pattern at line 126. Same payload shape (no `edge` field — the reference uses one event for both edges + a CSS class check `.gantt-event-resizer-start` to distinguish).
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventResizing.ts:224-249` — `eventResizeStop` mirrors at line 244, also before the commit at line 251.
- `packages/gantt/src/interaction/interactions/EventResizing.ts:134-222` — `handleHitUpdate` updates the in-place resize preview state via `SET_EVENT_RESIZE` dispatches but does not trigger any emitter event. Confirms: reference has no continuous "resize move" emit either.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 16)

- **The reference's `isDragging` gate is what makes "click vs drag" clean.** Without it, every pointerdown on a draggable element would fire `eventDragStart` even if the user immediately released without moving. With it, a click-without-movement fires neither start nor stop. Chronix's mirror: a `dragStartFired: Ref<boolean>` latch in `useGanttPointer`, reset in `begin()`, set to true on the first `advance()` with non-zero delta. Stop callbacks check the latch before firing.
- **Lazy-start solves chronix's "begin immediately" architecture.** Chronix's pointer composable starts a transaction at pointerdown (not after a distance threshold) because the transaction layer is pure-functional and needs an anchor immediately. Firing start eagerly at `begin()` would emit dragstart even on aborted 0-delta clicks, which would break consumers tracking "is something being dragged right now". Lazy-start sidesteps the gate-vs-state-machine mismatch by deferring the emit until the first non-zero advance.
- **`commit()` order: stop → commit-callback.** Reference's `handleDragEnd` line 450 (eventDragStop) precedes line 457 (mutation merge + eventDrop). Chronix mirrors: in `commit()`, fire stop BEFORE the kind-specific commit branch. This lets consumers reset "drag in progress" UI state before the mutation arrives — important when the mutation handler does something expensive (e.g. server save) and you want the spinner to fall away promptly.
- **`abort()` fires stop too.** Reference fires `eventDragStop` regardless of whether the mutation was valid; the only difference is whether `eventDrop` follows. Chronix's abort path (pointercancel + 0-delta-after-non-zero-advance edge case) needs to fire stop symmetrically so consumer drag-state resets cleanly. Gated by the same `dragStartFired` latch — an aborted transaction that never advanced doesn't fire a stop with no matching start.
- **Adapter is the right place to enrich the payload.** The composable callbacks carry just `{ barId }` (+ `edge`) because `useGanttPointer` is event-source-agnostic and doesn't take `bars` as input. The adapter has `props.bars` and the in-flight PointerEvent, so attaching `sourceBar` + `jsEvent` at the emit site is a one-line `find` + ref read — keeps the composable narrow and matches the existing `bar-click` enrichment pattern from Phase 12.
- **Refresh `lastJsEvent` at pointerup AND pointercancel.** The composable's `commit()` / `abort()` fire stop callbacks synchronously from the pointerup / pointercancel handlers. If `lastJsEvent` were last set at pointermove time, the stop emit would reference the wrong event (the move event, not the up/cancel event). Refreshing at pointerup / pointercancel makes the stop payload reference the event that actually ended the gesture.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 16)

- **Commit 1** (`6594f70`) — `adapters/vue3/src/use-gantt-pointer.ts` gains 4 callback types (`BarDragStartCallback / BarDragStopCallback / BarResizeStartCallback / BarResizeStopCallback`), 4 optional callback inputs (`onBarDragStart` etc.), `dragStartFired: Ref<boolean>` latch reset in `begin()`. `advance()` checks the latch + non-zero delta to lazy-fire start; `commit()` fires stop before the commit branch; `abort()` fires stop if the latch tripped. +6 vitest in a Phase 16 describe block covering: 0-delta drag (no fires), non-zero drag (start once → stop → drop order via `invocationCallOrder`), multi-advance (start fires EXACTLY ONCE), abort after non-zero (start + stop, no drop), 0-delta resize (no fires), non-zero resize (edge field propagation). **vue3 164 → 170.**
- **Commit 2** (`30d16cd`) — `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts` gains 4 public payload types (`BarDragStartPayload / BarDragStopPayload / BarResizeStartPayload / BarResizeStopPayload` — all carry `barId + sourceBar + jsEvent`, resize variants add `edge`). Setup gains `lastJsEvent: Ref<PointerEvent | null>` + `buildDragPayload(barId)` helper. `useGanttPointer({...})` call extended with 4 callback handlers that enrich the narrow composable payload into the public shape. New emits declared: `'bar-dragstart' / 'bar-dragstop' / 'bar-resizestart' / 'bar-resizestop'`. `onPointerdown / onPointermove / onPointerup / onPointercancel` refresh `lastJsEvent` so each lifecycle stage references its own event. Demo `App.vue` adds 4 handlers + 4 template bindings; events panel kind enum extended. `adapters/vue3/src/index.ts` re-exports the new public + callback payload types. +4 SFC tests covering: drag bar body (start on first non-zero move + stop on up + drop after stop + jsEvent.type='pointermove' on start, 'pointerup' on stop), 0-delta click (no dragstart/stop + bar-click still fires), drag end-edge (resizestart with edge='end' + resizestop + resize after stop), pointercancel mid-drag (start + stop, no drop). **vue3 170 → 174. Chronix total 364 → 374.** VRT baselines re-verified clean post-Commit 2 (5/5 idempotent — emits are runtime-only, no DOM change).

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 16)

- **Accidental duplicated `import type { ... } from '@chronixjs/gantt'`** at Commit 2 — when adding new payload type definitions I copied an import block from the file's top into the middle, producing duplicate identifiers. Caught by TS hint diagnostics (line ranges 14-23 + 66-75). Resolved by deleting the duplicate. Lesson: when adding type declarations that depend on types already imported, just add the declarations — don't re-import.
- **`lastJsEvent` refresh discipline.** First draft only refreshed `lastJsEvent` in `onPointerdown` / `onPointermove`. The `'bar-dragstop'` emit would have referenced the last pointermove event rather than the pointerup that actually ended the drag. Fix: refresh in `onPointerup` + `onPointercancel` too, BEFORE calling `pointer.commit() / abort()`. Caught by writing the SFC test that asserts `jsEvent.type === 'pointerup'` on the stop payload — TDD-style discovery.

### Naming justifications (Phase 16)

- **`bar-dragstart` / `bar-dragstop`** (hyphen, lowercase) vs the reference's `eventDragStart` / `eventDragStop` (camelCase) — chronix's emit naming convention uses Vue3's standard hyphen-lowercase pattern (`@bar-drop`, `@bar-click`, `@empty-area-click`). "stop" matches the reference rather than "end" because "end" might confuse with the resize's `edge: 'end'` semantics.
- **`BarDragStartCallback` (composable) vs `BarDragStartPayload` (adapter)** — same-name suffix collisions are avoidable by splitting by layer: callback shapes (narrow, content-space) carry `Callback`; emit payloads (wide, DOM-aware) carry `Payload`. Both are exported from the adapter package index so consumers can pick the right one for their integration depth.
- **`buildDragPayload` (helper fn)** vs `enrichBarId` or `lookupSourceBar` — "build" matches existing helper-fn naming for vnode / payload factories. The narrower "lookupSourceBar" would have implied a single-purpose accessor, but the function does both lookup AND null-defensive shape construction.
- **`dragStartFired` (latch)** vs `hasDragStarted` or `dragLifecycleActive` — "fired" is past-tense (the event already happened); "started" is ambiguous (could mean the transaction started, which is unrelated). The latch encodes specifically "have we already emitted start", and "fired" reads that intent.

### Open / parked (Phase 16)

- **Continuous "drag move" / "resize move" emits** — parked. Reference has none; chronix consumers can subscribe to `pointer.activeTransaction.value` (a `ComputedRef`) for live mid-drag state if needed. Adding a per-pointermove emit would invert the cost model (1000s of emits per drag vs 2-3 lifecycle events).
- **Cross-context `drop` emit** (external draggable dropped into the timeline) — parked. Chronix doesn't model external drag sources; the reference's `drop` event is specifically for that handoff. Will revisit if a consumer needs external HTML5 drag-and-drop integration.
- **Start/stop emits for `progress-handle` and `calendar-range-select` transactions** — parked. The reference has no parallel start/stop pair for either; calendar's `select` already fires once on commit, and the progress-handle UI lives inside `EventDragging` in the reference rather than as a separate transaction kind.
- **`el` (subject DOM element) and `view` fields in payloads** — parked. Chronix's cross-framework portability rules out passing framework-specific DOM/View references through the public payload. Consumers locate the DOM via `barId` + their own queries.
- **`didCommit: boolean` flag on stop payload** — parked. Strict parity with the reference (no equivalent field). Consumers infer commit-vs-abort from whether `'bar-drop'` / `'bar-resize'` fires after `'bar-dragstop'` / `'bar-resizestop'` for the same `barId`. Additive in a follow-up if it bites.
- **Distance-threshold drag-confirm gate** — parked. The reference uses a small pixel threshold (e.g. 3px) before promoting a gesture from "potential click" to "confirmed drag", which feels slightly more forgiving than chronix's strict "first non-zero delta" rule. Chronix consumers who want this can wrap `onBarDragStart` with their own threshold logic. v0 keeps the strict 0-vs-non-zero rule.

## Phase 16 — DONE

- 3 commits total: `e53e6fa` (design doc) + `6594f70` (Commit 1: composable lifecycle callbacks + 6 vitest) + `30d16cd` (Commit 2: adapter wire-up + 4 SFC tests + demo + index re-exports).
- **199/199 core vitest** unchanged. **174/174 vue3 adapter tests** (was 164; +6 composable lifecycle + +4 SFC). **Total cumulative vitest 374.** 27 parity assertions unchanged.
- 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified idempotent — emits are runtime-only, no DOM change. Pixel-identical to pre-Phase 16.
- ci-check fully green. The lifecycle surface (`bar-dragstart / -stop / -resizestart / -resizestop`) closes the largest reference-emit-parity gap. Lazy-fire-on-first-non-zero-delta cleanly threads chronix's "begin immediately" transaction architecture through the reference's "isDragging gate" semantics; the `lastJsEvent` ref enrichment keeps the composable narrow while making the public emits carry the right framework-aware fields.

## Phase 17 — Side-by-side parity infrastructure (2026-05-15)

### Reference reading (Phase 17)

- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:23-410` — k-ui demo's `RESOURCES[]` (32 entries). Chronix v0 parity mode mirrors only the 32 `id` strings ('32', '25', '16', ..., '12') — `airportName / baseName / workshopName` metadata is parked.
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:691-1271` — k-ui demo's `generateTestEvents()` (25 events). Chronix parity mode's bar dataset comes from the same time-anchor / id-naming as this function; the existing `parity.spec.ts:441-489` already replicated it inline. Extracted to `tooling/golden-runner/src/parity-events.ts` as a shared module so both demo and tests draw from the same source.
- `examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1273-1290` — k-ui's `resourceAreaColumns` (`airportName / baseName / workshopName`). Chronix demo's existing 3 columns (`region / base / name`) serve the same purpose; column-content parity is parked.
- `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts:441-489` — `buildTestEvents(todayMs)` previously inline; now moved to the shared module as `buildParityEvents`.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 17)

- **The "input alignment" gap is non-obvious until you try cross-demo parity.** PARITY_RECHECK.md (2026-05-15) pointed at parity.spec.ts as the assertion home, and the 4 discipline layers (memory / template / skill / hook) ALL pointed there. But the existing parity.spec.ts pattern is "chronix function in-process vs k-ui DOM" — works for pure-core algorithms. For adapter / render / interaction phases, the algorithm lives in the Vue adapter and only manifests in the rendered DOM. The only honest test is "drive both demos with same inputs, compare both rendered DOMs". Until Phase 17, this was impossible because the two demos shipped different sample data (`bar-N` on `workshop-N` rows vs `event-N` on numeric-string rows). Two demos with different inputs produce different outputs — you can't tell algorithm drift from data divergence.
- **Coordinate frame matters for cross-demo bar X parity.** First attempt measured bar bbox relative to chart-root (`.demo-app-main` for k-ui, `div.cx-gantt-wrapper` for chronix). Both include the sidebar but the sidebars differ in width — k-ui's resource panel is ~288px at viewport 1440 (20% width), chronix's 3-column sidebar is 240px. Measuring bar.left − chartRect.left baked the sidebar-width delta into X, producing ~7px-class mismatches that LOOKED like algorithm drift. Fix: measure relative to TIMELINE-BODY content space — k-ui's `.gantt-timeline-body-wrapper`, chronix's `svg.cx-gantt-body`. The axis x=0 anchor is the body's left edge in both. After fix: 13 paired bars match within 1px.
- **K-ui filters bars to the visible day-view range, chronix renders all bars at off-axis x.** Cross-demo bar diff finds 12 bars "only in chronix" — chronix renders `event-1` at x≈-3539 (clipped off-axis), k-ui omits it from the DOM entirely because its hit-test / virtualization model skips off-range bars. Documented as v0 acceptable: `mismatches.length === 0` is the hard assertion; `onlyInKui` / `onlyInChronix` are warnings. A future phase could equalize the virtualization behavior, but it's not algorithm drift — it's a render-strategy difference both demos consistently apply to their own data.
- **`?parity=true` URL toggle is the right surface.** Alternatives considered: env-var build flag (Vite `import.meta.env.VITE_PARITY`), separate demo entry (`/parity.html`), forked demo app. URL query wins because: (1) no build-time switching, (2) easy to flip in a browser tab while iterating, (3) chronix's banner conditionally renders only when active so default-load is byte-for-byte unchanged (verified — VRT baselines all idempotent post-Phase 17).
- **The /phase-close discipline catches gaps even before the skill is registered.** Walked the 6-step gate manually for Phase 17 (skill was created in this same session so the harness doesn't see it yet). Each check produced an explicit ✅ / ❌ verdict before the status flip — that's the value of the gate, independent of whether the skill machinery is hot. Once the skill is registered next session, invoking it will run the same checks faster and more reliably.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 17)

- **Commit 1** (`6c1fef9`) — `tooling/golden-runner/src/parity-events.ts` exports `PARITY_RESOURCE_IDS` (32-id array, k-ui RESOURCES order) + `buildParityEvents(todayMs)` (25 events with `event-N` ids + start/end epoch math + progress values for event-1/2/3/17). `tooling/golden-runner/package.json` gains an `exports` field at `"./parity-events": "./src/parity-events.ts"`. `parity.spec.ts` removes inline `buildTestEvents`, imports `buildParityEvents` instead. `examples/gantt-vue3/src/sample-data-parity.ts` imports from the shared module and adapts `ParityEvent` → `BarSpec`. `examples/gantt-vue3/package.json` adds `@chronixjs/golden-runner` workspace dependency. `examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue` reads `?parity=true` URL query, swaps `initialBars / initialRows / initialLinks` (links cleared in parity mode), renders a conditional yellow banner. `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css` adds `.cx-demo-parity-banner` rule. Browser-verified via headless Playwright: parity mode → 25 bars × 32 rows × banner visible; default mode → 16 bars × 4 rows × no banner.
- **Commit 2** (`7e88f6c`) — `tooling/golden-runner/src/parity-helpers.ts` ships `loadBothDemos / extractBarsSnapshot / diffBarsSnapshots / formatParityDiff` + types `ParityScenario / BothDemos / DomBarSnapshot / ParityTolerance / ParityMismatch / ParityDiff`. `parity.spec.ts` adds the `cross-demo parity (Phase 17 helper)` describe block with the day-view bar X+width assertion. Bar bbox measured relative to TIMELINE-BODY (not chart-root) so sidebar-width delta doesn't pollute X. Verified end-to-end: both demos launched, `pnpm exec playwright test -g 'cross-demo'` → 1 passed.
- **Commit 3** (`b3d0b5a`) — `audit/PHASE_TEMPLATE.md` `## Parity assertion plan` section gains an example comment showing the canonical helper-row format. `.claude/skills/phase-close/SKILL.md` check #1 gains a "positive signal" line: imports from `../src/parity-helpers.js` evidence the canonical cross-demo pattern. Memory `feedback_chronix_parity_discipline.md` (committed separately since memory lives outside repo) gets a new "How to write the assertion" section pointing at the helper for adapter / render / interaction phases.

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 17)

- **Coordinate-frame surprise.** First attempt of cross-demo bar diff produced ~7px-class X mismatches on every paired bar. Suspicious because the existing in-process parity already established X parity to ±1px. Root cause: measuring bbox relative to chart-root, which includes the sidebar. Sidebar widths differ between demos. Fix: measure relative to TIMELINE-BODY wrapper. Lesson: when normalizing observable measurements across two render pipelines, the COORDINATE FRAME of the measurement is itself part of the algorithm to verify. The body-wrapper is the natural choice because it's the element whose left edge IS the axis x=0 anchor in both demos.
- **`buildTestEvents` inline → shared module migration risk.** Initial edit removed the inline `buildTestEvents` but the next call site (`runBarPlacementParity`) still referenced it. TS hint caught it immediately (`Cannot find name 'buildTestEvents'`). Renamed call to `buildParityEvents`. Tests pass. Single-source-of-truth migration paid off — if I had duplicated rather than extracted, the chronix demo's parity dataset and the test fixture would have drifted next time someone touched only one.
- **Workspace import resolution edge case.** Chronix demo imports `@chronixjs/golden-runner/parity-events`. golden-runner is private workspace pkg with no build step. Solved by adding `"exports": { "./parity-events": "./src/parity-events.ts" }` to golden-runner's package.json — Vite resolves the `.ts` source directly at dev time, no build needed. TS resolves through the same export map for type checking. Worked first try once `pnpm install` re-linked.
- **Skill not hot-loadable in same session.** Created `/phase-close` skill in this session; tried to invoke it via Skill tool; harness rejected (`Unknown skill: phase-close`). Skills are loaded at session start. Walked the checklist manually instead. Next session the skill will be invocable.

### Naming justifications (Phase 17)

- **`parity-events.ts`** (vs `parity-fixtures.ts` or `kui-equivalent-data.ts`) — "events" matches the k-ui domain term ("events" + "resources"). chronix internally renames events → bars, but the dataset is conceptually "the 25 k-ui events"; the file's name reflects what it mirrors.
- **`?parity=true`** (vs `?mode=parity` or `?fixture=kui`) — boolean flag form is idiomatic for opt-in URL toggles; the value is intentionally `true` not `1` to make grep / docs cleaner.
- **`extractBarsSnapshot(source, chart)`** (vs `getBarBoxes` or `snapshotBars`) — "extract" matches the implication that data is being lifted out of DOM; "snapshot" suffix matches the type name `DomBarSnapshot`. The `source` parameter is `'kui' | 'chronix'` (string union) rather than an enum so it's grep-friendly and matches the helper's mental model.
- **`loadBothDemos(browser, scenario)`** (vs `setupParityFixture` or `mountTwoContexts`) — verb-noun, says exactly what it does. "Both demos" makes the cross-demo intent visible at the call site.
- **`ParityTolerance.x | y | width | height` with `Infinity` to skip a channel** — semantic: "tolerance of Infinity means any delta passes" maps directly to the channel-skip use case without inventing a separate skip flag. Default 1px per channel matches the existing `parity.spec.ts` tolerance threshold.

### Open / parked (Phase 17)

- **Resource RENDER order (k-ui's baseName grouping)** — chronix v0 renders rows in `PARITY_RESOURCE_IDS` (= k-ui RESOURCES input) order; k-ui re-sorts internally. Cross-demo Y parity is impossible until chronix gains a row-hierarchy sort. Documented; v0 parity assertions use `y: Infinity, height: Infinity` to skip the channel.
- **Tick / header / sidebar-cell channels** — `extractTicksSnapshot` / `extractHeadersSnapshot` / etc. would each be a separate `extract<Channel>Snapshot` + `diff<Channel>Snapshots` pair. Additive; ship as future phases need them.
- **Pointer-gesture driving** — `applyGesture(steps)` extension on `loadBothDemos` to drive identical pointer sequences on both demos and diff the resulting states. Needed for Phase 9 cross-row drag parity, Phase 14 sidebar resize parity, Phase 16 lifecycle parity. Not in scope for Phase 17; will land when the first phase needs it.
- **Resource metadata (`airportName / baseName / workshopName`)** — chronix parity mode fills the 3 columns with generic placeholders. Column-content parity is a separate phase; would require chronix demo to ingest k-ui's full nested resource structure.
- **Event styling (`backgroundColor / dependencies / extendedProps`)** — out of v0 scope. Geometry-only parity for now.
- **k-ui demo's day-view bar virtualization (12 off-axis bars not in DOM)** — k-ui filters bars to visible range; chronix renders all bars regardless. `mismatches.length === 0` is the hard check; `onlyInChronix.length === 12` is a v0-acceptable warning. Equalizing the strategies is a future phase.

- **199/199 core vitest** unchanged. **174/174 vue3 adapter tests** unchanged. **1 new parity-spec assertion** (`day-view bar X + width parity across both rendered demos`) — passes end-to-end with both demos running. **Total cumulative vitest 374** + **23 parity-spec assertions** (was 22).

## Phase 18 — weekendsVisible filter (DONE, 2026-05-15)

First post-discipline phase: every check in `/phase-close` walked
green BEFORE any status flip. Closes the sole 🔴 BLOCKING drift
from `audit/PARITY_RECHECK.md` Batch 1 #10 — `weekendsVisible` was
plumbed through the input type but never read by `axis-range-planner.ts`.

### Reference reading (Phase 18)

- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/DateProfileGenerator.ts:380-410` (`initHiddenDays`) — reads `props.weekends === false` and pushes day-of-week 0 + 6 into the hidden-day hash. Generalized form reads `props.hiddenDays` array first. All-days-hidden throws. Provides the canonical "Sat=6, Sun=0" mapping mirrored by chronix's `isHiddenWeekendDay`.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/timeline/timeline-date-profile.ts:160-167` — the `slotDates.push` loop's filter: `if (isValidDate(date, ...)) slotDates.push(date)`. Establishes the dense-packed post-filter semantics (`slotDates` array has no gaps; rendered geometry is `i × slotWidth` for dense `i`) that chronix's tick X positions mirror.
- `d:/work/k-ui/examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1296` (`weekendsVisible = ref(true)`), `:1375` (passes `weekends: weekendsVisible.value` to the lib), `:1622` (toggle handler), `:1941` (the `显示周末` checkbox markup) — the reference demo's UI wiring, used by the new parity tests to click-flip the checkbox.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 18)

- **Slot-width depends on slot-count depends on the filter.** Considered a post-pass on `axis.ticks` that drops weekend entries, rejected — `deriveSlotWidth(viewportWidth, slotCount, isTimeScale)` runs once per plan call and seeds every downstream X position. A post-pass would either need to re-run half the planner OR accept that filtered ticks render at the wrong X. Inline filter inside each `planXxx` keeps slot derivation single-pass.
- **Dense-packed tick X post-filter is what the reference does, not just an aesthetic choice.** `slotDates` after the reference's `isValidDate` filter is a dense array, then rendered at dense `<th>` cell positions. Chronix's `x = ticks.length × slotWidth` (using the post-push count as the dense index) is mathematically equivalent. Verified by the `week-view dayCells set equality` parity test: chronix emits `'5/11周一','5/12周二','5/13周三','5/14周四','5/15周五'` and the reference DOM has the same 5 labels in the same dense order.
- **`slotDurationMs` semantics stay constant under the filter.** Chronix's downstream layout passes (`BarPlacementPass`, `LinkRouter`) compute `pxPerMs = slotWidth / slotDurationMs`. The filter shrinks `slotCount` and (via `deriveSlotWidth`) potentially shrinks `slotWidth` too, but `slotDurationMs` stays at `MS_PER_HOUR` / `MS_PER_DAY` because each visible slot still nominally covers 1 hour or 1 day of real time. A bar whose start falls on Sat in weekends-off mode renders at its raw `(t - axisStart) × pxPerMs` offset, which may visually overlap into the next weekday's slot — matches the reference's pre-lane-slicing geometry. Lane-slicing is parked.
- **Day view is deliberately exempt.** Reference behavior: trimming hidden days on a single weekend-day render range returns null and the view fails to render. Chronix v0 keeps day view always-rendering (the type-docstring scope is "week-and-wider views") so a host can drill into a Saturday without the view going blank. The `day view is unaffected: still 24 hourly ticks even when the anchor is a Saturday` unit test pins this regression-guard.
- **The reference demo's `显示周末` checkbox is the natural Playwright handle.** Vue3 demo wraps `<input type="checkbox" ... />` in `<label>...显示周末</label>`. `page.getByLabel('显示周末')` resolves the input; default state is checked, one click flips off. The checkbox sidebar section sits OUTSIDE the chart locator, so the click is rooted at `page`, not `chart`. This makes the parity tests one-shot deterministic — no need for keyboard shortcuts or fragile selectors.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 18)

- **Commit `bccc93d`** — design doc `audit/PHASE_18_WEEKENDS_VISIBLE_FILTER_DESIGN.md` (483 lines). 13-row reference catalog spanning the boolean filter, the array-generalization parked path, the slot-loop filter, snap-index filter (parked), `trimHiddenDays` (rejected), day-view exemption, week/month/season-halfYear-year filter scope, dense-packed X, header-band recompute, `slotDurationMs` invariance, and lane-slicing parked. Approach section includes the helper `isHiddenWeekendDay(d, weekendsVisible)`, the `countDaysAcrossMonths → countVisibleDaysAcrossMonths` generalization, and per-`planXxx` refactor sketches. 3 alternatives considered (post-pass filter, generalize-to-hiddenDays-now, slice-bars-this-phase) all rejected with documented reasons.
- **Commit `7575231`** — algorithm + unit tests + parity assertions, all in one commit per parity discipline.
  - `packages/gantt/src/layout/axis-range-planner.ts`: new `isHiddenWeekendDay(d, weekendsVisible)` helper; `countDaysAcrossMonths` generalized to `countVisibleDaysAcrossMonths(start, monthCount, weekendsVisible)` (2 call sites updated); `planWeekView` restructured to walk `(visibleDay, hour)` instead of flat hour count, emitting 5 dayCells + 120 ticks when weekendsVisible:false; `planMonthView` + `planMonthBandedAxis` filter inside the day loop with dense `x = ticks.length × slotWidth`; `planDayView` unchanged with a code comment locking in the exemption.
  - `packages/gantt/src/layout/types.ts`: `weekendsVisible` JSDoc rewritten — old "When false, Saturday + Sunday slots are omitted from week-and-wider views" replaced with a 4-paragraph description covering filter scope, dense-X behavior, day-view exemption, and the lane-slicing park notice.
  - `packages/gantt/src/layout/axis-range-planner.test.ts`: +8 vitest covering weekendsVisible:false across all 6 views — week dayCells/ticks/no-weekend-labels/dense-X, month visible-day-count (May 2026: 21 weekdays), season (May+Jun+Jul = 66), halfYear (May..Oct = 131 — within the design doc's [125,135] sanity range), year (2026: 261 weekdays), day-view regression-guard with a Saturday anchor.
  - `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts`: +2 Playwright parity tests in a new `test.describe('parity: chronix vs reference demo — weekendsVisible: false (Phase 18)')` block. Both drive the reference demo's `显示周末` checkbox via `page.getByLabel(...)` to flip weekendsVisible OFF, then compare against in-process chronix planner output. (1) `week-view dayCells set equality + count` — both sides emit the same 5 Mon-Fri dayCells. (2) `halfYear-view slot count count equality` — both sides yield 131 day ticks (Mon-Fri only).
- All test runs green: chronix gantt 199 → 207 vitest (+8 new), adapter unchanged 174, total 374 → 381. Parity assertions 22 → 24 in-process (Phase 17's 1 cross-demo unchanged); both new ones pass on first run after rebuilding dist (the memory note `feedback_rebuild_dist_for_cross_package_changes.md` caught a stale-dist bite when first run produced 7 dayCells / 184 slots).

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 18)

- **Stale dist bit again.** First Playwright run of the new parity tests showed chronix planner emitting 7 dayCells / 184 halfYear slots — old behavior. Golden-runner imports `@chronixjs/gantt` through built `dist/`, not src. Ran `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt build` and tests passed on re-run. Fourth time this has bitten (Phase 8, 9, 12, now 18). The memory rule (`feedback_rebuild_dist_for_cross_package_changes.md`) is genuinely load-bearing. Considered automating via `pretest` script on golden-runner but build is fast (~150ms) and explicit rebuild gives a discoverable failure mode rather than hidden caching.
- **Banned-identifier scanner caught a strong-ban reference in JSDoc.** Initial draft of `axis-range-planner.ts` + `axis-range-planner.test.ts` included a JSDoc reference to a strong-banned reference-codebase class name (the `DateProfile`-something generator at upstream) for grounding. Pre-commit hook hard-failed. Rewrote to say "the reference's weekends-off semantics: day-of-week 0 (Sunday) and 6 (Saturday) are filtered out of the slot loop" — same information, no banned identifier. Lesson: chronix code/tests/comments must read standalone (per memory rule `feedback_no_external_repo_refs_in_chronix.md`); cite mechanism, not the function name. The audit journal + design doc may name the reference; chronix source may not.

### Naming justifications (Phase 18)

- **`isHiddenWeekendDay(d, weekendsVisible)`** (vs `isFilteredWeekend` or `isWeekend`) — "hidden" matches the semantic role ("this day is hidden from the axis") rather than the pure calendar property ("this date is a weekend"). The function returns `false` when `weekendsVisible` is true even though Saturday IS a weekend day — the predicate is "should this be filtered out", not "is this a weekend". The name reflects that.
- **`countVisibleDaysAcrossMonths(start, monthCount, weekendsVisible)`** (vs `countWeekdays` or `countDaysExcludingWeekends`) — the function's contract is "count visible days under the current `weekendsVisible` setting", not "always count weekdays". When `weekendsVisible: true` it counts all days (same as the original `countDaysAcrossMonths`); when `false` it counts weekdays only. "Visible" reflects the per-input behavior; "Weekdays" would over-promise. Replaces `countDaysAcrossMonths` directly rather than living alongside it (only 2 call sites; YAGNI keeps both shapes).
- **Variable `visibleDays: Date[]`** (in the restructured `planWeekView`) — pre-resolves the 7 candidate days, filters in-place. The "visible" prefix mirrors `countVisibleDaysAcrossMonths` and matches the user-facing semantic; "weekdays" would be wrong because under `weekendsVisible: true` the array holds Mon-Sun.

### Open / parked (Phase 18)

- **Bar slicing on hidden weekend days** (lane-slicer equivalent) — bars whose timestamps fall on Sat/Sun in weekends-off mode render at their raw `(t - axisStart) × pxPerMs` offset, which may visually overlap into the next weekday's slot. The reference slices the bar at the hidden-day boundary so it visually shrinks. Chronix v0 keeps the bar intact; visible difference under weekends-off mode for bars that straddle weekends. Park as a follow-up phase. Demo data + new parity assertions deliberately stay axis-only (no cross-demo bar parity under weekends-off) so this park doesn't pollute the gate.
- **Generalized `hiddenDays: number[]` array** — reference supports any subset of `[0,1,2,3,4,5,6]`. Chronix v0 has only the boolean `weekendsVisible`. Chronix v0.1 would extend `isHiddenWeekendDay(d, weekendsVisible)` to `isHiddenDay(d, hiddenDays)` and desugar `weekendsVisible: false` to `hiddenDays: [0, 6]`. Low priority — no demo or audit ticket requesting it.
- **Snap-index filter** (the reference's `snapDiffToIndex` skips hidden days for interaction snapping) — chronix's snap math uses `slotDurationMs` directly and doesn't currently produce a per-date snap array. Revisit if a future phase observes that snap-during-drag on a hidden day produces wrong commits.
- **Chronix demo `?weekends=false` URL toggle** — chronix demo hardcodes `weekendsVisible: true`. A URL toggle (matching Phase 17's `?parity=true` pattern) would let users see the filter without writing custom host code. Out of scope for Phase 18 (closes the algorithm gap only); pair with the next chronix-demo overhaul or a Phase 18.x.
- **VRT baselines for weekends-off** — adding `chronix-view-week-weekends-off.png` etc. would lock the rendered geometry. Skipped because Phase 18 doesn't touch chronix demo defaults; VRT additions are zero-risk but high-yield once a `?weekends=false` URL toggle lands.

## Phase 19 — Validation callbacks (DONE, 2026-05-15)

Closes 4 of the 7 items from `audit/PARITY_RECHECK.md` Batch 5 §12
P0: `eventAllow`, `selectAllow`, `eventOverlap`, `eventConstraint`.
The remaining 3 (`selectOverlap`, `selectConstraint`, per-bar
overrides, `'businessHours'` / groupId / recurring-event constraint
shortcuts, per-event `editable` flags) parked with catalog
dispositions. First post-Phase-17 phase to declare `chronix-new`
for its parity plan (silent commit-time gate vs the reference's
live hitupdate cue is a deliberate v0 divergence).

### Reference reading (Phase 19)

- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/validation.ts:81-256` (`isInteractionPropsValid`) — the canonical drag/resize validator. Loops over subject + still events; constraint check via `allConstraintsPass`; overlap check with `isSameResourceRow` shortcut for same-row stacking; per-subject `allows` array iteration. Short-circuit order: constraint → overlap → allow.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/validation.ts:261-325` (`isDateSelectionPropsValid`) — same trio for range-select. Subject is the `dateSelection` span; no movingEvent.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/validation.ts:330-396` (`allConstraintsPass` + `constraintToRanges`) — constraint dispatch: `'businessHours'` string expands via `expandRecurring`, groupId string filters event store by `groupId` field, EventInput object expands itself. Chronix v0 ships the object shape `{ range, rowIds? }` only.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/structs/constraint.ts:9-12` — type signatures: `ConstraintInput = 'businessHours' | string | EventInput | EventInput[]`, `OverlapFunc = (still, moving) => boolean`, `AllowFunc = (span, moving) => boolean`. Chronix ports `OverlapFunc` and `AllowFunc` verbatim semantically; `ConstraintInput` is intentionally narrowed.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/options.ts:184-200` — public option declarations: `eventOverlap: boolean | OverlapFunc`, `eventConstraint: ConstraintInput`, `eventAllow: AllowFunc`, `selectConstraint`, `selectOverlap`, `selectAllow`. Phase 19 ports the first 4; the latter 2 + the per-event variants are parked.
- `d:/work/k-ui/examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1372` — the reference demo wires `eventOverlap: true` (allow-all). No live rejection cue is observable in the demo today; chronix's silent commit-time gate is an honest no-regression for the demo's rendered behavior.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 19)

- **Same-row overlap is rendering-correct, not just k-ui convention.** Chronix's `BarStackHeightPass` greedy-packs same-row bars into vertically stacked sub-rows. Two bars on the same row with intersecting time ranges therefore don't visually collide — they share the row height and stack. Cross-row overlap is the meaningful conflict signal (one bar leaves row A at hour 10 and another bar arrives on row B at hour 10 — a scheduling conflict the host might want to forbid). The `if (stillBar.rowId === proposal.rowId) continue` skip in `satisfiesOverlap` is therefore semantically aligned with `BarStackHeightPass`'s output, not just a tribute to the reference's `isSameResourceRow` shortcut.
- **Pure validators in `packages/gantt/src/api/validation.ts` keep the core's "pure pixel-and-time math" purity intact.** The adapter (vue3) does the wiring: it pulls validator props off the component, builds a `ValidationContext` (which resolves `MaybeRefOrGetter` to plain values), and dispatches to the core's `validateDrop` / `validateResize` / `validateSelect`. The session layer (`defaultPointerCaptureSession`) stays validation-free — its job is producing the `resolvedRange`, not gating it. Decision documented as alternative #3 in the design doc.
- **Rejection-emit shape is the host's main observability hook.** The `*-rejected` payloads carry `oldRange`, `attemptedRange`, and `reason`. A host can show `'cannot move past 8pm (constraint)'` toast text directly from `reason` without re-running the predicates. Three separate emits (rather than one with a `rejected: { reason }` field on existing emits) means `bar-drop` is exclusively about successful commits — host code branches on emit kind, not a flag.
- **Bar-stack visual stacking + same-row exclusion fits both v0 BarSpec semantics AND k-ui's resource-row semantics.** K-ui's `eventDef.resourceIds: string[]` can attach one event to MULTIPLE resources; chronix `BarSpec.rowId: string` is single. Chronix v0 doesn't multi-row by design (parked). The single-row exclusion matches the reference's effective behavior when `subject.resourceIds.length === 1`, which is the common case.
- **Progress-handle is the only commit that intentionally skips validation.** Reasoning: changing progress is a value mutation (number 0..100), not a date/row mutation. Validators take `DropProposal { range, rowId }` — there's no field for "progress changed". A future "progress validator" would be `progressAllow(barId, oldProgress, newProgress)` and live in a separate path. The unit test `progress-handle commit is never gated by eventConstraint` pins this regression-guard.
- **The validator gate is opt-in.** Each validator prop is optional; when `bars` isn't threaded into `useGanttPointer` (test fixtures that don't pass it) or when all 4 validator props are undefined (host hasn't wired any), the gate is a no-op. Test `regression guard: with no validator props, commits go through as before` proves this — pre-Phase-19 fixtures (which don't pass `bars`) continue to work unchanged.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 19)

- **Commit `e7e0fa8`** — design doc `audit/PHASE_19_VALIDATION_CALLBACKS_DESIGN.md` (514 lines). 17-row reference catalog. 5 alternatives considered (live cue, per-bar overrides, validate-in-session, unified `onBarMutation`, throw-instead-of-emit) all rejected with reasons. Parity assertion plan declares `chronix-new` with rationale.
- **Commit `973db04`** — implementation + tests + demo wiring, single commit per parity discipline.
  - `packages/gantt/src/api/validation.ts` (new, 152 LOC): types `DropProposal` / `EventAllowFunc` / `SelectAllowFunc` / `EventOverlapFunc` / `EventConstraint` / `RejectionReason` / `ValidationContext`; pure validators `validateDrop` / `validateResize` (alias) / `validateSelect`; private helpers `satisfiesConstraint` / `satisfiesOverlap` / `rangesIntersect`.
  - `packages/gantt/src/api/validation.test.ts` (new, 280 LOC): 19 vitest covering all 4 predicate codepaths + same-row vs cross-row overlap + boolean vs function vs undefined `eventOverlap` + short-circuit order + select-side variants.
  - `packages/gantt/src/api/index.ts` + `packages/gantt/src/index.ts`: re-export the 7 types + 3 functions.
  - `adapters/vue3/src/use-gantt-pointer.ts`: 4 new reactive inputs (`bars`, `eventAllow`, `selectAllow`, `eventOverlap`, `eventConstraint`) + 3 rejection callbacks (`onBarDropRejected` / `onBarResizeRejected` / `onSelectRejected`) + payload types (`BarDropRejectedPayload` / `BarResizeRejectedPayload` / `SelectRejectedPayload`); private helpers `buildValidationContext` / `runDropValidation` / `runResizeValidation` / `runSelectValidation`; `commitDrag` / `commitResize` / `commitSelect` consult validators before firing success callbacks.
  - `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: 4 new props + 3 new emits; thread to composable.

  - `adapters/vue3/src/index.ts`: re-export the 3 rejected payload types.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue`: 4 sample predicates (`eventOverlap: false` constant, `eventConstraint` 08:00–20:00 today, `eventAllow ≥ 8am`, `selectAllow ≤ 4h`), 4 toggle checkboxes, 3 rejection handlers logging `[reason]`-tagged event-panel entries.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css`: `.cx-demo-validation-toggles` block (flex layout, padding-top divider).
- All test runs green: chronix gantt 207 → 226 vitest (+19), adapter 174 → 180 vitest (+6), total 381 → 406. Existing 24 in-process parity assertions stay green after k-ui demo restart. Chronix demo at `http://localhost:8702/` confirmed serves cleanly with the new validation toggle row.

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 19)

- **Test fixture had same-row when I meant cross-row.** Initial validation tests for overlap rejection used `proposal('r2', 11, 13)` for a moving bar at r1 — but the still bar was ALSO on r2, so the proposal hit r2 and the same-row exclusion skipped the overlap check, returning `null` instead of `'overlap'`. Three tests failed with `expected 'overlap', got null`. Root cause: I conflated "moving bar's original row" with "still bar's row" when writing the fixtures. Fix: set proposal rowId to the moving bar's original row so the still bar (on a different row) becomes the cross-row intersect. Lesson: write the assertion expectation in terms of `proposal.rowId !== stillBar.rowId` for the cross-row predicate, not in terms of "what row the moving bar starts on".
- **Stale dist bit AGAIN (5th occurrence).** After writing `validation.ts` + re-exports, the adapter's `import { validateDrop } from '@chronixjs/gantt'` failed with `has no exported member 'validateDrop'`. Adapter imports through `dist/`, not src. Ran `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt build` to rebuild; imports resolved. Then again after adapter changes, the demo's `import { BarDropRejectedPayload } from '@chronixjs/gantt-vue3'` failed with the same shape — adapter `dist/` was also stale. Ran `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt-vue3 build`. Memory rule `feedback_rebuild_dist_for_cross_package_changes.md` is genuinely load-bearing — both rebuilds are needed when cross-package types ripple from core to adapter to demo.
- **Parity tests all failed mid-run because k-ui dev server died.** The full vitest sweep passed (406/406), then `playwright test parity.spec.ts` reported `24 failed`. Diagnostic showed `net::ERR_CONNECTION_REFUSED at http://localhost:8701/` — the k-ui demo had stopped between sessions. Restarted at 8701, re-ran, 24/24 passed. Lesson: when picking up across sessions, always re-verify ports `8701` (k-ui) + `8702` (chronix) are live before relying on parity-suite output.

### Naming justifications (Phase 19)

- **`DropProposal { range, rowId }`** (vs `MutationProposal` / `CommitProposal` / `DateSpan`) — "drop" matches the user-facing gesture verb ("drag to drop"); "proposal" makes the not-yet-committed shape explicit. Range-select uses the same shape (no separate type), so the name needs to read naturally for both drag/resize AND range-select. `DateSpan` would mirror the reference too closely.
- **`RejectionReason = 'constraint' | 'overlap' | 'allow'`** (vs `RejectedBy` / `BlockedReason` / `FailureKind`) — three-character names that match the predicate names exactly. Host code typically does `switch (reason) { case 'overlap': ... }` and the case label IS the predicate name, which is readable. `allow` for the predicate-returned-false case is slightly counter-intuitive ("allow rejected, so reason = 'allow'") but matches the prop name `eventAllow` so the trace from prop → rejected reason is obvious.
- **`runDropValidation` / `runResizeValidation` / `runSelectValidation`** (adapter-private helpers, vs `validate*` or `gate*`) — "run" prefix signals these are adapter-side dispatch wrappers around the pure core `validateDrop` / `validateResize` / `validateSelect`. Two different verbs for the two layers prevents confusion between "call the pure function" and "call the adapter's wiring".
- **`bar-drop-rejected` / `bar-resize-rejected` / `select-rejected` emits** (vs `bar-drop-blocked` / `bar-drop-failed` / `bar-drop-veto`) — "rejected" reads as a passive-voice fact ("the drop was rejected") matching the chronix emit grammar (`'bar-drop'` is also a fact, not a request). "blocked" feels active (the host blocked it; chronix vetoed it autonomously — different semantics). "failed" implies an exception path; this is a successful validator result, not a failure.
- **`useEventOverlap` / `useEventConstraint` / `useEventAllow` / `useSelectAllow` (demo state refs)** — Vue idiom is `useXxx` for composable helpers, NOT boolean state. But the toggle naming here pairs naturally with the prop ("use the `eventOverlap` validator? checkbox checked = yes"), and renaming to `eventOverlapToggle` or `isEventOverlapActive` reads worse in the template. Demo code only — no public API impact.

### Open / parked (Phase 19)

- **Live validation cue during hitupdate** (the reference's `interaction.isValid` flag + red mirror + cursor change). Chronix v0 ships silent commit-time gate. v1 path: route the validator result into the active-transaction render path; add `cx-gantt-bar--invalid` class + a `cursor: not-allowed` rule; possibly throttle the validator call to once per N pointermoves. Out of scope for Phase 19 — would double the surface and the perf-cliff analysis.
- **`selectOverlap` + `selectConstraint` (the 2 select-side validators)** — additive surface; can land in a Phase 19.x if a host requests them. `selectOverlap` would consult the same `bars` list at commit time; `selectConstraint` would re-use `EventConstraint`.
- **Per-bar overrides (`BarSpec.overlap?` / `BarSpec.constraint?` / `BarSpec.editable?` / etc.)** — k-ui's per-event config layer. Chronix v0 component-level only. Adding per-bar would require config merging (`subjectConfig` + `componentConfig`) at every predicate site, doubling the validator complexity.
- **Constraint string shortcuts (`'businessHours'`, groupId, recurring `EventInput`)** — all depend on parked infrastructure (businessHours rendering, groupId IR field, recurring events). The `{ range, rowIds? }` object shape covers the explicit "stay-in-window" case. Re-expose if/when a host wants e.g. `eventConstraint: 'businessHours'`.
- **Live render of `eventConstraint` window** — the demo's "today 08:00–20:00" constraint is invisible — the user sees the bar revert without a visual hint of WHY. v1 could overlay a faint window on the axis (`.cx-gantt-constraint-window`) when `eventConstraint` is non-null. Out of scope for Phase 19.
- **Parity assertion for the rejection path** — declared chronix-new because the reference demo doesn't wire matching predicates. v1 path: extend the chronix demo's `?parity=true` mode (Phase 17) to wire identical predicates to a manually-edited reference demo build for cross-comparison. Big lift; defer.
- **Demo wiring with imperfect predicates** — the `eventAllow ≥ 8am` toggle rejects ALL drops starting before 8am, INCLUDING drops landing exactly at 8am that started elsewhere — the toggle is illustrative, not production-grade. A more nuanced predicate would consider the bar's `oldRange` too. Documented as "illustrative" in the design doc; demo aside.

## Phase 20 — Bar color pipeline (DONE, 2026-05-16)

Closes 4-of-13 of PARITY_RECHECK Batch 5 §5 P0 (event rendering /
styling). Adds `barColor` / `barBackgroundColor` / `barBorderColor`
/ `barTextColor` props + 3 callbacks. Wires the long-dormant
`BarSpec.style` field (defined in Phase 1, unused for 19 phases)
through the render. **Phase 10 amendment**: reverses Phase 10's
"bar fills stay in CSS" architectural call — bar colors move to
theme tokens + inline attributes so the cascade can reach the
final rendered value at runtime. Non-color hooks (rx, ry, cursor)
stay in CSS.

### Reference reading (Phase 20)

- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/options.ts:184-192` — the 4 color option declarations (`eventBackgroundColor`, `eventBorderColor`, `eventTextColor`, `eventColor`). `eventColor` is the documented umbrella.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/options.ts:356` — default `eventTextColor: '#fff'`. Chronix theme default `barTextColor: '#ffffff'` matches.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/component/event-rendering.ts:471-536` (`buildEventContentArg`) — assembles the initial `EventContentArg` with 16 fields. Chronix's `BarStyleArg` carries 4 essentials + 3 cascaded defaults; 12 of the reference's fields depend on infrastructure chronix doesn't have (multi-segment, nowTimer, full event-api).
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/component/event-rendering.ts:575-627` (`getEventStyles`) — runs `eventBackgroundColor` → `eventBorderColor` → `eventTextColor` callbacks; the umbrella logic at lines 604-612 inherits resolved bg as border when callback set bg but not border. Chronix ports the same umbrella but extends it to fire across ALL override layers (prop, spec.style, callback), not just callbacks.
- `d:/work/k-ui/packages/gantt/src/component/event-rendering.ts:198-221` — `EventContentArg` shape (16 fields). Chronix's `BarStyleArg` is 8 fields total (4 identity + 3 cascade defaults + 1 transaction state).
- `d:/work/k-ui/examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1327, 1438` — reference demo's `eventBorderColor: '#3788d8'` + `eventTextColor: '#fff'` defaults. Chronix parity-mode App.vue now pins matching `:bar-background-color="'#3788d8'"` so cross-demo color parity tests have a deterministic baseline.
- `d:/work/k-ui/examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue:1500-1520` — reference demo's `eventStyleCallbacks.eventBackgroundColor` reading `extendedProps.priority`. Chronix demo's `samplePriorityCallback` ports the same predicate.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 20)

- **The cascade defaults must mirror the prior CSS literals byte-for-byte or the no-override case visibly regresses.** Existing `.cx-gantt-bar { fill: #3b82f6; stroke: #1e40af }` becomes `theme.barBackgroundColor: '#3b82f6'` + `theme.barBorderColor: '#1e40af'`. All 5 chronix VRT baselines re-verified unchanged — the inline-attribute render is pixel-equivalent to the CSS-class render when the painted colors match. This is the most fragile part of the Phase 10 amendment: any default mismatch would surface as a 5/5 VRT diff.
- **Background-overrides-border umbrella must be tracked PER-CHANNEL through the cascade, not just at the callback layer.** The reference checks the umbrella only at the callback stage. Chronix tracks `backgroundFromOverride` / `borderFromOverride` flags across all 4 layers, so `barBackgroundColor: '#X'` (prop) gives `stroke="X"` too even with no callback. Reason: prop-only override is the common ergonomic case; restricting the umbrella to callbacks would force the host to also wire `:bar-border-color="..."`. The implementation passes 14 unit tests including 3 dedicated umbrella scenarios (theme-only, prop bg, callback bg) and 1 negative (both prop bg + prop border → umbrella doesn't fire).
- **Progress label color stays at `theme.progressLabel`, NOT `barTextColor`.** Design tension: should `barTextColor` override progress text? Decision: no — the progress label has its own dedicated theme token (`#064e3b` dark green on translucent green) for default readability. Wiring `barTextColor` to progress would force the host to also pass a progress-readable text color whenever they want to change "the bar's color". The SFC test `progress label fill stays at theme.progressLabel` pins this regression-guard. `barTextColor`'s consumer in v0 is `BarSlotArgs.resolvedTextColor` for custom slot renderers + future bar-title text rendering.
- **Cross-demo color parity is honest: chronix parity-mode pins the reference's color defaults.** The reference demo wires `eventBorderColor: '#3788d8'` as a hard-coded default. Chronix's CSS literals (`#3b82f6` / `#1e40af`) DIVERGE from the reference — so a default-default comparison would always fail. Phase 20's parity-mode wiring (`barBackgroundColor: '#3788d8'` only when `?parity=true`) makes the cross-demo color test deterministic without changing chronix's own defaults for the standalone demo experience.
- **`getComputedStyle().fill` returns `rgb(R, G, B)` form regardless of inline vs CSS source.** Cross-browser SVG fill resolution normalizes to rgb. The new `hexToRgbString('#3788d8')` helper produces `rgb(55, 136, 216)` for direct comparison against the extracted snapshot. This abstraction makes the cross-demo color test robust to inline-vs-class painting differences (k-ui paints via inline `style={{ backgroundColor }}`, chronix via inline `fill=` attribute).
- **The parity dataset has no `extendedProps.priority` metadata so the priority callback defers for every bar.** This is intentional: the callback test verifies the cascade ROUTES correctly (callback is exercised, returns undefined, falls through to prop layer), without conflating "callback predicate logic" with "rendered color matches reference". The "rendered color matches reference" assertion uses the prop-layer default test.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 20)

- **Commit `1dadef3`** — design doc `audit/PHASE_20_BAR_COLOR_PIPELINE_DESIGN.md` (582 lines). 17-row reference catalog. 5 alternatives considered (keep CSS + add inline, combined `barStyles` object prop, add bar-title text rendering, plumb fontSize/fontWeight, Vue3 `<style>` injection) all rejected with reasons. Phase 10 amendment documented as the load-bearing architectural call.
- **Commit `e2ab288`** — implementation + tests + demo + parity helper + 2 cross-demo color tests, single commit per parity discipline.
  - `packages/gantt/src/api/bar-style.ts` (new, 178 LOC): types (`BarStyleArg`, `BarColorFunc`, `ResolvedBarStyle`, `ResolveBarStyleInput`) + pure `resolveBarStyle` resolver. Tracks `backgroundFromOverride` / `borderFromOverride` flags across all 4 cascade layers for the cross-layer umbrella.
  - `packages/gantt/src/api/bar-style.test.ts` (new, 200 LOC): 14 vitest covering theme default, `barColor` umbrella, `BarSpec.style` overrides, callback override + defer + arg cascade-defaults + isSelected/activeTransaction forwarding, 4 umbrella scenarios (theme, prop, callback, both), full-cascade precedence.
  - `packages/gantt/src/api/chronix-theme.ts`: 3 new tokens (`barBackgroundColor`, `barBorderColor`, `barTextColor`); defaults match prior CSS byte-for-byte (`#3b82f6` / `#1e40af` / `#ffffff`).

  - `packages/gantt/src/api/index.ts` + `packages/gantt/src/index.ts`: re-export new types + `resolveBarStyle` function.
  - `packages/gantt/src/render/bar-slot.ts`: `BarSlotArgs` gains `resolvedBackgroundColor` / `resolvedBorderColor` / `resolvedTextColor`. Additive — existing slot renderers still work.
  - `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.ts`: 7 new props (4 colors + 3 callbacks). `resolveBarStyle` runs per placed bar in the render loop; inline `fill=` / `stroke=` on the default rect; resolved colors threaded into `BarSlotArgs`. The progress label intentionally stays at `theme.progressLabel`.
  - `adapters/vue3/src/chronix-gantt.test.ts`: +6 SFC tests covering each cascade source + barColor umbrella + the progress-label-stays-theme regression-guard.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/sample-data.ts`: 3 sample bars (`bar-2`, `bar-5`, `bar-8`) get `extendedProps.priority` so the demo's priority callback toggle has something to read.

Parity mode wires `barBackgroundColor: '#3788d8'` + `barBorderColor: '#3788d8'`. URL flag `?priorityCallback=true` opts the priority callback into parity mode.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css`: `.cx-gantt-bar` loses `fill` + `stroke` (Phase 10 amendment); keeps `stroke-width: 1` + `rx: 3` + `ry: 3` + `cursor: move`.

  - `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts`: +2 cross-demo color parity tests in a new `cross-demo bar fill parity (Phase 20)` describe. Both pass against running demos at 8701/8702.
- All test runs green: chronix gantt 226 → 240 vitest (+14), adapter 180 → 186 vitest (+6), total 406 → 426. Parity assertions 25 → 27 (1 cross-demo + 2 new color parity). 5/5 chronix VRT baselines pass unchanged.

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 20)

- **Two dist rebuilds needed (stale-dist lesson reinforced for the 6th time).** After writing `bar-style.ts` + re-exports in `@chronixjs/gantt`, the adapter's `import { resolveBarStyle } from '@chronixjs/gantt'` failed type resolution. Ran `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt build`. After wiring 7 new props + payload types in `@chronixjs/gantt-vue3`, the demo's `import { BarColorFunc } from '@chronixjs/gantt'` STILL failed even though core dist was fresh — the adapter's dist hadn't been rebuilt to pick up the prop-type changes. Ran `pnpm --filter @chronixjs/gantt-vue3 build`. Both rebuilds were essential. Memory rule `feedback_rebuild_dist_for_cross_package_changes.md` is the durable fix.
- **The umbrella tracking is more subtle than the reference's.** Initial draft tracked `backgroundFromOverride` only at the callback layer (mirror of reference's `event-rendering.ts:604-612`). Unit test `fires when background is overridden but border stays at theme` would have failed with `barBackgroundColor: '#10b981'` set via prop alone (no callback) — umbrella wouldn't fire → border stays at `theme.barBorderColor`. Caught at design time, not test time: extended umbrella tracking across ALL layers so prop-only bg override also triggers border-inherits-bg. Deliberate chronix extension — the reference's narrower umbrella scope was an artifact of its layered callback architecture, not a deliberate API call.
- **Pre-existing stylelint warnings in demo styles.css when ci-check ran.** Lines 10-48 had `order/properties-alphabetical-order` errors unrelated to my Phase 20 edit (which only modified line 178+). Pre-existing issues — not introduced by Phase 20. The Phase 20 edit zone (removing `fill` + `stroke` from `.cx-gantt-bar`) didn't trigger stylelint hits because the remaining declarations (`stroke-width`, `rx`, `ry`, `cursor`) are alphabetically ordered.

### Naming justifications (Phase 20)

- **`barColor` / `barBackgroundColor` / `barBorderColor` / `barTextColor`** (vs reference's `eventColor` / etc.) — chronix calls them "bars" throughout the codebase (BarSpec, BarPlacementPass, BarStackHeightPass, BarSlotArgs, etc.); the prop surface mirrors this. The reference's "event" prefix is its domain noun (event scheduler), not chronix's.
- **`barBackgroundColorCallback` etc.** (vs reference's nested `eventStyleCallbacks.eventBackgroundColor`) — flat prop shape matches the rest of `<ChronixGantt>`'s prop surface; nesting under a `styleCallbacks: { ... }` object would diverge from chronix's flat convention.
- **`resolveBarStyle(input): ResolvedBarStyle`** — verb-noun pure-function naming consistent with `defaultLinkRouter.route` etc. "Resolve" reflects the layered cascade semantic; "compile" would mirror the reference's `compileEventUi` but reads as build-time. The chronix function runs per render frame.
- **`BarStyleArg`** (vs reference's `EventContentArg`) — chronix-native name avoiding the reference's "content" verbiage. Arg, not Args (singular), matching `BarDropPayload` / `BarResizePayload` etc. — chronix convention is "[Noun]Payload" or "[Noun]Arg" for single-arg callbacks, plural for output-bag shapes (`BarSlotArgs`).
- **`hexToRgbString` (parity-helpers)** — narrow utility; the name says what goes in and what comes out. Considered `normalizeColor` (rejected — too broad; no other color formats supported in v0) and `rgbFromHex` (rejected — reads as "rgb taken FROM hex" rather than "hex turned into rgb-string").

### Open / parked (Phase 20)

- **`eventFontSize` / `eventFontWeight` callbacks** — depend on bar-title text rendering, which is itself parked. Add as part of the bar-title text phase whenever it lands. `BarSpec.style.fontSize` / `style.fontWeight` (defined in Phase 1) similarly unwired.
- **Bar-title text rendering** — the chronix default `<rect>` has no `<text>` child. Adding one is a UX scope (truncation, ellipsis, multi-line, RTL, alignment, padding) outside Phase 20's color-pipeline focus. v0's `barTextColor` consumer is `BarSlotArgs.resolvedTextColor` for custom slot renderers; default render has no visible consumer for text color beyond the (separately themed) progress label.
- **k-ui's `EventContentArg.isMirror` / `isStart` / `isEnd` / `isPast` / `isFuture` / `isToday`** — depend on multi-segment bar rendering + nowTimer + multi-day-spanning bars. Chronix's `BarStyleArg` carries `activeTransaction` (which covers the mirror/dragging/resizing space) but the date-relative flags wait for nowIndicator infrastructure (Phase 21 candidate).
- **Per-bar `BarSpec.editable` / `BarSpec.startEditable` / `BarSpec.durationEditable`** — separate from the color pipeline. Component-level `editable` covers the demo. Add when a host requests per-bar editability override.
- **`selectMirror` overlay** — k-ui renders a separate `<g>` during drag showing the destination state. Chronix mutates render geometry in place (no mirror element). Separate phase if added; Phase 20's color pipeline doesn't include mirror-specific styling.
- **Bar fill default color reconciliation between chronix demo and reference** — chronix demo defaults to chronix's `#3b82f6` blue; reference demo defaults to its `#3788d8` slightly-different blue. Cross-demo parity uses parity-mode to align. Phase 20 doesn't change either side's standalone defaults — that's a separate "match reference baseline aesthetics" call.
- **Visual feedback in mid-drag / mid-resize** — the resolved style currently doesn't differentiate "live drag" state (other than via `activeTransaction` callbacks receive). A future phase could add `barDraggingBackgroundColor` etc. tokens for mid-gesture color shifts. Currently parked; demo's "themed bars" toggle shows static colors only.

## Phase 20.5 + 20.6 — Infrastructure for 2.0 scale (DONE, 2026-05-16)

Two paired infrastructure phases landed in one session via the new
batch-design + batch-impl pattern. **Phase 20.5** centralizes the
parity-helper layer (snapshot extractors + generic diff) so the
remaining ~80 2.0 phases each add ~5 LOC of parity assertion
instead of ~50 LOC of bespoke `chart.evaluate(...)`. **Phase 20.6**
refactors the demo's hand-wired toggle plumbing to a URL-query
driven config layer so each new demo toggle is 1 line instead of
~30 LOC. Both are prep work for sustaining 100+ phase 2.0 roadmap
without per-phase cost growing linearly.

### Reference reading (Phase 20.5 + 20.6)

- `D:/work/chronix/tooling/golden-runner/src/parity-helpers.ts` (Phase 17 + 20 baseline) — existing `extractBarsSnapshot` shape that Phase 20.5 generalized while preserving backward-compatible defaults.
- `D:/work/chronix/tooling/golden-runner/src/reference-dom-map.ts` — allow-listed boundary for reference-side CSS class names. Phase 20.5 honors this: chronix-side selectors centralize in a private `CHRONIX_SELECTORS` map; reference-side selectors continue to flow through the existing exports.
- `D:/work/chronix/tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity.spec.ts` Phase 17/18/20 cross-demo tests — existing 27 parity assertions that Phase 20.5 must keep green via backward-compatible `DomBarSnapshot` + `ParityDiff` types.
- `D:/work/chronix/examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue` (360 LOC at Phase 20 endgame) — the per-toggle ~30 LOC pattern (ref + computed prop + checkbox + reset) that Phase 20.6 collapses to 1 schema line.
- `d:/work/k-ui/examples/gantt/vue3/src/DemoApp.vue` (~2285 LOC) — the reference demo's growth curve as a cautionary tale. Chronix demo without Phase 20.6 was on the same trajectory.

### Mechanisms understood (Phase 20.5 + 20.6)

- **`DomBarSnapshot.fill` stays top-level for backward compat; new `DomElementSnapshot` puts colors under `style` map**. Splitting the channels lets `diffSnapshots` walk style keys uniformly via `Object.keys(snapshot.style)` rather than enumerating known fields. Tests for legacy bar shape pass without modification; new helpers use the generic shape.
- **`ComputedStyleKey` string-literal union is the safe choice over `keyof CSSStyleDeclaration`**. The latter has ~600 keys including many that browsers compute differently (font shorthand, transform-origin sub-fields). Restricting to 16 named keys catches typos at compile time AND signals intent: "these are the keys the parity layer is currently designed to compare". New phases extend the union explicitly.
- **The variance issue with `Record<string, ConfigField<unknown>>`**: when `exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` is on AND `ConfigField` has a function-typed property (parse: (raw) => T), the contravariance check rejects `ConfigField<ViewId>` from being assignable to `ConfigField<unknown>`. Switching the constraint to `ConfigField<any>` bypasses variance (any is bivariant in TS). The internal `infer T` in the mapped type still recovers the per-key type, so `cfg.view.value` keeps its `ViewId` type at the call site.
- **happy-dom's history origin pins to `localhost:3000`** — any test that drives `window.history.replaceState` must use the same origin or the call throws. The fix in `demo-config.test.ts`: construct URLs via `new URL(window.location.origin)` rather than hardcoded `'http://localhost/'`.
- **Auto-generated URL schema panel = self-documenting demo**: `describeConfigSchema(schema)` walks the schema fields and emits `{ key, defaultValue, description }`. The template renders this as a `<details>` table. Adding a new toggle to the schema = the panel auto-updates. Zero hand-maintained URL docs to drift from reality.
- **k-ui demo's tick + header cells have no stable class**, so `extractTicksSnapshot` / `extractHeaderCellsSnapshot` accept an `options.labelRegex`. chronix-side uses class selectors (`.cx-gantt-tick-label`); k-ui-side walks leaf `<text>` elements + regex-filters. The asymmetric implementation is honest about the DOM contract difference — k-ui's text-only rendering means we MUST walk leaves for k-ui.

### Chronix work derived (Phase 20.5 + 20.6)

- **Commit `e93a746`** — design doc `audit/PHASE_20_5_PARITY_INFRASTRUCTURE_V2_DESIGN.md` (381 lines). 9-row catalog of channels chronix needs to extract; chronix-new declaration for parity. Interaction recording + VRT matrix deferred to Phase 22 / 21 respectively.
- **Commit `5e85bd9`** — design doc `audit/PHASE_20_6_DEMO_CONFIG_REFACTOR_DESIGN.md` (342 lines). 5 alternatives considered (Pinia / single config object / localStorage / global URL writes / co-locate predicates) all rejected with reasons. Parity / VRT preservation strategy: default URL state = pre-refactor state.
- **Commit `003e73a`** — Phase 20.5 implementation:
  - `tooling/golden-runner/src/parity-helpers.ts`: +839 LOC. New `ComputedStyleKey` union, `SnapshotOptions`, `DomElementSnapshot`, `SnapshotTolerance`, `SnapshotMismatch`, `SnapshotDiff` types. `extractBarsSnapshot` accepts options + optional `style` capture. New `extractTicksSnapshot` / `extractHeaderCellsSnapshot` / `extractSidebarSnapshot` extractors. New `diffSnapshots` generic + `formatSnapshotDiff` formatter. Private `CHRONIX_SELECTORS` map centralizes chronix-side DOM entry points. Existing `DomBarSnapshot` + `ParityDiff` + `ParityTolerance` types preserved verbatim.
  - `tooling/golden-runner/tests/parity-helpers.unit.spec.ts` (new): 17 unit tests covering `hexToRgbString` round-trip + null fallback, `diffSnapshots` per-channel tolerance + Infinity skip + text exact/skip + style equality + per-key skip + numeric style tolerance + only-in lists + style-key-on-one-side, `diffBarsSnapshots` legacy adapter regression guard, `formatSnapshotDiff` happy + populated.
- **Commit `975a8d4`** — Phase 20.6 implementation:
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/demo-config.ts` (new, ~180 LOC): `bool` / `str` / `num` / `enumOf` field factories + `useDemoConfig(schema)` composable + `describeConfigSchema(schema)` helper. URL is source of truth; `history.replaceState` writes back with default-value filtering. SSR-safe via `typeof window` gates.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/demo-config.test.ts` (new): 10 vitest covering field factory parsing/serialization + URL round-trip + reset + unrelated-key preservation + schema introspection.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/sample-callbacks.ts` (new, ~60 LOC): `sampleEventOverlap` / `sampleEventConstraint` / `sampleEventAllow` / `sampleSelectAllow` / `samplePriorityCallback` + `PRIORITY_BACKGROUND` / `THEMED_BAR_BACKGROUND` / `THEMED_BAR_BORDER` / `UMBRELLA_BAR_COLOR` / `PARITY_REFERENCE_COLOR` constants. Domain predicates separated from demo plumbing.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/App.vue`: refactored to use `useDemoConfig(DEMO_SCHEMA)` + import predicates from sample-callbacks.ts. Template binds `v-model="cfg.X.value"` per toggle. New `<details>` URL schema panel auto-generated from schema.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/vitest.config.ts` (new): happy-dom env so demo-config tests can drive `window.location`.
  - `examples/gantt-vue3/src/styles.css`: `.cx-demo-url-schema` rules for the new `<details>` panel.

Test count: 426 → 453 (+17 Phase 20.5 + 10 Phase 20.6). 61 parity + VRT all green. 5 chronix VRT baselines + 27 parity assertions unchanged by either phase.

### Bugs / gotchas hit (Phase 20.5 + 20.6)

- **`exactOptionalPropertyTypes: true` + variance check on `ConfigField<unknown>`**: initial draft of `useDemoConfig` constrained S to `Record<string, ConfigField<unknown>>`. TypeScript rejected because `ConfigField` has a `serialize: (value: T) => string | null` (contravariant in T), so `ConfigField<ViewId>` is not assignable to `ConfigField<unknown>`. Fix: switch constraint to `ConfigField<any>` — any is bivariant, bypassing the check. The internal mapped type's `infer T` still recovers per-key types at the call site.
- **happy-dom origin restriction**: `demo-config.test.ts` initial draft tried `new URL('http://localhost/')` for `setUrl`. happy-dom's default origin is `http://localhost:3000`, and `history.replaceState` rejects cross-origin updates. Fix: construct via `new URL(window.location.origin)` so the simulated URL matches the existing origin.
- **`getComputedStyle` index access types as `string | undefined`**: initial draft of style-map extraction had `map[k] = (cs as unknown as Record<string, string>)[k]`. TypeScript's `noUncheckedIndexedAccess: true` types the result as `string | undefined`, incompatible with `Record<string, string>`. Fix (applied via sed across all 4 extractors): `map[k] = (cs as ...)[k] ?? ''` — empty string fallback preserves the strict type without changing runtime semantics.
- **JSON formatting artifact from Playwright**: running the parity suite caused `tooling/golden-runner/recordings/event-resize-right/log.json` to be rewritten with multi-line array formatting (was inline). Unrelated to Phase 20.5/20.6 work. Reverted via `git checkout` before committing.

### Naming justifications (Phase 20.5 + 20.6)

- **`ComputedStyleKey`** (vs `CssProperty` or `StyleKey`) — explicit about the source: these are keys we read from `getComputedStyle()`, not arbitrary CSS properties. The naming reads as "key for use with `getComputedStyle()` output" at the call site.
- **`DomElementSnapshot`** (vs `ElementSnapshot` or `Snapshot`) — "Dom" prefix signals these are derived from DOM bbox + computed style, not from any logical model layer. Matches existing `DomBarSnapshot` convention.
- **`SnapshotTolerance.style: Record<ComputedStyleKey, number | 'exact' | 'skip'>`** — union of number (numeric px tolerance like fontSize ±1) + `'exact'` (default for color strings) + `'skip'` (bypass entirely). Reads cleanly as "tolerance per style key": `{ fontSize: 1, fill: 'exact', cursor: 'skip' }`.
- **`diffSnapshots`** (vs `compareSnapshots` or `snapshotDiff`) — verb-noun matches `diffBarsSnapshots` precedent. The output is a `SnapshotDiff` object, so the verb is `diff` and the noun is the snapshots being diffed.
- **`useDemoConfig`** (vs `createDemoConfig` or `defineDemoConfig`) — Vue's composable convention is `useXxx`. Returns reactive refs + helpers; matches the Vue 3 idiom.
- **`bool` / `str` / `num` / `enumOf`** (vs `boolField` / `stringField` / etc.) — brief factory names since they're called inline in the schema literal. Each schema declaration is a one-liner: `editable: bool(true, '...')`. Verbose names would clutter the schema.
- **`enumOf`** (not `enum`) — `enum` is a reserved word in TypeScript. `enumOf(values, default)` is clear about the values being passed.

### Open / parked (Phase 20.5 + 20.6)

- **Interaction recording + replay helpers** (`recordPointerGesture` / `replayPointerGesture`) — parked from Phase 20.5 scope. Lands when Phase 22 (toolbar) needs button-click recording-replay parity.
- **VRT scenario matrix** (`(viewId × scenarioFlag)` cartesian capture) — parked from Phase 20.5 scope. Lands when Phase 21 (todayLine + nowIndicator) introduces the first multi-flag visual state worth capturing systematically.
- **Style numeric tolerance for non-px values** — `Number.parseFloat('14px')` works for px values; would fail for `'1.5em'` or `'2rem'`. v0 only supports px-style numeric values; non-px style keys fall through to exact-equality. Revisit when a phase needs em/rem comparison.
- **`localStorage` mirror for demo config** — current implementation is URL-only. A future enhancement could mirror to `localStorage` so reload preserves state when URL is shared as a deep link. Out of scope for v0; URL alone covers 95% of the shareable-link use case.
- **Cross-page navigation preserve / lose** — `replaceState` (used here) preserves the URL on reload but resets when the user navigates to a different page. Demo is single-page so this is irrelevant in practice.
- **Enum with TypeScript types other than string** — `enumOf` is hard-coded to `string` literal unions because URL params are strings. Numeric enums or boolean unions would need separate factories. None needed for current demo.
